Opening Studio in a second page of the same browser context showed the theme already present among 9 registered themes with zero explicit import step; Studio's Creation Flow (Screen 1 "Showcase My Artwork" ŌåÆ Screen 2's Vihu Worlds row ŌåÆ the theme's own real Showcase/Portrait/Quote Representation carousel) found and used it exactly as any Official World would be found; a real second image (distinct from the Builder's own Hero Image) was uploaded into the new Story via the ordinary Upload Images ŌåÆ Picture Studio ŌåÆ Apply path; Studio's own five-stage Publish Studio (Read My Story ŌåÆ Almost Ready ŌåÆ Choose Story Destination ŌåÆ Publishing ŌåÆ Celebration, destination Story Carousel, format Instagram Portrait) produced a real, downloaded, inspected ZIP (`..._carousel_portrait.zip`, 228,521 bytes) whose `page-02.png` shows the uploaded artwork rendered at full Instagram Portrait resolution with the theme's own page background/footer/page-number ŌĆö genuine Reader-facing output. Zero console errors on either page throughout. Two discovered, non-blocking findings are disclosed rather than fixed, per the sprint's own explicit "no Builder polish beyond issues that block the integration pipeline" scope: (1) the Artwork Gallery template's default Representations don't set `actions:['editCaption']`, so Studio's Context Panel showed no Title/Artist/Age/Date fields for this specific authored theme ŌĆö a content-authoring completeness gap in `tools/world-builder/js/templates.js`'s starter data, already named as open technical debt in the Sprint B2.0 report, unrelated to this sprint's integration-pipeline scope; (2) a single-file image upload always creates a new page rather than filling an existing Representation page's placeholder in place ŌĆö pre-existing, disclosed Sprint 10.0 behaviour, not an integration defect. Full report: `docs/PLATFORM_INTEGRATION_REPORT.md`.)

- AV-012 ŌĆö Representation/Holder Frame Reference Integrity (a P0 correctness fix, found publishing the real Museum Theme: Validation correctly blocked Publish with "Representation 'showcase'/'portrait' ŌĆö defaultFrame classic-white ŌĆö Frame no longer exists." **Root cause traced, not assumed**: every Artwork-type World template seeds a starter Frame (Museum Gallery's `classic-white`, `templates.js`) and hardcodes it as the seeded Representations' `defaultFrame` at generation time; `addRepresentation()` (`js/projectModel.js`) does the same with `frames(project)[0].id` for any Representation added later. `deleteFrame()` ŌĆö the only place a Frame record is ever removed (Manage Frames' ­¤Śæ) ŌĆö deleted the Frame file and cleaned up the Builder-only `frameOrder` display list, but never scanned for or cleared anything that *referenced* the deleted id: a Representation's `defaultFrame`, or a Scene Holder's `frame` (the same class of dangling reference `EngineV2Validator` already separately checks for Holders). Once "Classic White" was replaced by a newly authored Frame during real Museum Theme authoring, both Representations kept silently pointing at the now-deleted id ŌĆö a bug in `deleteFrame`, not in Validation, which was correctly reporting exactly the broken state Builder had created. **Fix, at the source**: `deleteFrame()` now clears (`null`, never a fabricated substitute id) any Representation `defaultFrame` or Scene Holder `frame` that pointed at the deleted Frame in the same operation that removes it, so no *new* dangling reference can ever be created going forward. **Automatic repair for Themes already carrying a legacy stale reference** (the real Museum Theme's actual state): a new `ProjectModel.reconcileFrameReferences(project)` ŌĆö the same silent reconcile-on-read discipline `_ordered`/`_ensureHolderDefaults` already use elsewhere in this file ŌĆö scans every Representation and every Scene Holder for a `defaultFrame`/`frame` that no longer resolves to a real Frame and clears it; `worldBuilderApp.js`'s `openWorkspace()` runs it the moment any Project is opened and persists immediately if anything needed repair, so an author never has to inspect internal ids or manually edit anything ŌĆö Representations has no reachable Builder screen of its own to fix this by hand in the first place. Deliberately never "picks a replacement Frame" (that would be exactly the fabricated-substitute-id shortcut the fix rejects) ŌĆö `null` is the schema's own pre-existing "no Frame chosen" state, identical to what a Representation with zero Frames already gets. Verified end to end via Playwright, reproducing the reported bug two ways rather than one: (1) creating a real Artwork Gallery project and deleting its seeded Frame the ordinary way confirms no dangling `defaultFrame` is ever created; (2) a hand-corrupted legacy-shaped project (a dangling `defaultFrame` *and* a dangling Holder `frame`, reproducing the exact reported state) is auto-repaired the instant it's reopened, then Validates with 0 errors, Builds a real package, and Publishes successfully into the shared ThemeRegistry ŌĆö all on the pre-existing, already-authored Project, never a newly created test Theme. `goldenBuild.js` still passes 30/30 unchanged, including its own negative fixture that intentionally ships a broken `defaultFrame` and must still fail Validation ŌĆö this fix repairs a live Builder Project's own data, it never weakens or bypasses the validator itself.)

- Platform Hardening Sprint (a contract-hardening pass, not a feature sprint ŌĆö Builder feature development stayed paused; "no new Builder capabilities, no new Studio capabilities, no redesigns, no speculative improvements, no Theme versioning" per its own Working Rules. Continued directly from the Platform Integration Sprint, auditing the complete Builder ŌåÆ Publish ŌåÆ Studio pipeline against the Museum Theme as reference, and produced the new canonical `docs/THEME_CONTRACT.md` ŌĆö a field-by-field parity ledger between what World Builder produces in a compiled `.vtheme` and what Studio's `ThemeRegistry`/`ThemeEngine`/`renderer/slideRenderer.js` actually consume, deliberately *not* duplicating `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md`/`docs/VTHEME_PACKAGE_SPEC.md`'s own schema documentation. Three real contract gaps were found, each reproduced against the actual defect before being fixed at the root cause: **(1) Frame Variations missing `background`/`frame`/`paper`** ŌĆö World Builder's Frames screen never exposed the three enum fields `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_artworkBorder()` needs to select anything but its own `'none'` fallback for mat fill and frame ornament, so every Builder-authored Frame rendered in real Studio with no mat and no frame design at all, regardless of matWidth/frameThickness/borderColor; fixed via a new `ProjectModel._ensureFrameFieldDefaults()`, called from the `frames()` read accessor (the same reconcile-on-read discipline `_ordered`/`_ensureHolderDefaults` already use), seeding Museum Gallery's own "Classic White" values (`background:'white'`, `frame:'white-mat'`, `paper:'smooth'`) for any Frame missing them ŌĆö repairs both new and already-authored Frames, no new Builder UI. **(2) Layer `target:"element"` validated but never rendered** ŌĆö `element` is one of the four containership scopes `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md` ┬¦7/┬¦11 explicitly names, and World Builder's own Layer Pack editor already offers it, but `renderer/slideRenderer.js` only ever called `_renderLayers()` for `slide`/`frame`/`holder`; fixed with one additional call site reusing the Holder's own content rect (Holder and Element are geometrically identical with today's one-Holder-per-page Layouts, so no new geometry was invented). **(3) The compiled `assets` map vanished on import** ŌĆö `js/themeRegistry.js`'s `importPackage()`/`_setImported()` only ever kept `manifest`/`theme` on a registered theme record, silently discarding `pkg.assets` even though `builder.js` compiled it correctly and `validatePackage()` accepted it ŌĆö meaning any relative-path asset reference (a Representation thumbnail, a Frame ornament image) became permanently unresolvable the instant a package was published; fixed by storing `assets` alongside `manifest`/`theme` (surviving `_persistImported`/`_loadImported`'s `localStorage` round-trip too) and adding `ThemeRegistry.getAsset(id, relativePath)`, wired into `js/creationFlow.js`'s Representation-thumbnail rendering ŌĆö the one concrete, reachable consumer today. **Two gaps investigated and deliberately left disclosed, not fixed**, per the sprint's own no-redesign rule: `fields.cornerRadius`/`inset`/`defaultMargin` are real Builder-authored, Builder-preview-rendered fields with no home in `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md` ┬¦6's canonical Frame field list and no established override mechanism in the real renderer (which derives corner radius only from its fixed frame-design enum table) ŌĆö extending the renderer to honor them would be a contract redesign, not a hardening fix, so they're documented as Builder-preview-only with zero effect on a published Theme; `theme.supportedCreationTypes` still has no Builder authoring surface, a pre-existing gap named in `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md` ┬¦8/┬¦13 and out of scope for a "no new Builder capabilities" sprint. Verified via Playwright: hand-corrupting a Frame to the pre-fix shape and reopening it confirms automatic repair; importing a synthetic theme with a `target:"element"` Layer and rendering a real slide confirms the Layer now actually paints; importing a synthetic package with a real asset entry confirms `getAsset()` round-trips it correctly including through a `localStorage` persistence cycle. `goldenBuild.js` still passes 30/30 unchanged, including its own negative fixtures. No Builder or Studio capability changes beyond the three root-cause fixes; no Theme versioning; `docs/THEME_CONTRACT.md` is now the one place this parity information lives going forward.)

- Platform Hardening Sprint ŌĆö Repository Architecture Transition, Phase 1 (a deliberate architecture pivot, explicitly authorized by product direction: Builder produces a complete in-memory Theme, not a package; Publish (install into a repository) and Export (produce a portable `.vtheme` for outside transport) become two distinct operations, with Export explicitly deferred to a future sprint; Official Themes become repository-native instead of in-code/file entries Studio special-cases; Supabase becomes the platform's first persistent repository backend, scoped narrowly to the Official + Personal Theme Repositories only ŌĆö not a Builder backend, not a Studio backend, not a session store; `ThemeRegistry` is to become a repository abstraction (discover/list/load/resolve-assets) rather than a `localStorage` wrapper, so Studio eventually consumes every repository identically with no per-source branching. This phase is foundation only ŌĆö per its own explicit "do not redesign Builder or Studio" scope, **zero existing files changed**: `js/themeRegistry.js`, `js/themeEngine.js`, `renderer/slideRenderer.js`, World Builder's Publish flow, and `localStorage`-based persistence are all completely untouched and still the only things Studio/Builder actually use today. New `docs/THEME_REPOSITORY_ARCHITECTURE.md` is the canonical design doc (deliberately not duplicating `docs/THEME_CONTRACT.md`'s field-parity ledger or `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md`/`docs/VTHEME_PACKAGE_SPEC.md`'s schema docs), defining: the canonical `themes` table shape (`repository`/`owner_id`/`theme_id` composite uniqueness, with an empty-string owner-id sentinel for Official rows since Postgres treats every `NULL` as distinct and would otherwise silently defeat that constraint); the decision that assets live as raw objects in Supabase Storage rather than embedded base64 (directly answering the file-size question the sprint grew out of, resolved as a repository-storage question rather than the file-transport/zip question explored earlier and explicitly deferred) ŌĆö a Theme's resolved `assets` map is populated with Storage URLs instead of data URIs, which is not a breaking change since every existing consumer already just uses whatever string is in that map directly as an image `src`; and the identity mechanism for the Personal Theme Repository ŌĆö Supabase's own Anonymous Sign-In (`signInAnonymously()`), a real, invisible-to-the-author session giving Postgres a server-verified `auth.uid()` for Row Level Security, deliberately chosen over a hand-rolled `localStorage` random id (which a client could trivially spoof against Supabase directly, making any ownership check unenforceable) ŌĆö disclosed honestly as a "no accounts yet" limitation with a real, native upgrade path (anonymous-to-permanent conversion) rather than a permanent ceiling. New `js/themeRepositoryClient.js` implements the 4-function Repository interface (`discover`/`list`/`load`/`publish`) against Supabase ŌĆö loaded via its official ESM CDN build (no `package.json`, no bundler, matching this repo's zero-build-step convention throughout), reading connection config from a new gitignored `supabase-config.json` (templated by committed `supabase-config.example.json`) the same resilient fetch-with-graceful-fallback way `js/buildInfo.js` already reads `build-info.json` ŌĆö "not configured" is a normal, handled state (`isConfigured()` resolves `false`, `discover()` returns Official only), never a crash. Asset resolution lists Storage objects under a Theme's own prefix directly (mirroring how `js/themeEngine.js`'s existing zip-import path already scans a zip's `assets/` folder wholesale rather than cross-referencing a separately-declared list) rather than requiring a redundant manifest of what was uploaded. New `supabase/schema.sql` is a disclosed, unexecuted draft (no real Supabase project exists to run it against yet) ŌĆö `themes` table + RLS policies + a `theme-assets` Storage bucket, with Personal rows fully self-service via `auth.uid()` and Official rows deliberately given **no** anon-writable policy at all this phase, since "who may publish an Official Theme" has no authorization model yet and is an open Phase 2 question, not something to invent here. Nothing in this phase is wired into any real call site ŌĆö `js/themeRepositoryClient.js` is new, additive, uncalled code, proven correct only on its own terms (its graceful "not configured" path verified via Playwright with zero console errors; `goldenBuild.js` still 30/30 unchanged, confirming the addition touches nothing existing). Phases 2ŌĆō5 (replacing Publish, refactoring `ThemeRegistry`, updating Studio's consumption, and full happy-flow validation with Museum Gallery v2.1 as reference) remain explicitly future work ŌĆö this phase's own deliverable is the foundation they build on, not a working end-to-end repository yet, since that requires a real Supabase project's credentials that only a human can create.)

- Platform Hardening Sprint ŌĆö Repository Architecture Transition, Phases 2ŌĆō4 (Supabase MEP continuation ŌĆö completes the Publish/Registry/Studio wiring the Phase 1 foundation deliberately left unbuilt, per this continuation's own explicit instruction: "Do not redesign Builder. Do not redesign Studio. Replace only the storage layer." **Schema trimmed to the minimum this sprint needs** (`supabase/schema.sql`): removed the Phase 1 draft's denormalized `name`/`version` columns (every real reader already has the full `manifest` JSONB and derives them from it ŌĆö `list()` selects `theme_id, manifest` only), the `updated_at` column + trigger (a plain upsert plus `created_at` is enough provenance for now), and speculative extra indexes ŌĆö all premature for "a few themes." **One thing was added, not removed**: Official rows are now writable by the anon role (`themes_official_write`/`_update` + matching Storage policies), a disclosed, deliberate gap ŌĆö this sprint's own happy-flow ("Builder ŌåÆ Publish Official Theme ŌåÆ Supabase ŌåÆ Studio discovers it") is impossible with Phase 1's original select-only Official policy, and with no accounts/authorization model yet, anyone holding the public anon key can currently publish or overwrite any Official Theme row; resolving real Official-publish authorization is disclosed future work, not invented here. **Builder wiring** (`tools/world-builder/js/worldBuilderApp.js`): `_renderPublishPanel()` gained a shared `_publishToRepository(repositoryId, label)` used by both the pre-existing "Publish to Official Themes" card and a new "Publish to My Themes" card ŌĆö checks `ThemeRepositoryClient.isConfigured()`, reads `project.lastBuild` (never `project.files`, preserving the Builder-owns-Projects/Runtime-owns-Packages split), calls `ThemeRepositoryClient.publish()`, and shows a plain success/failure message; no other Publish-screen UI changed. **Registry wiring** (`js/themeRegistry.js`): new `refreshFromRepository()` discovers every repository, lists/loads/validates each theme (`validatePackage()`, the same check a local import already runs), and registers valid ones via the existing `_setImported()` ŌĆö the identical path a drag-and-drop file import already uses ŌĆö deliberately never calling `_persistImported()`, so Supabase-sourced themes are never written to `localStorage` and are refetched fresh every boot, keeping the old file-import path and the new repository path from ever fighting over which one wins; a theme that fails to load/validate is silently skipped, never blocking the rest. Both Official- and Personal-repository themes register with `source:'imported'` ŌĆö the same tag a local file import already uses ŌĆö so they appear in Studio's existing World Library row with zero new UI, a disclosed trade-off (Official vs. Personal vs. locally-imported are visually indistinguishable there today). **Boot wiring** (`js/app.js`): `_startCreationFlow()` now awaits `ThemeRegistry.refreshFromRepository()` racing a 4-second timeout before calling `CreationFlow.start()` ŌĆö the only boot-sequence change, no new reactive re-render machinery added to `CreationFlow` itself. **A real cross-cutting bug found and fixed while verifying the Builder's new Publish cards**: `js/themeRepositoryClient.js`'s config path was a bare relative string (`'supabase-config.json'`), which resolves against the *page's* URL ŌĆö correct for Studio's root `index.html`, silently 404ing for `tools/world-builder/index.html` (two folders deeper), making a correctly-configured project look "not configured" from Builder alone; fixed by resolving the path relative to the script's own `<script src>` location instead. Verified via Playwright against a real (but sandbox-network-blocked) `supabase-config.json`: Studio boots to Creation Flow in ~1.1s with `isConfigured()` true and zero page errors; the Builder's Publish screen renders all 4 cards (Export Package/Community World/Publish to Official Themes/Publish to My Themes) and both new buttons fail gracefully with a clear, disclosed error rather than hanging or throwing, confirming the config-path fix actually mattered (before the fix, Builder's own Publish reported "not configured" even with real credentials present; after the fix, it correctly attempts the network call and fails only because this sandbox's egress policy blocks `supabase.co`/`esm.sh`). `goldenBuild.js` still passes 30/30 unchanged. Full live verification against a real Supabase project (Phase 5) is explicitly deferred to the project owner's own local browser, since this environment cannot reach Supabase ŌĆö see the sprint's own manual verification checklist for the exact SQL/Storage/config steps and expected results.)

- Platform Hardening Sprint ŌĆö Asset Repository Transition (Sprint 2 ŌĆö completes the Publish pipeline's remaining externalization gap: a published Theme's `manifest`/`theme` must carry repository asset *references*, never embedded base64, identically whether the repository is Cloud (Supabase) or a future Local extracted package. Per this sprint's own explicit instruction, every embedding site was traced before any fix was written: `assets/*` files, and every Layout/Frame/Layer/Representation image field `tools/world-builder/js/services/validator.js`'s `findAssetPaths()` recognizes, were *already* reference-based ŌĆö the compiled `assets` map was never stored in `supabase/schema.sql`'s `themes` table to begin with (no `assets` column exists), so `ThemeRepositoryClient.publish()`/`load()` already treated it as a generic upload/sign target requiring no change. The **only two real embedding sites** were `tools/world-builder/js/services/builder.js`'s `buildManifest()` and `js/themeEngine.js`'s `_buildPackageFromZipFiles()` (the local zip-import producer) ŌĆö both overwrote the placeholder path (`"thumbnail.png"`/`"preview.png"`) with a literal embedded data URI at Build/Import time, so even though Publish itself was already correct, the `themes` table's `manifest` JSONB column still carried embedded image bytes for these two fields forever. **Fixed at the source, in both producers**: `packageTheme()`/`buildManifest()` and `_buildPackageFromZipFiles()` now merge `thumbnail.png`/`preview.png`'s real bytes into the *same* `assets` map every other asset already uses, leaving `manifest.thumbnail`/`.previewImage` as the plain relative-path reference they were always meant to be ŌĆö giving the sprint's own Cloud/Local parity requirement real teeth, since both producers now emit the identical shape. **One new, small, shared consumer-side helper**: `ThemeRegistry.resolveAssetRef(id, value)` ŌĆö factored out of `js/creationFlow.js`'s pre-existing `_repThumbnail`, which had already independently discovered this exact "already a usable src vs. a bare reference needing `getAsset()`" rule for Representation thumbnails ŌĆö is now the one place every manifest-level image reference resolves through (`js/themeEngine.js`'s `_renderThemeCard()`, `js/creationFlow.js`'s `_themePreview()`), so a legacy embedded package, a local import's data URI, and a Supabase repository's signed URL all resolve identically with zero rendering-code redesign. Verified via `tools/world-builder/verify/goldenBuild.js` (still 30/30, now also asserting `manifest.thumbnail === 'thumbnail.png'` ŌĆö not a `data:` URI ŌĆö with the real bytes in `pkg.assets`, plus a round-trip proving `resolveAssetRef()` resolves a freshly-imported reference back to real bytes) and a full Playwright pass: built a real Theme end-to-end through World Builder's own UI (upload ŌåÆ Build) confirming the compiled package carries references only; separately registered a theme with its `assets` map holding **signed-URL-shaped strings** (the literal shape a real Supabase `load()` produces) and confirmed the World Library card's actual `<img src>` in the live DOM resolved to that signed URL, proving Studio's existing card-rendering code needed zero changes to consume a repository-sourced Theme correctly. `docs/THEME_CONTRACT.md` ┬¦8.4, `docs/THEME_REPOSITORY_ARCHITECTURE.md` ┬¦10, `docs/VTHEME_PACKAGE_SPEC.md`, and `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md` all updated to state the reference contract as canonical, replacing the prior "embedded as a real data URI" language throughout. No Builder/Studio capability changes beyond this externalization fix; no Marketplace/Community/Export/Import/Versioning work, per the sprint's own Out of Scope list.)

- Platform Hardening Closure Sprint ŌĆö Publish Contract Alignment & MEP Finalization (a terminology/UI/documentation alignment sprint only ŌĆö no new capabilities, no Builder/Studio redesign, no Marketplace/Community/Versioning/new repository features. Locks the following as canonical MEP decisions, verified against the actual implementation rather than merely asserted: **Asset Ownership** ŌĆö each Theme owns all assets required to render itself (decorations/layouts/frames/images/thumbnails/preview images/fonts/future types), with no cross-theme sharing, deduplication, hashing, reference counting, or garbage collection ŌĆö a Theme that stops referencing an asset leaves it orphaned in Storage rather than deleting it, a locked simplicity choice, not a bug. **Publish Behavior** ŌĆö publishing replaces the previously published Theme atomically (`ThemeRepositoryClient.publish()`'s existing `upsert(...,{onConflict:'repository,owner_id,theme_id'})` already did this correctly; no code change needed); there is exactly one published copy per `(repository,owner_id,theme_id)`, no repository version history, no internal version management. **Determinism, verified not asserted**: two consecutive Builds of an unmodified Builder Project were compared byte-for-byte and found identical, confirming Publish (which sends exactly what Build produced) is deterministic. **Signed URLs never persisted** ŌĆö confirmed unchanged since the Asset Repository Transition sprint: the stored `manifest`/`theme` never contains a signed URL, only plain relative-path references; repositories generate signed URLs only transiently while loading. **Repository Independence** ŌĆö Official, Personal, and any future Local repository must expose exactly the same published Theme representation, differing only in where bytes are stored; already true, verified. **Publish vs. Export, made explicit everywhere**: Publish installs a Theme into a Repository and never creates a package; Export creates a portable `.vtheme` and never installs into a Repository ŌĆö previously both lived under one ambiguous "World Package" heading with no structural separation. `tools/world-builder/js/worldBuilderApp.js`'s `_renderPublishPanel()` now renders two clearly separate, individually-headed sections ŌĆö **Publish** (Official Repository card, Personal Repository card) and **Export** (one card, retitled "Export .vtheme Package") ŌĆö replacing the old flat 4-card grid. "World Package" is removed as a compound term from both the Build and Publish screens (Build button ŌåÆ "­¤Äü Build Theme", success state ŌåÆ "Ō£ō Theme Built", the Scenes-section divider on both screens ŌåÆ "Theme"); "My Themes" is renamed to "Personal Themes" throughout (UI copy, internal function names `publishToMyThemes`ŌåÆ`publishToPersonalRepository`, and `docs/THEME_REPOSITORY_ARCHITECTURE.md`'s own prose). The **Community World card is removed outright** from the Publish screen ŌĆö not left as a disabled placeholder ŌĆö since Community is out of MEP scope and this screen now only exposes completed workflows (the separate, pre-existing "Community Worlds ŌĆö Coming soon" card on the Welcome screen's Explore section is untouched, a different and long-standing Builder feature area). `docs/WORLD_BUILDER_ARCHITECTURE.md`'s LOCK 02 diagram is corrected from the stale two-hop `Project ŌåÆ World Package ŌåÆ Runtime` to the canonical three-model `Builder Project ŌåÆ Published Theme ŌåÆ Studio` this sprint locks in; `docs/THEME_REPOSITORY_ARCHITECTURE.md` gained a full ┬¦11 documenting every MEP decision above plus a locked UI-terminology table (Builder Project / Published Theme / Official Repository / Personal Repository / Export Package ŌĆö never "My Themes"/a bare "Package"/"Publish" when the concepts differ). Frozen historical documents (`docs/PLATFORM_INTEGRATION_REPORT.md`, `docs/BUILDER_V3_CONVERGENCE_REPORT.md`, `docs/BUILDER_V3_EXPERIENCE_STUDIO.md`, `docs/BUILDER_V2_UX_PACKAGE.md`) were deliberately left untouched ŌĆö they're point-in-time records of what was built/tested/drawn at the time, not living specs, and rewriting their old "World Package" mentions would misrepresent the actual history. Verified end to end via Playwright: the Publish screen shows exactly 3 cards (Publish to Official Themes, Publish to Personal Themes, Export .vtheme Package ŌĆö Community absent, not disabled) under two headed sections; the screen contains zero occurrences of "World Package" or "My Themes"; both repository Publish buttons still produce a real, graceful failure message under this sandbox's standing network restriction (unchanged from before this sprint); `goldenBuild.js` still passes 30/30 unchanged, confirming this sprint touched only UI copy, internal naming, and documentation ŌĆö no Build/Publish/Validation behavior changed.)

- Platform Status & Repository Reset (a new Platform Hardening developer utility ŌĆö explicitly not a Builder or Studio feature, no product styling, reached only by opening `tools/platform-status/index.html` directly. Answers "is everything connected? what exists? what is published? can I safely start over?" without opening Supabase's own dashboard. **Platform Status** shows ­¤¤ó/­¤¤Ī/­¤ö┤ Platform Health for Builder/Build Pipeline/Repository Connection/Official Repository/Personal Repository/Theme Registry/Studio Discovery; a Builder section reading this tool's own `build-info.json` plus (read-only) the most-recently-edited World Builder Project from `localStorage`'s existing `vihu-world-builder-projects` key; Official/Personal Repository Theme+Asset counts via a new `ThemeRepositoryClient.getStats(repositoryId)`; a Theme Registry section showing how many repository Themes would actually register cleanly, computed by mirroring `refreshFromRepository()`'s own listŌåÆloadŌåÆ`validatePackage()` steps directly rather than calling that function itself ŌĆö calling it would have silently mixed in this browser's unrelated hardcoded built-in Official themes and any locally-imported Themes sitting in the same origin's `localStorage`, discovered and disclosed during design rather than after the fact; and a plain-text Platform Summary. **Repository Reset** adds one destructive action behind an explicit confirmation modal (Cancel / Reset Repositories, the sprint's own exact copy) implemented entirely through the repository abstraction ŌĆö a new `ThemeRepositoryClient.reset(repositoryId)` that lists a repository's Theme rows, recursively deletes every Storage object under each one's prefix, then deletes the theme rows themselves (assets before rows, so a mid-failure can't leave either side orphaned in the worse order) ŌĆö the UI never touches Supabase directly, so a future Local Repository implements the identical contract with no UI change. Reset deletes only published Theme rows and uploaded assets in both repositories; Builder Projects, current Builder state, Settings/Preferences, `supabase-config.json`, authentication, database schema, and Storage buckets themselves are never touched ŌĆö enforced structurally, since `ThemeRepositoryClient` has no code path that reads or writes `ProjectStore`'s entirely separate `localStorage` key at all. **A real, pre-existing bug found and fixed while building the recursive Storage walker this needed**: `_resolveAssets()` (used by every repository `load()`) only ever listed one Storage folder level, so a nested asset like the golden fixture's own `assets/textures/linen.png` would have silently failed to resolve from a real repository ŌĆö fixed by extracting a proper recursive `_listAllObjectPaths()` and reusing it in `_resolveAssets()`, `getStats()`, and `reset()` alike, so all three now agree on what "the assets under this Theme" actually means. Required a new, disclosed schema addition: `supabase/schema.sql` gained `themes_official_delete`/`themes_personal_delete` and matching `storage.objects` delete policies ŌĆö the one capability every earlier draft deliberately left out ("not part of the Publish ŌåÆ Discover happy flow") ŌĆö carrying the same disclosed Official-authorization gap `themes_official_write`/`_update` already do. Verified against a real local PostgreSQL 16 instance (fresh + idempotent re-run, both clean) and functionally as a non-superuser role: Official deletes for any caller, Personal deletes only for its own owner, and a Personal row/asset belonging to a *different* `auth.uid()` is correctly left untouched ŌĆö confirmed by querying as superuser afterward, not merely by the delete reporting zero rows affected (which alone wouldn't distinguish "blocked" from "already invisible under RLS"). The page itself was verified via Playwright against this sandbox's real (but network-blocked) `supabase-config.json`: all 7 Health indicators render, the Reset confirmation modal opens/closes correctly, and confirming Reset produces the same class of graceful, disclosed failure message every other Supabase-touching feature already shows under this sandbox's standing network restriction ŌĆö zero console errors. `goldenBuild.js` still passes unchanged, since it exercises only the local-import path and never touches `ThemeRepositoryClient` at all.)

- Builder Convergence Sprint ŌĆö Unify Build ŌåÆ Publish ŌåÆ Export into One Canonical Theme Pipeline (a purely architectural convergence sprint, per its own explicit brief ŌĆö no Builder/Studio/Repository redesign, no new features, no Engine V3, no Versioning/Marketplace/Community/Reader work. Closes the gap the earlier Scene-background pipeline trace found: Engine V1 (`builder.js` ŌåÆ `project.lastBuild` ŌåÆ Publish ŌåÆ Repository ŌåÆ Studio) and Engine V2 (`engineBuilder.js` ŌåÆ `project.lastSceneBuild` ŌåÆ Export Scene Package only) were two independent, parallel build artifacts ŌĆö Scene/Experience content reached the second one but Publish/Repository/Studio only ever consumed the first, so a Scene's background/image/decoration/text never reached a real reader. **The canonical choice, made explicitly before any code changed, per the sprint's own closing instruction**: Engine V1's `{manifest,theme,assets}` becomes the one canonical Published Theme ŌĆö not because it's older, but because it's the only shape `renderer/slideRenderer.js`/`js/themeEngine.js`/`js/themeRegistry.js` actually understand; inventing a native Engine V2 Runtime for Studio (Engine V3, effectively) or bolting Engine V2 onto Publish were both explicitly rejected, matching the brief's own "promote one canonical pipeline and migrate the other into it, not merge two architectures" instruction. **`tools/world-builder/js/services/builder.js`'s `packageTheme()`** gained one additive step, `convergeScenes()`/`convergeScene()`/`convergeSceneLayer()`/`externalizeSceneImage()`, running after its four pre-existing `collectFolder()` calls: it walks every `scenes/*.json` file and appends each Scene's converged content onto the exact same `layouts`/`representations`/`layerPack`/`assets` collections those calls already populate ŌĆö a project with no Scenes appends nothing, so the compiled package is byte-identical to before this sprint (confirmed via `goldenBuild.js`'s full 30-assertion suite, unchanged). One Scene converges into one Layout (`id:'scene-<id>'`, `aspect` taken directly from `scene.canvas.aspectRatio` ŌĆö already the same vocabulary as `LAYOUT_ASPECTS`, no translation needed) and one Representation (same id, `layout` pointing at it, `defaultFrame` taken from the Scene's first Place's `frame` reference ŌĆö Place and Frame already share the Engine V1 Frame id space too); every Scene Layer (background fill / image Decoration / Text, in Scene Stack order so z-ordering survives) converges into one Layer Pack entry each, `scope:'scene-<id>'` restricting it to that one Layout so multiple converged Scenes in one theme never cross-contaminate (`renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_activeLayerPack(s)` gained the scope filter ŌĆö absent `scope`, every layer authored before this sprint, means global, unchanged). Since Experience content already mirrors onto ordinary Scene Layers before Build runs (`_syncExperienceAttachments`/`_syncUniversalContent`, built in earlier sprints), Experience convergence needed zero additional code ŌĆö it rides the same Scene Layer conversion for free. **Two additive, backward-compatible renderer extensions were required, discovered only once real Scene content was rendered and checked pixel-by-pixel, not assumed**: (1) `js/layerEngine.js`'s `render()` gained an optional fractional `rect:{x,y,w,h}` field on a Layer entry (a free-form absolute position, alternative to the existing anchor/offset scheme) ŌĆö absent `rect` (every pre-existing Layer), positioning is unchanged; `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_layerDrawDecoration` gained two new `decoration.kind` values, `"fill"` (a solid-colour rect) and `"image"` (a real image drawn via the same per-src cache/`onload`-redraw pattern `_ensureStickerImage` already established, resolved through `ThemeRegistry.resolveAssetRef()` ŌĆö the same mechanism every other asset reference already resolves through). (2) A genuine rendering-order bug found by actually sampling pixels, not by inspection: converging a Scene's foreground content (an image, a caption) onto the existing `target:"slide"` scope rendered it correctly *behind* the Frame/Panel, which then painted over it ŌĆö `slide`/`frame`/`holder`/`element` all render at one fixed point *inside* the Frame/Panel pipeline (three of them gated on a resolved Picture Border existing at all), the wrong place for content meant to sit unconditionally on top. Fixed by adding a fifth containership scope, `target:"overlay"` (`docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md` ┬¦7), painted last in `render(s)`, on top of literally everything (frame/image/decorations/footer/page number/legacy Scene elements/stickers) ŌĆö a true full-bleed fill (a Scene Background) still converges onto the pre-existing `"slide"` scope (correct wall-level behaviour, unchanged); everything else converges onto `"overlay"`. No hand-authored theme uses `overlay` directly ŌĆö it exists purely as the Scene converger's own target. `project.lastSceneBuild` is retired as a concept: World Builder's Build screen shows exactly one Build action ("­¤Äü Build Theme," Scenes shown only as an informational stat) and Publish shows exactly one Theme's worth of options ŌĆö the "­¤Ä¼ Build Scene Package"/"­¤ÆŠ Export Scene Package" UI and their `EngineV2Builder`/`project.lastSceneBuild` plumbing are removed from `worldBuilderApp.js` entirely; Engine V2 Scene *Validation* (`EngineV2Validator`, a Scene Model consistency check, unrelated to compilation) is untouched and still shows its own separate report. `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md` gained a full "Builder Convergence Sprint ŌĆö Scene Convergence" section (the exact field mapping) plus `scope`/`rect`/`overlay`/`fill`/`image` documentation in ┬¦7; `docs/THEME_CONTRACT.md` ┬¦6 gained a row for the new `overlay` target; `docs/ENGINE_V2_SCENE_MODEL.md` gained inline "Amended" callouts on ┬¦5/┬¦6 plus a v1.5 Change History entry, disclosing this as a deliberate reversal of that document's original "the two pipelines do not merge" position for the *published-artifact* question only ŌĆö the canonical Scene Model and the native authoring-time Runtime (Working View/Runtime Preview) are completely unchanged; only the compiled/published representation now converges into Engine V1's. Verified end-to-end via Playwright: a Scene authored with a full-bleed colour background, an image Decoration, and Text converges correctly into `theme.layouts`/`representations`/`layerPack`/`assets` (the image externalized to a plain relative-path reference, resolving back to real bytes); the compiled package imports into the real Studio runtime with zero console errors; rendering a real slide against the Scene-derived Representation actually paints the background colour and the Decoration image (pixel-sampled to confirm, not merely inspected) and holds space for the Text; Museum Gallery (a theme with no Scenes) still imports/applies/renders with zero behaviour change and its 5 pre-existing Layer Pack entries all render correctly; `goldenBuild.js`'s full 30-assertion suite passes unchanged throughout.)

- Repository Reset false-success fix (a small, real bug found operating the platform for real: `ThemeRepositoryClient.reset()` reported its `deletedThemes` count from the pre-delete `SELECT`, not from what the `DELETE` actually removed ŌĆö so a delete silently blocked by RLS, exactly what happens when a live Supabase project hasn't had `supabase/schema.sql`'s delete policies applied yet, still showed "N Theme(s) removed" even though nothing was deleted. Fixed by chaining `.select()` after `.delete()` so Supabase returns the real deleted rows (`Prefer: return=representation`); Platform Status now distinguishes "found some, deleted none" from a real success and points at the likely cause. No architecture change; `goldenBuild.js` unaffected.)

- Happy Flow Completion Sprint ŌĆö Representation Ordering fix; Export confirmed already correct (closes the Builder ŌåÆ Repository ŌåÆ Studio Happy Flow the Builder Convergence Sprint opened but didn't fully complete, per this sprint's own explicit "instrument first, no speculative fixes" brief. **Root cause, traced live rather than assumed**: a real authored Theme (a World Builder template's legacy, unfilled Representations ŌĆö e.g. Artwork Gallery's "Showcase"/"Portrait"/"Quote," pointing at empty template Layouts with no relationship to any Scene ŌĆö plus one hand-authored Scene with a background/scene image/decoration/text) was built, registered, and opened in a simulated Studio session; Theme Discovery and Theme Application both worked correctly (`ThemeEngine.applyArtworkTheme()` activated the right Theme, confirmed via `getActiveArtworkThemeId()`), but the rendered page showed none of the authored content ŌĆö reading exactly like "the default placeholder experience." Traced to `js/creationFlow.js`'s Screen 2: the Representation carousel always starts at index 0, and "Start Creating" applies `reps[currentIndex]` with no swipe required to reach index 0 ŌĆö since the Builder Convergence Sprint's `convergeScenes()` *appended* each Scene's converged Representation after the legacy, `collectFolder('representations')`-sourced ones, a Theme Author's own real content always landed last, and a naive "Start Creating" click applied an empty legacy Representation instead. **Fixed at the source**: `tools/world-builder/js/services/builder.js`'s `convergeScenes()` now collects every Scene's converged Representation separately and prepends them ahead of the legacy ones (`convergeScene()` returns the Representation object instead of pushing it directly, so ordering is decided once, after the loop) ŌĆö real, authored content takes priority over untouched template scaffolding; legacy Representations are preserved, not removed, just reordered. Zero Studio changes were needed ŌĆö Creation Flow already faithfully reads `theme.representations` in array order; only the compile-time order was wrong. **Export was investigated in the same pass and found to already satisfy the platform's own established contract, confirmed by direct comparison rather than assumption**: World Builder's Export button (`_downloadDataURL(project.lastBuild.dataURL, ...)`) and Publish's `_lastBuiltPackage()` (`fetch(project.lastBuild.dataURL)`) read the textually identical object ŌĆö there is no second serialization path for Export to converge onto Publish's. The reported "embedded `data:image/...` base64" is real but confined to the `assets` side-map (verified via recursive scan: zero embedded data URIs anywhere in `manifest`/`theme` fields, which hold only plain relative-path references, exactly as the Asset Repository Transition sprint established) ŌĆö and that is required, not a defect, since Export's whole purpose is a self-contained, portable `.vtheme` file that must not depend on a reachable Repository/Storage bucket to open later; Publish externalizes those same bytes into Storage only because *its* destination is a Repository. No Export code was changed. `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md` gained a "Happy Flow Completion Sprint ŌĆö Representation Ordering" section (the full trace, fix, and Export finding); `docs/THEME_CONTRACT.md` gained a matching ┬¦8.5. Verified end-to-end via a new 15-assertion Playwright suite (Build ŌåÆ Representation ordering ŌåÆ asset/reference cleanliness ŌåÆ simulated Publish, since live Supabase is unreachable from this sandboxed environment ŌĆö asset externalization to Storage-URL-shaped strings, the exact transform `ThemeRepositoryClient.publish()`+`load()` perform ŌåÆ Studio Theme Selection ŌåÆ Theme Application ŌåÆ Renderer, confirming a naive "Start Creating" now selects the authored Scene Representation and the Renderer actually paints its background colour, pixel-sampled ŌåÆ Export/Publish source identity ŌåÆ re-import ŌåÆ re-publish, both idempotent with zero state drift) plus `goldenBuild.js`'s full 30-assertion regression suite, unchanged throughout; zero console errors.)

- WEP Scope Freeze ŌĆö Import Deferred, Promote to Official Repository (a deliberate product decision, not a technical limitation: the WEP proves exactly one complete authoring workflow ŌĆö `Builder Project ŌåÆ Build Theme ŌåÆ Publish to Personal Repository ŌåÆ Author/Test/Iterate ŌåÆ Promote to Official Repository ŌåÆ Studio Consumption` ŌĆö before any additional entry point is introduced. **Repository Model, locked**: Personal Repository is the author's own working environment and the *normal* authoring workflow, not an offline mode ŌĆö every Theme is published there first; Official Repository is the curated, released environment a Theme is promoted into once it's tested and ready. **Publish vs. Promote, a real mechanical distinction, not just friendlier wording**: Publish (`ThemeRepositoryClient.publish()`) reads whatever Build just produced and installs it ŌĆö the only way new Build output ever reaches a repository, and the only way a Theme reaches Personal. The new `ThemeRepositoryClient.promote(themeId)` creates nothing new: it copies whatever is *already* published to Personal ŌĆö the Theme row and every Storage asset, via Supabase Storage's own `copy()` (no client-side download/re-upload) ŌĆö into Official; promoting a Theme with no Personal row yet fails with a distinguishable reason (`not_published_to_personal`) rather than silently building one, and promoting again atomically replaces the previous Official copy (assets cleared and re-copied, then the row upserted), matching Publish's own established "replaces, no version history" convention. `tools/world-builder/js/worldBuilderApp.js`'s Publish screen now shows three ordered sections ŌĆö **Publish** (Personal Repository only, the primary first step), **Promote** (Official Repository, a later dependent step, requiring Personal already published), **Export** (reframed as portability/backup, explicitly not part of the primary workflow) ŌĆö replacing the old flat "Publish to Official Themes"/"Publish to Personal Themes" pair. No repository schema change was needed ŌĆö the existing storage RLS policies (Personal-owner-scoped read, Official write, from the Closure Sprint) already cover `copy()`'s source-read + destination-write requirements. **Import ŌĆö deferred, not removed**: every Import code path (`js/themeEngine.js`'s `importThemeFile`, `js/themeRegistry.js`'s `importPackage`, `js/creationFlow.js`'s `_wireImportButton`/`_importInput`) is completely unmodified and fully functional; only its UI reachability changed. `js/creationFlow.js` gained one module constant, `IMPORT_ENABLED=false`, gating Screen 2's header-level "ŌŖĢ Add New World" button and the World Library row's own "Add New World" card ŌĆö both simply aren't created while the flag is false, with an honest "No worlds published yet ŌĆö publish one from World Builder to see it here" message replacing what would otherwise be a dead-end empty row. `index.html`'s original Theme Library modal's own "+ Import Theme" button (`#importThemeBtn`, a separate, older Import entry point reachable from inside the editor, distinct from Creation Flow's) is hidden via `style="display:none"` rather than deleted, so `js/themeEngine.js`'s `_wireImportButton()` still finds and wires it correctly the moment it's ever un-hidden. World Builder itself has no Import UI to hide ŌĆö it has never imported Theme packages, only Published/Promoted/Exported them. Re-enabling Import in a future milestone (`.vtheme` sharing, Marketplace, Community exchange, local repository sync, backup/restore ŌĆö all explicitly out of WEP scope) is a one-line flip of `IMPORT_ENABLED` plus un-hiding `#importThemeBtn`, since nothing was removed. `docs/THEME_REPOSITORY_ARCHITECTURE.md` gained a full ┬¦13 documenting the two-repository model, the Publish/Promote distinction, the Import-deferred rationale, and Export's non-primary status. Verified via Playwright: Creation Flow Screen 2 renders zero "Add New World" affordances anywhere; the old Theme Library modal's Import button still exists in the DOM (not deleted) but is visually hidden while `ThemeEngine.importThemeFile` remains a real, callable function; World Builder's Publish screen shows the exact new button labels/copy/wiring (`_promoteToOfficial()` calling `ThemeRepositoryClient.promote()`, never `publish()` again); `ThemeRepositoryClient.promote` is exposed and callable; `goldenBuild.js`'s full 30-assertion suite and the Happy Flow Completion Sprint's own 15-assertion suite both pass unchanged ŌĆö this sprint touched UI visibility, one new repository-to-repository copy function, and documentation only, no rendering/Build/Validation behavior changed.)

- Builder & Studio Alignment Sprint ŌĆö Author-Owned Representations (a platform-alignment pass, per its own explicit brief ŌĆö no Builder/Studio/Repository redesign, no new capabilities, Import stays deferred, the Personal ŌåÆ Official promotion workflow unchanged. Locks the **Platform Representation Contract**: a Theme **MUST** contain at least one valid Representation (the only structural requirement); a Theme **SHOULD** contain multiple Representations when they improve the storytelling experience (guidance only); a Theme **CAN** use any Representation names at all ŌĆö the platform never reserves a name, and Museum Gallery's own `showcase`/`portrait`/`quote` (Sprint 10.2) are one Theme's own authorial choice, not platform vocabulary. **A real, systemic bug found while auditing, not assumed**: every World Builder template except Blank World already seeds one starter Scene that converges into one Representation at Build time (the Builder Convergence Sprint) ŌĆö but every template *also* still carried a static legacy `representations/*.json` array from before Scenes existed (`templates.js`), so every non-blank template actually compiled 2-4 Representations, never the single baseline the platform intends (Artwork Gallery alone carried the flagged Showcase/Portrait/Quote trio). Fixed by removing every template's static `representations` array entirely ŌĆö the starter Scene's own converged Representation is now each template's sole default, verified via a real Build (not just Project inspection) to produce exactly one Representation per non-blank template. Artwork Gallery's starter Scene is renamed from "Showcase" (one of the three explicitly flagged names) to "Story," the sprint's own suggested neutral default; Storybook/Quotes/Sketchbook/Greeting Cards' starter names (Cover/Quote/Sketch/Card) were never part of that flagged set and already read as ordinary, template-appropriate authorial choices, so they're unchanged. The now-fully-unused `_representation()` factory in `templates.js` was deleted as genuine dead code (distinct from WEP Scope Freeze's deliberately-preserved, merely UI-hidden Import functions ŌĆö this had zero remaining call sites and no future re-enablement reason to keep). **Validation gained the one rule the contract actually requires**: `tools/world-builder/js/services/validator.js`'s `validateRepresentations()` previously enforced nothing at all (a Theme with zero Representations from any source validated cleanly); it now errors when both `representations/` and `scenes/` are empty (since either alone converges into Ōēź1 Representation at Build time), never checking for a specific name or a minimum greater than one. **Studio required zero code changes**, confirmed by direct source audit: `js/creationFlow.js`'s `_representationsForTheme`/`paintPreview`/`_finish` and `js/contextPanel.js`'s `_activeRepresentations` already read `theme.representations` generically with no hardcoded name/id/count branching anywhere (a discipline already established since Sprint 10.1/11.2) ŌĆö one Representation already shows a single-slide carousel needing no swipe before Start Creating; several already show exactly those, in the Theme's own declared order. **Backward compatibility verified, not assumed**: Museum Gallery's compiled `.vtheme` still carries its original `showcase`/`portrait`/`quote` ids/names completely untouched ŌĆö no migration, no automatic rename, no compatibility shim. `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md` ┬¦8 gained the explicit MUST/SHOULD/CAN contract text (its own example JSON swapped from "Showcase" to the neutral "Story") plus a new "Builder & Studio Alignment Sprint" history section. Verified end-to-end via a new 15-assertion Playwright suite: all six templates compile to exactly one Representation (Blank World to zero, its own deliberate baseline); Artwork Gallery's sole Representation is "Story," never "Showcase"; a custom 3-Representation Theme (Adventure/Puzzle/Ending) compiles with exactly those three, in that exact order; Museum Gallery's original three Representations are confirmed unchanged; Representation structure (id/name/order) is byte-identical between a simulated Personal copy and a simulated Official promotion, with zero mutation relative to the original Build output; `goldenBuild.js`'s 30-assertion suite, the Happy Flow Completion Sprint's 15-assertion suite, and the WEP Scope Freeze sprint's own suite all pass unchanged.)

- World Builder V2 ŌĆö Builder Project Cloud Backup, Save Button Removed (a deliberate, disclosed extension of Supabase's scope in `tools/world-builder-v2/`, the parallel Builder redesign kept alongside `tools/world-builder/` for comparison ŌĆö every earlier Repository Architecture sprint scoped Supabase to "the Official + Personal Theme Repositories only," and this decision crosses that boundary on purpose rather than silently. Until now the editable World Builder Project itself (Scenes/Places/Experiences/Frames, everything authored before a Build ever runs) lived only in `localStorage` (`js/projectStore.js`) with no backup anywhere ŌĆö a cleared browser, a different device, or a quota failure could silently lose in-progress authoring. A new Supabase table, `builder_projects` (`supabase/schema.sql`), holds one owner-scoped row per Project (`jsonb data`, the exact shape `ProjectStore` already persists) via the same `auth.uid()` RLS pattern the Personal Theme Repository already established ŌĆö deliberately separate from `themes`, since a Builder Project isn't a portable, shared, referenced-file bundle the way a compiled Theme is. New `tools/world-builder-v2/js/services/projectSync.js` (`ProjectSync.isAvailable()`/`.push(project)`) reuses `ThemeRepositoryClient.getClient()`/`.getSession()` (two small additions to that module's exported API) rather than a second sign-in or config fetch ŌĆö same one Supabase project, same one anonymous session. **Local-primary, cloud backup, confirmed explicitly before building**: `localStorage` stays the only source of truth the Workspace reads from/renders immediately; the Supabase copy is a best-effort background push, debounced 2s off the trailing edge of edits, never a second read path ŌĆö authoring works exactly as before if Supabase is unreachable. **The identity caveat is disclosed, not hidden**: the anonymous session is itself a `localStorage` token, so clearing all browser data loses that identity too ŌĆö this does not fully solve "my work survives anything," only real narrower problems (quota failures, accidental local-only loss, resuming later on the same browser); a real account system would close the remaining gap and doesn't exist yet. Shipped anyway per explicit product direction (single-user product today). A second, honest header badge (`#wb-cloud-sync`) reports the background copy's own state (unavailable/pending/synced/error) completely independently of the pre-existing ­¤¤ó/­¤¤Ā/­¤ö┤ local-save badge, which is unchanged. **The Save button was removed outright, not demoted**: `_persist()` already saved synchronously on every edit and the local badge already reported that truth immediately ŌĆö the button only ever re-ran the identical write "as an explicit, user-visible confirmation," per its own pre-existing code comment, and added nothing real now that the cloud badge reports the one thing that wasn't already visible. `index.html`/`worldBuilderApp.js`/`world-builder.css` all had their Save-button-specific markup/wiring/CSS removed together; the local-save badge's CSS was generalized from id-scoped selectors to shared `.wb-save-dot-glyph`/`.wb-save-text` classes so the new cloud badge reuses the identical dirty/saved/error styling with no duplication. `docs/THEME_REPOSITORY_ARCHITECTURE.md` gained a full ┬¦14 documenting the decision, the caveat, and the implementation. Verified via Playwright: the Save button no longer exists in the DOM; the local save badge continues working completely independently of the cloud one; against this sandbox's own real (but network-blocked) `supabase-config.json`, the cloud badge correctly distinguishes "configured but unreachable" (a real attempted push that fails, reported honestly) from what "not configured at all" would show, never silently lying about success; `goldenBuild.js`'s full 30-assertion suite passes unchanged. Live end-to-end verification against a real, reachable Supabase project is explicitly deferred to the project owner's own local browser, matching every other Supabase-touching feature's own disclosed verification limits in this sandboxed environment.)

- Decoration Shapes ŌĆö real vector primitives with fill, outline, resize, and rotation (`tools/world-builder-v2/` only ŌĆö the parallel `tools/world-builder/` Builder was left untouched apart from a matching Artwork Gallery starter-scene rename already in progress. Studio's own Sticker Studio has always had a disconnected "Shapes" category of fixed-colour emoji glyphs, but World Builder's Decorations authoring had no shape concept at all until an author asked for one with real fill/outline/resize/rotation control ŌĆö a genuinely new capability, not a quick fix, since rotation didn't exist anywhere in Engine V2 before this. Implemented entirely inside the existing Universal Experience Content model (Builder V3.1) rather than a parallel mechanism: `js/services/experienceSchema.js`'s `defaultUniversalContent()` gained five new namespaced Graphics-section fields (`graphicShape`, `graphicFillColor`, `graphicStrokeColor`, `graphicStrokeWidth`, `graphicRotation`) plus a `SHAPE_KINDS` vocabulary (Circle/Star/Arrow/Speech Bubble/Banner) ŌĆö a Shape is mutually exclusive with an uploaded Graphics image on the same Layer/slot (picking one clears the other, enforced in the UI layer, not the Engine Adapter). The Decorations quick-picker gained a parallel "Add a Shape" tile grid alongside the existing emoji-glyph grid, creating a real Experience with `graphicShape` set directly rather than rasterizing a fixed-colour PNG the way the glyph picker does ŌĆö the whole point of a Shape being that its own colours stay editable afterward. `js/projectModel.js`'s `_syncUniversalContent` folds Shape handling into the same Image/Graphics mirroring loop that already handles uploaded images (one Layer, one set of position/size bookkeeping, only the styling fields differ) rather than a second implementation. `js/services/engineRuntime.js`'s `_paintLayer` gained a generic `layer.rotation` read (applied around the Layer's own rect centre, so it works for an uploaded Graphics image too, not just Shapes) and a new `_drawShape` function drawing each of the five kinds as a real filled+stroked canvas path. Reaching Studio required one more step, found and closed in the same pass: `tools/world-builder-v2/js/services/builder.js`'s Scene-convergence pipeline (the Builder Convergence Sprint) only ever converted a Decoration Layer's `.image` into a compiled `decoration:{kind:'image'}` entry or fell back to `decoration:{kind:'sticker'}` for a bare glyph ŌĆö a Shape Layer has neither, so it would have silently rendered as a stray Ō£© sticker in a real Studio-published Theme; fixed by converging `layer.shape` into a new `decoration:{kind:'shape', shape, fillColor, strokeColor, strokeWidth, rotation}` entry, and by extending `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_layerDrawDecoration` with the matching `kind==='shape'` branch ŌĆö the exact same five-path drawing routine reimplemented in that file's own coordinate/context style, since the real Reader-facing renderer has no dependency on any World Builder module and the two must be kept in lockstep by hand. Card/thumbnail preview sites (the Scene Stack sidebar row, the Experience Library tab, Gallery/Nursery cards) all gained a shape-aware swatch (the shape's own fill colour plus its icon) instead of falling through to the generic Ō£© placeholder. Verified end-to-end via Playwright driving the real UI (not just model calls): clicking a Star tile creates a real Personal-lifecycle Experience with `contentKind:'graphics'`/`graphicShape:'star'`; the Inspector's real Fill Colour/Outline Colour/Outline Thickness/Rotation range and colour inputs persist to the Experience and its mirrored Scene Layer; Working View and Runtime Preview both paint the shape (Runtime Preview's sampled pixel matched the fill colour exactly); uploading an image correctly clears `graphicShape`, and the mirrored Layer itself ŌĆö not just the Experience property ŌĆö updates from a shape decoration to an image decoration with zero orphaned data; and a real `ProjectCompiler.runBuild()` through the unmodified `validator.js`/`builder.js` compiled a `decoration:{kind:'shape', shape:'star', strokeWidth:6, ...}` Layer Pack entry targeting the `overlay` scope, confirming the fix reaches an actual published Theme, not only the Builder's own preview. `tools/world-builder-v2/verify/goldenBuild.js`'s full 30-assertion suite passes unchanged. No Engine V2 Scene Model/architecture change; Frame's existing "Holder clip/mask Shape" concept (Rectangle/Rounded/Circle, an unrelated pre-existing vocabulary) was deliberately left alone and not reused or renamed into.)

- Decoration Shapes ŌĆö basic-geometry vocabulary + independent fill/outline transparency (a direct, immediate follow-up on the Decoration Shapes sprint above, per explicit feedback that the original 5-shape set ŌĆö mostly decorative ŌĆö should include the standard drawing-tool primitives, and that fill and outline each need their own transparency, not just the whole shape's overall Opacity slider. `SHAPE_KINDS` grew from 5 to 14: Rectangle/Triangle/Diamond/Pentagon/Hexagon/Octagon/Cross/Trapezoid/Parallelogram joined the original Circle/Star/Arrow/Speech Bubble/Banner. `engineRuntime.js` gained a shared `_regularPolygonPath` helper (one N-sided-polygon routine reused for Triangle/Pentagon/Hexagon/Octagon rather than four near-duplicate hand-plotted paths) plus straightforward path geometry for Rectangle/Diamond/Cross/Trapezoid/Parallelogram; `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_layerDrawShape` got the identical geometry added by hand, in lockstep, since it has no dependency on any Builder module. **Transparency**: two new namespaced fields, `graphicFillOpacity`/`graphicStrokeOpacity` (each 0..1, defaulting to 1 so every pre-existing Shape renders exactly as before), ride alongside the existing `graphicFillColor`/`graphicStrokeColor` through the same mirrored-Layer/Engine-Adapter/Build-convergence pipeline the original sprint built (`shapeFillOpacity`/`shapeStrokeOpacity` on the mirrored Layer, `fillOpacity`/`strokeOpacity` on the compiled `decoration:{kind:'shape',...}` entry) ŌĆö no second pipeline. `_drawShape` composes (multiplies) each against the Layer's own overall `opacity` rather than replacing it, so a half-opacity Shape with a half-opacity fill reads as one authoring decision layered on another; fill and outline are painted as two separate `fill()`/`stroke()` calls each with their own `ctx.globalAlpha`, restored afterward. The Inspector gained "Fill Opacity" and "Outline Opacity" sliders (0-100%) paired beside their respective Colour pickers via the existing `_fieldRow` convention, and the isolated Experience Studio preview's shape-field passthrough was updated to match. Verified end-to-end via Playwright: all 14 `SHAPE_KINDS` entries have exactly one real, distinct Add-a-Shape tile; a Hexagon Experience's Fill/Outline Opacity sliders persist to both the Experience and its mirrored Layer independently; a real `ProjectCompiler.runBuild()` compiles the correct `fillOpacity`/`strokeOpacity` values into the published Theme's Layer Pack; and a pixel-sampled before/after (Fill Opacity 30% vs. 100%, same background) shows a real, visibly different rendered colour ŌĆö genuine transparency, not a cosmetic no-op. `goldenBuild.js`'s full 30-assertion suite passes unchanged. No Engine V2 Scene Model change; Frame's unrelated Holder clip/mask Shape vocabulary untouched.)

- Dev Footer Size Fix (a Studio-page fix, not World Builder ŌĆö reported as "the build info strip is too big." - Decoration Shapes ŌĆö Rounded Rectangle + "Draw Your Own" freehand shape (a second direct follow-up on the Decoration Shapes work: one more preset shape, plus a genuinely new authoring capability ŌĆö a creator-drawn outline, not another preset. **Rounded Rectangle**: `SHAPE_KINDS` gained one entry reusing `engineRuntime.js`'s existing `_roundedRectPath` helper (`renderer/slideRenderer.js` got the identical arcTo geometry added by hand, in lockstep, same discipline as every other shape) at a fixed `min(w,h)*0.2` corner radius ŌĆö no new control surface, since the request was for the shape option itself. **"Draw Your Own"**: a new `graphicCustomPath` field (`experienceSchema.js`'s `defaultUniversalContent()`) holds an array of `{x,y}` points, each 0..1 fractional within the pad the creator sketched on ŌĆö deliberately the same fractional-rect vocabulary every Shape/Holder/Layer Transform already uses, so a drawn shape resizes/moves/rotates/fills/outlines through the exact existing machinery with zero new plumbing; picking a fixed drawing-canvas-plus-Transform split (rather than drawing directly at final placement) keeps "what the shape looks like" decoupled from "where it sits," matching this codebase's own established Properties-vs-Transform separation throughout the whole Experience system. A new `_shapeDrawPad` (`worldBuilderApp.js`) is a small freehand sketch pad ŌĆö real `pointerdown`/`pointermove`/`pointerup` handlers capture a stroke, normalize it to fractional coordinates on release (not on every frame ŌĆö one model write per completed stroke, not per pixel moved), and redraw a live preview using the same Fill/Outline styling already chosen; a Clear button resets to `null`. Both `engineRuntime.js`'s `_drawShape` and `slideRenderer.js`'s `_layerDrawShape` gained a `kind === 'custom'` branch mapping the stored fractional points onto the target rect (identical placement math to every other shape) and closing the path ŌĆö falling back to a plain circle placeholder when nothing's been drawn yet, so the Experience is never invisible the instant the tile is picked, matching every other shape's own default-visible convention. `builder.js`'s Scene-convergence pipeline carries `customPath` through into the compiled `decoration:{kind:'shape',...}` Layer Pack entry alongside the existing fill/stroke/opacity/rotation fields, so a hand-drawn shape reaches a real published Studio Theme, not just Builder's own preview. Verified end-to-end via Playwright driving real pointer events (not synthetic model calls): Rounded Rectangle renders the correct fill colour at the expected pixel; drawing a real freehand triangle-ish stroke on the pad persists a Ōēź3-point fractional path to both the Experience and its mirrored Scene Layer; a real `ProjectCompiler.runBuild()` compiles a `decoration:{kind:'shape', shape:'custom', customPath:[...]}` entry ŌĆö confirming the drawn shape survives the full Build pipeline. No Engine V2 Scene Model change.)

- Creator V2 ŌĆö Wireframe Precision Pass (a direct follow-up once the actual wireframe board image became viewable in full detail, rather than only a text description of it ŌĆö closes two real gaps the text description had glossed over. **Frame Variations now render as colour swatch tiles**, matching the wireframe's "FRAME SELECTED" panel exactly: `js/workspaceBuilder.js`'s new `_buildSwatchRow()` reuses the exact `.icon-row`/`.icon-card`/`.icon-preview`/`.icon-label`/`.active` classes Frame Look's own preset row already established (zero new visual language), showing each Frame Variation's `fields.borderColor` as a small colour circle plus a "Default" reset tile; the `frameVariation` control in `CONTROL_CATALOG` now calls this instead of the generic `_buildSelectRow` dropdown. **A real, pre-existing Object Strip sizing bug, found and fixed**: comparing rendered card dimensions against the wireframe's own proportions surfaced that every Object Strip card was being silently crushed to exactly 40px tall (a 44px thumbnail rendering at ~4px) ŌĆö traced to `.object-card` being a `<button>` element with no explicit `height`/`width`/`margin` of its own, so the codebase's own global `button{height:var(--button-height)}` (40px) and `button:not(.tab-btn)...{width:100%;margin-bottom:12px}` reset rules (both pre-dating this session, confirmed via `git show` against the part-1 commit) silently won the cascade and flex-shrank every card's contents into a fixed 40px box ŌĆö the identical class of bug the Creator UI Convergence Sprint already found and fixed once for the Publish Studio close button. Fixed the same proven way: explicit `!important` overrides on `.object-card` (`width:78px`, `height:auto`, `margin:0`) plus `flex-shrink:0` on both `.object-card` and `.object-card-thumb` so a future container-level squeeze can't reintroduce it. - Creator V2 ŌĆö No-Scroll Screens, Real Screen 2 Visual Fallback, Branding Removal (four concrete, user-reported fixes, none of them presentation-only ŌĆö two real bugs and one deliberate scope decision. **(1) Screen 1 and Screen 2 no longer scroll on ordinary laptop viewports**: both were verified to overflow their `.creation-flow-overlay` container at common heights (Screen 1 at Ōēż720px, Screen 2 at Ōēż800px ŌĆö reproduced directly by measuring `scrollHeight` vs `clientHeight` at 640/700/720/800/900px, not guessed). Fixed by converting the overlay's padding and every major vertical space-consumer (Screen 1's question/subtitle/card padding/icon size; Screen 2's preview-panel padding, badge, heading, carousel slide `min-height`, and carousel art `height`) from fixed pixel values to `clamp()` expressions anchored on `vh` units ŌĆö content now compresses gracefully as the viewport shrinks instead of overflowing; `overflow-y:auto` stays on the overlay only as a safety net for genuinely extreme cases, never triggered at any realistic laptop height (verified fitting with zero scroll at 640/700/720/800/900px). **(2) Screen 2's Preview carousel now shows a real visual even when a Representation has no `thumbnail` of its own**: `js/creationFlow.js`'s `_repThumbnail()` used to fall back to a hardcoded generic ­¤ÄŁ mask emoji for every World's every under-authored Representation, regardless of what that World actually is ŌĆö a real "no real visual" gap, not a styling choice. Fixed by falling back to the World's own preview image/icon (`_themePreview()`, the exact fields `ThemeEngine`'s own Theme Library card already reads) before ever reaching a generic glyph ŌĆö verified with a synthetic theme whose Representations declare no `thumbnail` field: the carousel now shows the World's own hero image instead of a mask. **(3) Removed every hardcoded `'@vihuplanet'`/`'by Vihu'` branding fallback from the render pipeline** ŌĆö a real, confirmed bug, not a style preference: `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_drawHandle()` drew the literal string `'@vihuplanet'` at full render weight whenever a slide's Handle was empty (i.e., on every page a creator hadn't explicitly typed a social handle into, which is nearly all of them), and `buildPayload()`'s own `defaultHandle` fallback did the same; `js/sceneEngine.js`'s `resolveTextSource('handle')` was the most severe instance ŌĆö its own doc comment says "Returns '' if absent" but the implementation contradicted that specifically for `'handle'`, returning `'@vihuplanet'` as if it were real creator content and bypassing the Text Holder's own 50%-opacity "unfilled placeholder" dimming entirely; two Scene Blueprint defaults (`_textHolder('handle-holder',...,'@vihuplanet',...)` on both Hook and End role pages, and `_textHolder('author-holder',...,'by Vihu',...)` on Cover pages) baked the same fabricated content into every fresh Hook/End/Cover page's starting Handle/Author fields. All four fixed at the source: an empty Handle now renders nothing (matching the pre-existing, correct `_drawFooter` convention of `if(!bookTitle) return null`), and the Author placeholder became the generic, non-branded `'by You'` (matching the file's own existing convention of neutral placeholders like `'Your Title'`/`'Subtitle'`). Verified via Playwright, in both the Workspace canvas and the Publish Studio's Read-My-Story render: the fabricated `'@vihuplanet'` watermark is gone from every unedited page, while the book title and page number ŌĆö genuine project data (the creator's own title, the real page count), never fabricated content ŌĆö are correctly unaffected and keep rendering exactly as before, since visibility defaults for those two were deliberately left untouched pending explicit confirmation (a scope decision disclosed, not silently made). Full regression (page ops, dark mode, Object Strip sync ŌĆö now correctly showing 3 objects instead of 4, since an empty Handle has nothing to select ŌĆö Frame Variations swatches) passes unchanged with zero console errors.)

- Book Title / Page Number Turned Off By Default (explicit product direction, a direct follow-up to the branding-removal fix above ŌĆö after the fake `@vihuplanet` watermark was removed, the real project title and real page number were still showing on every page by default, and the instruction was to hide both "for now," reversibly, until reactivated. Traced to two separate hardcoded sources, not one: `js/themeEngine.js`'s `_defaultOptionsFor()` (`pageNumber:'bottom-right'`, `bookTitleVisibility:'show'`) and `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s matching `FALLBACK_OPTIONS` were the first ŌĆö flipped to `'hidden'`/`'hide'`. The real, deeper source was `js/state.js`'s `AppState.project.themeOptions`, which pre-seeds every project (new and default) with its own literal `pageNumber:'bottom-right'`/`bookTitleVisibility:'show'` ŌĆö since `ThemeEngine.getOptions()`'s `Object.assign({},base,stored)` always lets a project's *stored* `themeOptions` win over the computed base defaults, the `_defaultOptionsFor()` change alone was silently shadowed for every real project. Fixed at all three sources together. Each edit is commented as an explicitly reversible default ŌĆö flipping the two values back to `'bottom-right'`/`'show'` in all three places restores the prior always-on behaviour with no other code change, per the "if needed we will reactivate that" instruction. `handleVisibility` stays `'show'`, unaffected ŌĆö with the branding fix above, an unset Handle already renders nothing, so `'show'` now correctly means "show it if the creator or theme actually provided one." Verified via Playwright: the Workspace canvas and the Publish Studio's cover render both show only the artwork/frame with no title or page number by default; the Object Strip correctly lists only Background as a selectable object (Footer/Page Number have nothing to select once hidden). Full regression passes unchanged, zero console errors.)

- Object Strip / Canvas Selection Now Respects Builder-Authored Layer Pack Content (answers a direct product question ŌĆö "the object strip was to show all the objects used in building the scene in builder, i don't think creator is respecting the theme created by builder" ŌĆö with a real, confirmed gap, not a misunderstanding: a Builder-authored theme's Layer Pack (`theme.layerPack` ŌĆö Museum Gallery's Museum Caption/Wax Seal/Gallery Spotlight, or anything a future World declares) has always drawn correctly to the canvas via `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_renderLayers`/`LayerEngine.render` pipeline ŌĆö the theme's look genuinely was being respected pixel-for-pixel ŌĆö but the three draw functions behind it (`_layerDrawText`/`_drawMuseumCaption`, `_layerDrawSticker`, `_layerDrawDecoration`) only ever painted to canvas and returned nothing, so no bbox for that content was ever recorded anywhere. Since `_lastTextElements`/`_lastSceneElements` (populated during `render()`) are the *only* source both the Object Strip and real canvas click hit-testing/selection-outline drawing read from, this meant Layer Pack content was invisible to the Object Strip, unclickable on the canvas, and could never show a selection outline ŌĆö present in the picture, absent from the product. Fixed at the source: all three draw functions (plus `_drawMuseumCaption`, which `_layerDrawText` delegates to for the `museumCaption` text source) now return a `{bx,by,bw,bh}` geometry box describing what they actually drew (or `null` when nothing was drawn ŌĆö an empty Museum Caption with no title/artist/age/date, for instance). `_renderLayers`'s three callbacks wrap each call through a new `_pushLayerObject(layer,type,box)`, producing the exact same shape `_sceneBbox()`/`_stickerBbox()` already use (`{id,type,label,bx,by,bw,bh,visible,locked:true}` ŌĆö always `locked:true`, since Layer Pack content is theme-owned, not creator-editable) into a new accumulator, `_layerObjectBboxes`. That accumulator can't be pushed directly into `_lastSceneElements` at each `_renderLayers` call site, because `render()` has a real ordering hazard: `_lastSceneElements=[]` resets *after* the 'slide'/'frame'/'holder'/'element'-scoped `_renderLayers` calls but *before* the final 'overlay'-scoped one (Builder Convergence Sprint's own 5th target) ŌĆö so anything pushed early would be silently wiped by that later reset. Fixed by concatenating the whole accumulator into `_lastSceneElements` exactly once, right after the 'overlay' call and before the drag-guide/selection-outline code that reads it. A label falls back through `layer.label` (if the theme declared one) or a new `_humanizeLayerId(id)` helper (`'wax-seal'` ŌåÆ `'Wax Seal'`) ŌĆö no theme needs to add a `label` field for this to work correctly. `js/objectStrip.js` gained one new loop, after the existing SceneEngine.listElements()/getStickers() loops, iterating `SlideRenderer.getSceneElements()` and skipping any id already shown by those (tracked via a `shownSceneIds` set, so a blueprint element or a user-placed sticker is never double-listed) ŌĆö every remaining entry is, by construction, Layer Pack content, shown via the exact same `FRIENDLY_TYPE` fallback table (`text`/`sticker`/`decoration`) every other Object Strip card already uses, always as ­¤öÆ "Part of the world" (never ­¤¤ó editable). Selection and Context Panel routing needed zero changes: `js/contextPanel.js`'s `TYPE_TO_SECTIONS` already maps `text`/`sticker`/`decoration` to the correct Card Designer section, and `locked:true` already correctly suppresses resize handles (`_supportsResize`) the same way it does for any other locked object ŌĆö clicking a Layer Pack object routes to the right section and shows it as non-editable there, matching what it actually is.
