Verified via Playwright with a synthetic Museum-Gallery-shaped theme carrying a 3-entry Layer Pack (a 'slide'-scoped Decoration, a 'frame'-scoped Sticker, and a 'holder'-scoped `museumCaption` Text): before a picture is added, only the 'slide'-scoped entry renders/selects (matching the pre-existing, correct "Frame/Holder/Element layers only draw once there's a picture" gating in `render()` ŌĆö not a bug); once a picture is set, all three appear correctly in both `SlideRenderer.getSceneElements()` and the Object Strip with the right labels and ­¤öÆ badges, and clicking each one selects it and routes Card Designer to the right section. Full regression (`regression.js`, `final_qa.js`, `frame_variation_test3.js`, `ws_check.js`, `publish_stages.js`, `lang_check.js`, `baseline3.js`) passes unchanged with zero console errors; two pre-existing test failures (`objstrip_check.js`, `ctx_states2.js`, both expecting a "Handle" card at a fixed index) were confirmed via `git stash` to already fail identically on the unmodified codebase ŌĆö a stale expectation left over from the earlier Book Title/Page Number default-hide fix, not a regression from this change.)

- Theme ŌåÆ Creator Map (`docs/THEME_TO_CREATOR_MAP.md`) ŌĆö a documentation-only addition answering a direct product question: for every field a `.vtheme` package can carry, where does it actually surface in Creator ŌĆö shown, editable, and reflected ŌĆö not just "does Studio's code consume it" (that parity question is `docs/THEME_CONTRACT.md`'s own job, and this document deliberately doesn't restate it). Built by tracing real call sites, not by re-deriving from memory: `js/workspaceBuilder.js`'s `CONTROL_CATALOG` (every dynamic control's storage location), the exact `WorkspaceBuilder.layout()` call sites in `js/cardDesigner.js`/`js/pageDesigner.js` (panelId ŌåÆ actual Creator section), `index.html`'s World Designer tab markup (`data-section` groups ŌåÆ control ids ŌåÆ `themeOptions.*` keys), and `js/contextPanel.js`'s Representation `actions` gating. Covers ten field groups (Manifest/Identity, core rendering fields, Presentation Presets, Layouts, Frame Variations, Layer Pack, Representations, the Editor block's full control-to-storage table, Assets, and a closing "reaches nowhere in Creator" list) plus a repeatable four-question method (Consumed? / Shown? / Editable? / Reflected?) for adding a new row when a future theme field ships. Cross-references, rather than duplicates, `docs/THEME_CONTRACT.md`/`docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md`/`docs/VTHEME_PACKAGE_SPEC.md` ŌĆö this is the one new thing none of those three answer: the Creator-facing "where does a person actually touch this" index.

- Creator Reconciliation Sprint ŌĆö Phase 1: The Render Tree Becomes Creator's Object Model (implements the user's own architectural directive ŌĆö "Builder becomes the single source of truth for both presentation and interaction... Creator should never reconstruct any of this independently... The render tree becomes Creator's object model" ŌĆö as a narrow, additive, backward-compatible first phase, arrived at only after three parallel investigation passes plus a dedicated Plan-agent validation pass, per the user's own explicit "investigate first, find the narrowest point" instruction. **The core finding**: World Builder already had the exact mechanism this sprint needed, fully authored, sitting unused. `tools/world-builder-v2/js/projectModel.js` has stored `holder.permissions`/`layer.permissions = {moveable, editable, visible}` (default all `true`) with real authoring UI since Builder V2/V3 (`_render{Holder,Layer,Text}PermissionBlock` in `worldBuilderApp.js`) ŌĆö but `tools/world-builder-v2/js/services/builder.js`'s `convergeSceneLayer()` (the function that turns a Builder Scene Layer into a compiled `theme.layerPack[]` entry) only ever read `layer.permissions.visible` onto the compiled package; `moveable`/`editable` were silently dropped at Build time. Completing that one half-finished wire, not inventing a new one, is this phase's entire mechanism. **Render tree becomes uniform**: a new shared `_sceneObject(raw, owner)` normalizer in `renderer/slideRenderer.js` gives every pushed entry into `_lastSceneElements` ŌĆö whether it started as a Cover/Hook/End blueprint element (`_sceneBbox`), a Story-Author-placed sticker (`_stickerBbox`), or a theme-authored Layer Pack entry (`_pushLayerObject`) ŌĆö the same uniform shape: `{id,type,label,bx,by,bw,bh,visible,owner,moveable,editable,locked}`. `owner` is `'world'` (Layer Pack) or `'story'` (blueprint/sticker ŌĆö exactly today's existing Sprint 8.3 Universal Object Consistency behaviour, now named explicitly instead of re-derived from `!locked` at five different call sites); `moveable`/`editable` default to `!locked` when not supplied, so nothing changes for any object type this sprint didn't give real Builder-sourced values to. `convergeSceneLayer()` gains two lines mirroring the exact, already-proven `visible` pattern (`!(layer.permissions && layer.permissions.X===false)`) ŌĆö a real gap found in review is resolved by this same arithmetic, not a separate fix: `_ensureSceneLayerDefaults` (Builder's own reconciler stamping `{moveable:true,editable:true,visible:true}`) only runs on-demand via `findSceneLayer`, never at Build time, so a Scene Layer positioned once and never reopened could reach `convergeSceneLayer` with `permissions` still `undefined` ŌĆö the mirrored pattern already resolves `undefined` to `true` for all three fields, identical to what the reconciler would have stamped, verified directly (`node -e` against the literal expression) before relying on it. Hand-authored `layer-packs/*.json` entries (the Builder's other, separate `layerPack` source, via `collectFolder('layer-packs')`, which never passes through `convergeSceneLayer`) simply never gain these keys ŌĆö `!!undefined` in `_pushLayerObject` resolves to conservative `false`, exactly matching every pre-sprint theme's existing always-locked behaviour (Museum Gallery, unchanged). **Object Strip becomes a pure render-tree reader**: `js/objectStrip.js`'s `refresh()` stopped calling `SceneEngine.listElements()`/`getStickers()` directly for blueprint elements and stickers ŌĆö a real architectural gap the investigation surfaced, since those two categories were being reconstructed from SceneEngine rather than read back from what actually rendered, while only Layer Pack objects went through the render tree, stitched together with a manually-maintained `shownSceneIds` de-dup Set. Now there is exactly one source (`SlideRenderer.getSceneElements()`+`getTextElements()`), the de-dup hack is gone by construction, and user-placed stickers appear in Object Strip for the first time (a pre-existing gap closed as a natural consequence of unification, not a separate feature). Background and Artwork remain the two disclosed synthetic entries (genuinely page-level concepts with no independent render-tree bbox today ŌĆö Background is the canvas itself, Artwork has no SceneEngine element on Story-role pages). The ownership badge is now driven by the entry's own `owner`/`editable` fields, and gained a third distinction the investigation found conflated before: `editable:false` used to always read "­¤öÆ Part of the world" even for a Story-owned object the child individually locked themselves ŌĆö now `owner==='story'` reads "­¤öÆ Locked" instead, `owner==='world'` keeps "­¤öÆ Part of the world". `_lastTextElements`' four Story-Theme-furniture entries (Story Text/Handle/Footer/Page Number) are deliberately untouched ŌĆö fixed Story Theme chrome, not Builder-authored variable content, out of this phase's scope. **Context Panel asks the selected object, not a type table**: a real, verified misleading-UX bug, not a harmless dead end, was the trigger for this ŌĆö selecting a Layer Pack object routed through the same `TYPE_TO_SECTIONS` a real blueprint element uses, opening a section (e.g. the decoration case in `cardDesigner.js`) that reads `slide.metadata.elementOverrides` without ever checking whether the selected id resolves to anything real; a child could select "Wax Seal" and land in a fully live-looking editor that doesn't target it at all. Fixed by a new `_findSceneObject(sceneId,sceneType)` (reading the identical render tree Object Strip already reads) checked before type-routing in `refresh()`: a selected object with `owner==='world'` never opens the generic section ŌĆö instead `_renderWorldObjectDisclosure(sceneObj)` shows an honest banner, worded from the object's own `editable` flag ("This is part of the World, but you may adjust it. That kind of edit isn't available in Creator yet." vs. plain "This is part of the World.") ŌĆö never a fabricated editor for content Creator has no real controls for yet. Every Story-owned object (blueprint/sticker/text) is completely unaffected ŌĆö verified directly: adding a real sticker via Sticker Studio and selecting it still opens its real, correctly-targeted section exactly as before. **Investigated and deliberately not done**: `js/contextPanel.js`'s `TYPE_TO_SECTIONS` and `js/app.js`'s `SCENE_TYPE_TO_SECTION` looked like a textbook duplicate-logic case worth consolidating (both 5-entry typeŌåÆsection tables) ŌĆö direct comparison found they are **not** interchangeable: `'image-holder'` maps to `['image']` in one and `'frame'` in the other, for genuinely different, documented reasons (Context Panel's Story-role-specific override vs. Card Designer's Universal Object Selection `focusSection()` on Cover/Hook/End pages) ŌĆö merging them without a full behaviour audit on Cover/Hook/End page selection risked a real regression the "preserve backward compatibility" constraint rules out, so this was disclosed as a finding rather than forced through. **Explicitly deferred, named not silently dropped**: Phase 2 (actually persisting a drag when a `moveable:true` Layer Pack object is moved ŌĆö needs one new small override bag mirroring `slide.metadata.elementOverrides`; a real generic Modify surface for Builder-owned editable content); Phase 3+ (Holder/Frame-level permissions as their own Object Strip row ŌĆö Frame Variation is already a separate, working, creator-editable control per `docs/THEME_TO_CREATOR_MAP.md` ┬¦5/┬¦8, not a render-tree object today; a `removable`/delete capability ŌĆö Builder's schema has none today, and nothing about Layer Pack objects is Creator-deletable today, correctly, so nothing changes here). `tools/world-builder/` (v1) is deliberately untouched throughout, per this codebase's own recent, explicit precedent (the Decoration Shapes sprint). No new rendering engine, no Theme Contract redesign, no second object model ŌĆö every change is an additive field or a read-path consolidation onto structures that already existed. Docs updated: `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md` ┬¦7 (new `moveable`/`editable` Layer fields), `docs/THEME_CONTRACT.md` (new ┬¦6.1), `docs/THEME_TO_CREATOR_MAP.md` ┬¦6 (corrected from "No, by design ŌĆö `locked:true` always" to the real capability-gated behaviour), `docs/ENGINE_V2_SCENE_MODEL.md` (a precisely-scoped v1.6 Change History entry ŌĆö its own "never a published render" claim stays exactly true for Engine V2's own native Runtime paint step, unmodified; what's new is a second, separate consumer, Studio itself, reading the same authored data through the already-open Scene-convergence path). Verified via a synthetic-theme Playwright harness test simulating real `convergeSceneLayer` output (three Layer Pack entries: real `moveable:true,editable:true`, explicit `false`, and legacy-shaped with neither field) confirming the render tree, Object Strip badges, and Context Panel disclosure wording all match exactly; a second test confirming a real Sticker-Studio-placed sticker still gets `owner:'story'` and still opens its real, correctly-targeted section; full existing Creator Playwright regression suite (`regression.js`, `final_qa.js`, `frame_variation_test3.js`, `diag_layerpack3.js`, etc.) passing unchanged with zero console errors; `tools/world-builder-v2/verify/goldenBuild.js` passing unchanged (36/36) confirming the two-line `convergeSceneLayer` addition broke nothing in the existing compile/validate/import pipeline; a direct `node -e` algebraic check confirming the absent-permissions-resolves-to-true reasoning before relying on it in the actual code.)

- Engine V2 Promotion Strategy (`docs/ENGINE_V2_PROMOTION_STRATEGY.md`) ŌĆö an investigation-and-strategy-only deliverable, no code changes, answering a direct architectural question: can Engine V2 (`tools/world-builder-v2/js/services/engineRuntime.js`, World Builder's own native preview runtime) be promoted into a shared platform runtime for Builder Preview/Creator Canvas/Publish/eventually Reader, replacing Engine V1 (`renderer/slideRenderer.js`) incrementally, with Builder's authoring architecture held frozen. Three parallel Explore investigations (Engine V2's real capability surface, Engine V1's full feature inventory, and exact consumer/Theme-Contract boundary mapping) converged on one confirmed, load-bearing blocker: `engineRuntime.js` has **zero** consumption of any compiled `.vtheme` field (`layouts`/`frameVariations`/`layerPack`/`representations`/`slide`/`holder`/`frame`/`panel`/`storyText`/`footerText`/`watermark` ŌĆö confirmed by grep, not inferred) ŌĆö it only ever renders a *live Builder authoring session's* in-memory Scene objects, resolving Frame references through Builder's own global `ProjectModel`, never a compiled Theme. `convergeSceneLayer`/`convergeScene` (Builder Convergence Sprint) is confirmed strictly one-way (Scene Model ŌåÆ Engine V1 shape); no reverse path exists. The verdict: **Engine V2 cannot be promoted as-is** ŌĆö doing so is a parity-building program, not a swap. Engine V2 is standalone/pure and is genuinely *ahead* of Engine V1 in two respects (real word-wrap for Scene text, where V1's Scene text draw calls never wrap at all; a 13-kind vector Shape system richer than V1's hand-mirrored 5-kind subset) ŌĆö but lacks, with no Engine V2 equivalent found anywhere: Layer Pack's 5-scope declarative containership system, Artwork Themes as an independent theme-layering dimension, Frame Variations' 7-preset ornament pipeline (storybook/polaroid/ribbon/wooden/magic/vintage/tape/cloud), Layout `composition` variants (especially Quote's entirely different no-Frame draw path), Presentation Presets' three-tier resolution, page furniture (Handle/Footer/PageNumber/decorative glyphs) with position enums, the full per-image adjustment stack (crop/focal/straighten/brightness/contrast/highlights/shadows/warmth/saturation/sharpness/vignette), the Cover/Hook/End blueprint dual-pipeline, and the DPR-aware `init(canvas,{dpr})` WYSIWYE mechanism itself (Engine V2 uses a genuinely different canvas model ŌĆö variable per-aspect pixel dimensions vs. Engine V1's always-fixed 1080├Ś1350 logical canvas). No live "Reader" surface exists anywhere in the codebase today (confirmed via repo-wide grep ŌĆö only `FileReader` API hits and doc prose using "reader" to mean the end consumer of a downloaded export), confirming the request's own "eventually Reader" framing is correctly forward-looking, not a near-term target. The proposed strategy: build one new, additive, Studio-side adapter (`js/engineV2Adapter.js`, proposed not built) translating a resolved compiled theme into Engine V2's Scene Model shape ŌĆö the missing reverse direction of `convergeSceneLayer`'s existing one-way translation ŌĆö then migrate **consumer by consumer, never feature by feature** (the Decoration Shapes sprint's own "kept in lockstep by hand" duplication is cited as a live demonstration of what a feature-split produces at scale): Phase 0 builds and pixel-verifies the adapter against Museum Gallery with zero call sites wired to any real UI; Phase 1 migrates the lowest-stakes one-shot consumer (Card Designer's Frame swatch or `ThumbnailEngine.generate()`); Phase 2 moves the real export engine (`js/storyDestinations.js`, where page-furniture/Quote-composition parity actually has to close, not stay deferred); Phase 3 moves the live editor canvas only after full-fidelity parity is proven; Phase 4 retires Engine V1 only once every consumer has migrated and a full regression pass shows zero behaviour change; Phase 5 (Reader) is named as a future consumer of the same runtime, explicitly out of this document's own scope. Builder's Scene/Holder/Layer authoring model, the compiled `.vtheme` shape, `convergeSceneLayer`'s existing one-way translation, and every already-published Theme are explicitly named as staying completely frozen throughout ŌĆö every proposed change is new Studio-side code (plus disclosed, scoped Engine V2 capability extensions for the ornament-preset/page-furniture gap, an explicit open question, not resolved by this document) reading from structures that already exist, never a change to how a Theme Author authors anything. Three real open risks are disclosed rather than glossed over: ornament-preset fidelity is sized as "the largest single fidelity gap" with no proposed solution yet; whether to extend `engineRuntime.js` with the missing drawing routines vs. keep a small permanent Engine-V1-only hybrid for page furniture is flagged as a real product decision needing explicit sign-off before Phase 2; and Engine V2's per-object drawing performance at editor-interaction frequency (every drag-move frame) was never measured and is flagged as needing a real performance pass before Phase 3, not assumed safe. No code was written ŌĆö this is a strategy proposal only; per the standing "architecture changes require explicit approval" rule, even Phase 0's isolated, zero-call-site adapter would need its own sign-off before implementation begins.

- Scene Adapter Architecture Analysis (`docs/SCENE_ADAPTER_ARCHITECTURE_ANALYSIS.md`) ŌĆö an investigation-only companion to `docs/ENGINE_V2_PROMOTION_STRATEGY.md`, no code changes, answering five questions about a proposed `Builder ŌåÆ Publish Theme ŌåÆ Standalone Scene Adapter ŌåÆ Canonical Scene ŌåÆ Shared Runtime ŌåÆ Creator/Publish/Reader` pipeline with Builder held frozen. **Q1 (remaining Creator work)**: the Adapter by itself retires almost none of the hard remaining work ŌĆö Object Strip/Selection are already Mostly Complete (Creator Reconciliation Sprint Phase 1 did this without any Adapter), but Rendering/Publish (gated entirely on the Shared Runtime reaching feature parity with Engine V1 ŌĆö see the Promotion Strategy doc's own gap list) and Context Panel/Editing/Save-Reload (all gated on redesigning Creator's override-bag key space from blueprint-element-ids/fixed-bag-keys to canonical Scene Object ids) all Require Significant Work regardless of whether the Adapter exists, because an Adapter reshapes data, it doesn't paint pixels or invent generic editing UI. One genuinely good finding, verified by reading `js/projectManager.js`'s `serialize()` directly: Creator's save format already stores Story-Author deltas plus a bare theme-id reference, never a resolved Theme snapshot ŌĆö the right shape for a re-derived-canonical-Scene architecture already, with re-keying as the only real gap. **Q2 (does the Adapter isolate Creator from Builder evolution)**: only partially, and the partition is precisely bounded by this session's own Phase 1 precedent ŌĆö additive changes (a new Scene property, a new capability flag, a new named preset within an existing closed vocabulary) cost only Adapter+Runtime changes, proven directly by how cheaply `layer.permissions.moveable/editable` shipped; structural changes (new object types, new Frame systems that don't fit the flat-band model, and ŌĆö not hypothetical, already on this project's own Roadmap as item 6 ŌĆö Audio, plus Animation/Perspective/Lighting) require changes all the way into Creator, because no Adapter can invent Runtime drawing capability or Creator interaction affordances that don't exist yet. **Q3 (permanent boundary, temporary layer, or unnecessary)**: temporary migration layer ŌĆö the key insight being that the proposed pipeline places the Adapter *after* Publish (consumption-time), while the codebase already has a Build-time translation step doing conceptually the same job (`convergeSceneLayer`), and every "Convergence Sprint" in this project's history has consistently preferred extending one existing pipeline over standing up a parallel one. The architecturally clean end-state is retargeting Build-time convergence to emit the canonical Scene shape directly (so Publish *is* the canonical Scene, no runtime-time Adapter needed) ŌĆö explicitly out of reach under "Builder frozen" as a near-term constraint, but named as the Adapter's own correct retirement condition, not a competing alternative. **Q4 (risk)**: short-term (bounded, expected to resolve) ŌĆö fidelity gaps during transition, dual-engine maintenance, unmeasured interactive-frequency performance, and doubled translation-drift risk while both `convergeSceneLayer` and the new Adapter exist simultaneously; long-term (only real if the Adapter is kept permanent) ŌĆö institutionalized double translation contradicting "minimal future duplication," unbounded Adapter complexity growth (the same kind-by-kind branching pattern `convergeSceneLayer` already shows, risking a second full rendering-semantics implementation), information loss (a concrete, already-observable risk ŌĆö `_resolveArtworkFields` already discards a chosen Frame Variation's authored *name*, keeping only resolved values, and Object Strip's Layer Pack labels already depend on Builder having authored an explicit `.label` field), a larger blast radius once multiple consumers share one Runtime with no existing compatibility-versioning practice in this codebase, and the risk of stakeholders over-trusting the Adapter as general Builder-evolution insulation when Q2 shows it's bounded to the additive case only. **Q5 (recommendation)**: Option A, conditionally ŌĆö build the Adapter exactly as `docs/ENGINE_V2_PROMOTION_STRATEGY.md`'s Phase 0-3 already proposed, but govern it explicitly as temporary scaffolding with a named retirement condition (a new Phase 4.5 this document adds: once Runtime fidelity parity and the canonical Scene shape are proven, retarget Build-time convergence to emit it directly and retire the runtime-time Adapter) rather than treating it as the platform's permanent boundary ŌĆö reasoned against plain Option B (real progress, proven this session, but has a hard ceiling: never reaches one shared Runtime, leaves the Decoration-Shapes-style hand-synced duplication permanent rather than temporary) and against unconditional Option A (institutionalizes exactly the double-translation duplication the investigation's own stated optimization goals rule out). No code was written; this is the second of two paired strategy documents, both explicitly gated behind the standing "architecture changes require explicit approval" rule before any implementation begins.

- Creator Runtime Pass Sprint ŌĆö Promote the Center Pane into the Page Runtime (`docs/CREATOR_PAGE_RUNTIME.md`; implements the user's own directive to formally promote Creator's existing center pane into a named "Page Runtime" ŌĆö the single source of truth for the active page, its rendered objects, and its selection ŌĆö with every surrounding panel becoming a pure consumer/projection of it, never independently reconstructing state; explicitly a **promotion, not a rewrite**, per the brief's own closing instruction: "reuse the existing implementation wherever possible... this sprint changes ownership of state, not rendering technology." Investigation (following directly from the Creator Reconciliation Sprint's own render-tree work) found most of the "Page Runtime" concept already existed in Creator, scattered across `js/app.js` with no single name and two divergent notify sequences ŌĆö five concrete, verified findings, not speculative: (1) `draw()` called directly from ~10 drag-handler sites, bypassing `window.redrawPreview()`; (2) two different, overlapping "notify everyone" tails ŌĆö the selection setters' 4-call sequence vs. `showSlide`'s own 6-call sequence; (3) **a confirmed real bug** ŌĆö `showSlide()` never cleared `_selectedSceneElement`/`_selectedTextElement`, so a selection from page N could open editing controls on page N+1 that don't correspond to anything real there, and `js/contextPanel.js`'s scene-element branch only checked whether the selected object still existed *after* deciding to open a section (only to pick disclosure wording), never to gate opening the section at all; (4) `PageOps.reorderPage`/`moveToEnd` duplicated or short-circuited the otherwise-uniform `_afterMutation` pipeline instead of going through it consistently; (5) "Start Creating" triggered three independent, redundant re-render sequences on one click. Save (`js/projectManager.js`'s `serialize()`) and Publish (`js/storyDestinations.js`/`js/publishStudio.js`/`js/pdfWriter.js`, confirmed rendering through the identical `SlideRenderer.buildPayload()`+`.render()` pair as the editor canvas on the same live slide reference, zero bypasses) were investigated and found to already satisfy the sprint's own requirements ŌĆö explicitly left unchanged, stated rather than re-implemented for its own sake. **The fix**: new `js/pageRuntime.js` (`window.PageRuntime`) is a thin ownership/dispatch layer ŌĆö not a new rendering system ŌĆö wrapping the exact existing `js/app.js` functions via the same `configure({...})` host-binding pattern `js/objectStrip.js`/`js/contextPanel.js` already used. Read accessors: `getActivePage()` (ŌåÆ `AppState.slides[AppState.currentSlide]`, now the one source every panel's `getCurrentSlide` host binding points at ŌĆö `CardDesigner`/`PageDesigner`/`StickerStudio`/`ContextPanel`/`ObjectStrip` alike), `getRenderedObjects()` (ŌåÆ `{scene, text}`, naming the Creator Reconciliation Sprint's own render-tree contract as the Runtime's object-discovery API, no new shape), `getSelection()` (ŌåÆ `{sceneId, sceneType, textId}`), `selectionIsValid()` (does the current selection still resolve to something actually rendered on the active page right now ŌĆö `'image-holder'` always valid as the disclosed synthetic exception, everything else checked against the render tree). Mutation entry points: `openPage(index)` (delegates to `showSlide`), `clearSelection()`, and **two** explicit selection functions ŌĆö `selectSceneObject(id,type)` / `selectTextObject(id)` ŌĆö deliberately not one `selectObject(id,type)` dispatching on `type==='text'`, because a Scene Object can itself legitimately carry `type:'text'` (a Layer Pack text entry like a Museum Caption) which is a completely different selection channel from Story Theme text furniture (Story Text/Handle/Footer/Page Number); an earlier single-function draft silently rerouted a selected Museum-Caption-shaped Scene Object into the wrong channel, caught by the sprint's own Playwright verification (clicking Museum Caption after Wax Seal left the Context Panel showing Wax Seal's stale banner) and fixed by the two-function split before shipping ŌĆö a real bug found and fixed via testing, not a hypothetical. `notify()` is the one dispatch function (`redrawPreview()` + `CardDesigner.refresh()` + `ContextPanel.refresh()` + `ObjectStrip.refresh()`) both selection setters and `showSlide` now end with, replacing their two divergent tails. The selection-teardown fix for finding (3) lives inside `showSlide` itself, not only inside `PageRuntime.openPage()` ŌĆö since `showSlide` is the one real choke point every page-change path already funnels through (thumbnail clicks, `PageOps._refreshSelection`, session restore, `CreationFlow`, `PublishStudio`'s "Fix in Editor", `ThemeEngine`'s theme-apply path all call it directly, confirmed by grep, zero bypasses), putting the fix there means every one of those callers gets it for free. `js/contextPanel.js`'s scene-element branch now checks `PageRuntime`-backed object existence **before** opening any section, not only before choosing disclosure wording ŌĆö a selection left over from a different page now falls through to the default view instead of a live-looking but id-blind editor. `js/pageOps.js`'s `reorderPage` and `moveToEnd` now always route through `_afterMutation` (the "not selected" branch's hand-duplicated pipeline collapsed into `_afterMutation(idx!==-1?idx:AppState.currentSlide)`, reusing the exact same object-identity-lookup logic instead of a separate inline copy). `js/creationFlow.js`'s `_finish` now calls `PageRuntime.openPage(AppState.currentSlide)` once instead of three independent re-render sequences. Deliberately **not** folded into `notify()`: the ~10 direct `draw()` calls inside continuous mousemove drag-tick handlers (resize/scene/text drag, image pan) ŌĆö a correct, pre-existing 60fps performance decision the code's own comments already call out, not an oversight; their `mouseup` drag-end handlers already run the full refresh sequence once the gesture completes, so routing every mousemove tick through `notify()` would have been a real, unrequested performance regression. Verified end-to-end via a new Playwright Runtime Pass test plus full regression across the existing Creator suite (`regression.js`, `final_qa.js`, `frame_variation_test3.js`, `ws_check.js`, `publish_stages.js`, `lang_check.js`, `baseline3.js`, `scene_object_test.js`, `sticker_owner_check.js`, `diag_layerpack3.js`) ŌĆö all pass unchanged, zero console errors; two pre-existing, already-stale failures (`objstrip_check.js`, `ctx_states2.js`, confirmed via `git stash` in the preceding sprint to fail identically on the unmodified codebase) carried forward unresolved, not new regressions. `docs/CREATOR_PAGE_RUNTIME.md` is the new canonical doc for runtime ownership, the Active Page lifecycle, object discovery, the selection lifecycle, the Runtime Pass, `PageRuntime`'s public API, and a full per-consumer before/after table. No Builder redesign, no Theme contract redesign, no rendering-engine redesign, no second page model, no second runtime ŌĆö the existing center pane was promoted into the canonical Page Runtime, exactly as scoped.)

- Creator Acceptance Sprint ŌĆö Theme Fidelity Pass (Museum Gallery) (`docs/CREATOR_THEME_FIDELITY.md`; a P0 product-convergence sprint, explicitly not a feature or architecture sprint, judged by one acceptance test: a Builder-authored page must open in Creator exactly as Builder's own Runtime Preview shows it, before any Story Author content exists ŌĆö "Creator does not recreate the page. Creator does not reinterpret the Theme." Investigation (three parallel code-verified traces: the compiled Museum Gallery package + Builder's Runtime Preview semantics via `engineRuntime.js`'s `_paintHolder`, Creator's actual image-less render/panel behaviour, and whether any placeholder mechanism already existed to reuse) found one root cause, not several unrelated bugs: `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_resolveBorder(s)` resolved an Artwork Theme's Frame only `if(hasImage)` (a deliberate Sprint 9.3 decision, "if a page contains no artwork, Artwork Theme has no effect," now reversed specifically for the Frame chrome). Because the Frame/mat/ornament/stroke/caption draw block and every Frame/Holder-scoped Layer Pack entry (Wax Seal, Gallery Spotlight, Museum Caption) only run when that resolved border is non-null, the entire World disappeared behind one boolean ŌĆö wall tone was already correctly image-independent (`_resolveWallTone`, Sprint 9.7), and every function the frame block calls (`_artworkBorder`/`_resolveArtworkFields`/`_drawPictureFrameFill`/`_drawArtworkPresentation`/`_drawArtworkCaption`) was *already* purely theme/card-override-driven with zero `s.image` dependency, so lifting the one gate closed the entire visual gap with no further drawing-code changes; only `_drawImage` itself correctly still requires a real image. `_artworkTheme(s)` returning `null` whenever no Artwork Theme is active scopes the fix to Artwork Theme pages only (zero effect on plain Story Theme pages), and Quote composition's own pre-existing `if(_composition==='quote'){...}else if(_border){...}` short-circuit keeps Museum Gallery's frame-less Quote layout frame-less regardless. New `_drawArtworkPlaceholder(panelRect,border,chromeColor)` mirrors Cover/Hook/End's own existing `_drawSceneImageHolder` "Add an image" dashed-placeholder pattern (Sprint 6.2) for the one shape that never had an equivalent ŌĆö a Story-role page's artwork content rect, since `SceneEngine.getRenderData` returns `null` for Story role by design ŌĆö but takes an explicit `chromeColor` (the same wall-tone luminance check already used for Handle/Page Number text) instead of the original's hardcoded white, since a light Frame Variation's wall (Museum Gallery's own "Classic White") would make a white dashed line invisible; wired into `render()` right after the existing image-draw call, using `_holderRectFor` so it sits exactly where the real picture will land. `js/objectStrip.js`'s Artwork card ŌĆö previously hard-gated on `slide.image` truthy, the reason "Tap Artwork Place ŌåÆ Replace Artwork" was unreachable before an image existed ŌĆö now always shows once there's no Scene blueprint, worded "Artwork Place" before a picture exists and "Artwork" once it does. **A second, deeper bug found while verifying this exact fix, not assumed**: the card's original gate was `slide.pageType==='story'`, but a freshly Creation-Flow-created page's `pageType` never gets promoted away from `'blank'` ŌĆö grepped every `pageType=` assignment site and confirmed nothing in `js/creationFlow.js`/`js/pageOps.js` ever sets it to `'story'` for that path (only the sidebar's separate bulk "Upload Images" importer does, on pages *it* creates); this would have left the Artwork card permanently absent for the actual primary onboarding path even after every other fix in this sprint. Fixed by matching the exact criterion `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s own `_hasScene` gate already uses (`SceneEngine.getRenderData(slide)!==null`) instead of a hardcoded pageType string ŌĆö correctly covers `'story'` and `'blank'` alike (and any future non-scene pageType), since the renderer already treats them identically. `js/contextPanel.js`'s default view gained a "Welcome to `<World Icon> <World Name>`" heading (new `_worldIdentity()`, reusing the exact `ThemeEngine.getActiveArtworkThemeId`/`ThemeRegistry.get` lookup `js/app.js`'s own header readout already makes) plus a two-line ownership legend ("Ō£Å’ĖÅ Objects marked editable can be changed." / "­¤īŹ Objects marked World belong to the World."), above the pre-existing, completely unchanged Page Style/Caption/Background/Add Sticker controls ŌĆö real Story-Author capability, not removed to match the acceptance spec's own illustrative minimal mockup. `_renderArtworkActions()` now reads "­¤¢╝’ĖÅ Add Artwork" before any picture exists, "­¤¢╝’ĖÅ Replace Artwork" after, and hides "Ō£é’ĖÅ Crop / Rotate" until there's something to crop (it already silently no-oped with nothing selected ŌĆö hiding it removes a dead button, not new capability). Object Strip's World-owned badge glyph changed from ­¤öÆ to ­¤īŹ to match the acceptance checklist's own explicit vocabulary and the ­¤īŹ icon Context Panel's World-object disclosure banner already used ŌĆö text/glyph only, the editable/owner gating logic (already correctly distinguishing editable, locked-World, and locked-Story) is unchanged. **Checked directly against the acceptance checklist and found already correct, no change made**: Sticker Studio (already CSS-hidden until "Add a Sticker" is clicked, never a default panel), the sidebar's "Upload Images" button (a separate, pre-existing bulk multi-page importer, never part of Context Panel's default view), `CardDesigner`'s image section (already gracefully disables its controls with no image), and Publish (`js/storyDestinations.js`/`js/publishStudio.js` render through the identical `buildPayload`+`render` pair as the editor canvas, so the fix reaches Publish for free ŌĆö verified directly by opening Publish Studio on an image-less page and confirming it renders without error, not merely asserted). **Two findings investigated and deliberately left disclosed, not fixed, per the sprint's own "do not redesign the Theme contract / do not build new capability" constraints**: `representation.defaultFrame` is authored in the compiled package but never consumed anywhere in the Creator runtime (Builder-authoring-time-only today) ŌĆö zero visible effect for Museum Gallery specifically since both real representations point at `classic-white`, whose fields are deliberately empty and already delegate to the `gallery` Presentation Preset's own System Defaults, so wiring it would render identically for this theme; flagged as real follow-up work for a future theme whose representations pick a non-default Frame Variation. The Museum Gallery `handle` Layer Pack entry's default-to-`'spotlight'` decoration kind (when a layer has no `decoration` payload) was investigated as a possible bug but found genuinely ambiguous ŌĆö `gallery-spotlight`, a different, clearly intentional entry, relies on the exact same default for its own glow, so "fixing" it risks silently removing a real, intentional effect and second-guessing Builder's own authored intent, which the sprint's own Golden Rule explicitly forbids; left untouched. Verified via a new Playwright test (`museum_fidelity_test.js`, scratch-only) driving a Museum-Gallery-shaped synthetic fixture (frameVariations + a full layerPack) through the real acceptance journey: before any picture, the canvas already paints wall tone + a mat/frame/placeholder (pixel-sampled non-blank), Object Strip lists Background/Artwork Place/Wax Seal/Gallery Spotlight (Museum Caption correctly absent ŌĆö an empty caption with no title still draws nothing, matching pre-existing correct behaviour), Context Panel's default view shows the Welcome heading + legend, and selecting Artwork Place shows only "Add Artwork"; after a real picture is set, the placeholder is gone (sampled pixel matches the uploaded image), the card renames to "Artwork," and selecting it shows "Replace Artwork" + "Crop / Rotate"; Publish Studio opens and renders without error on the image-less page. Full regression across the existing Creator suite (`regression.js`, `final_qa.js`, `frame_variation_test3.js`, `ws_check.js`, `publish_stages.js`, `lang_check.js`, `baseline3.js`, `scene_object_test.js`, `sticker_owner_check.js`, `diag_layerpack3.js`, `runtime_pass_test.js`) passes unchanged, zero console errors throughout. No Builder redesign, no Theme contract redesign, no new object model, no new editing capability ŌĆö every change either lifts a single overly-strict gate or makes an already-correct capability reachable at the right moment.)

- Museum Gallery Fidelity Trace ŌĆö real `.vtheme`, not a fixture, surfaces two silent crashes (a direct follow-up to the Theme Fidelity Pass above, requested explicitly to re-run the same acceptance journey against the real, compiled `themes/MuseumGallery.vtheme` file loaded through the real production import path ŌĆö `ThemeEngine.importThemeFile()` ŌåÆ `ThemeRegistry.importPackage()` ŌĆö rather than the hand-written, Museum-Gallery-*shaped* synthetic fixture every earlier test in that sprint had used. This surfaced two real, previously-invisible bugs no synthetic fixture had ever exercised. **Bug 1 ŌĆö a real crash, silently swallowed everywhere**: tracing the real file produced a fully blank canvas (`getImageData`ŌåÆ`[0,0,0,0]`), empty `SlideRenderer.getSceneElements()`/`getTextElements()`, and Object Strip's "Nothing on this page yet." Manually re-invoking `showSlide()`/`SlideRenderer.render()` outside the app's own defensive `try{...}catch(e){}` wrappers surfaced the real exception: `TypeError: Cannot read properties of null (reading 'variants')` at `js/themeEngine.js`'s `_defaultOptionsFor`, called via `getOptions()`ŌåÆ`resolveTheme()`ŌåÆ`renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `buildPayload()`. Root cause: Museum Gallery's `supportedCreationTypes` has no `'story'` entry, so `js/creationFlow.js`'s `_finish()` only ever calls `applyArtworkTheme()` for it, never `applyTheme()` ŌĆö on a genuinely fresh project whose only chosen World is a pure Artwork Theme, the Story Theme (`ThemeEngine.getActiveTheme()`) never gets set. This is not hypothetical: `js/themeRegistry.js`'s own comments disclose that Studio ships with **zero built-in themes today** (`OFFICIAL_THEMES` deliberately commented out, `storybook-classic` "deliberately left unresolved rather than rewired... exists only until reintroduced by import/publish") ŌĆö a null active Story Theme is an accepted, normal state in this Repository-only architecture, not something to paper over with a fallback registration. The real bug was that nothing downstream *handled* that accepted null state: `_defaultOptionsFor(theme)` dereferenced `theme.variants`/`.slide`/`.holder` assuming a real object; `resolveTheme()` dereferenced `base.id`/`base.frame.color`/etc. the same way; and `buildPayload()` called `ThemeEngine.resolveTheme()`/`getOptions()` **directly, with no try/catch**, bypassing the exact safety net `_theme(s)`/`_options(s)` already established elsewhere in the same file (both already fall back to `FALLBACK_THEME`/`FALLBACK_OPTIONS` on any thrown exception) ŌĆö and because `creationFlow.js`'s `_finish()` and `app.js`'s `showSlide()` both wrap their own calls in `try{...}catch(e){}` by design (so one bad refresh doesn't wedge the UI), the exception was caught and silently discarded at every call site, never surfacing as a console error. Fixed by normalizing `theme=theme||{}` at the top of `_defaultOptionsFor` (same "no theme = System Defaults" behaviour every other code path already has), adding a `_NO_THEME_FALLBACK` constant to `resolveTheme()` (deliberately identical values to `slideRenderer.js`'s own `FALLBACK_THEME`), and adding the same try/catch + fallback pattern to `buildPayload()`'s two direct calls for defense-in-depth ŌĆö this fixes the crash for every caller of `getOptions()`/`resolveTheme()` at once, several of which (`js/cardDesigner.js`, `js/contextPanel.js`) call these functions with no try/catch of their own and were equally exposed. **Bug 2 ŌĆö the `handle` Layer Pack entry drew an unintended glow and a nonsensical Object Strip card**: with the crash fixed, the real Object Strip showed a fourth World card literally labelled "Handle" ŌĆö meaningless to a child. `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md` ┬¦7 already documents the exact intended contract: an entry naming `page-number`/`handle` with no real content payload is **declarative-only** ŌĆö "the actual pixels are still drawn by the pre-existing, unrelated engine feature it names... never a second, competing renderer," and `position` is "only meaningful on the declarative handle/page-number ids." `_layerDrawText` already honours this correctly for `page-number` (no `text.content`/`.source` ŌåÆ returns null); `_layerDrawDecoration` had no equivalent guard for `type:"decoration"` entries ŌĆö with no `decoration` payload, `kind` defaulted to `'spotlight'`, so `handle` (real package: `type:"decoration"`, no `decoration` field, `position:"bottom-right"`) silently painted an unintended lighting glow across the whole slide *and* got pushed onto the render tree as its own selectable Scene Object. Fixed by making `_layerDrawDecoration` return `null` when `!layer.decoration && layer.position` ŌĆö the exact, spec-sanctioned signature of a declarative-only entry; `gallery-spotlight` (Museum Gallery's other content-less decoration entry) is unaffected since it has no `decoration` payload but also no `position` field, so it still resolves through the existing `kind==='spotlight'` default and keeps its real, intentional glow, confirmed unchanged in every regression fixture. **One separate, disclosed, NOT-fixed finding**: the Context Panel's "Welcome to `<icon>` Museum Gallery" heading shows the generic ­¤ō¢ fallback instead of ­¤Åø’ĖÅ for the real imported package, since `ThemeRegistry.get('museum-gallery')` returns only the `theme` sub-object (no `themeIcon` key at all ŌĆö that field lives only in the compiled package's `manifest.themeIcon`, and `ThemeRegistry.get()` discards `manifest` entirely); this is a pre-existing gap in the exact same lookup pattern `js/app.js`'s own header readout already uses, not something the acceptance checklist's named criteria cover (which concern the ownership legend/badges functioning, not which glyph appears) ŌĆö disclosed rather than silently fixed, since resolving it means deciding whether `ThemeRegistry.get()` should start merging manifest fields onto the theme object, a real design question out of this trace's scope. Verified via a new Playwright test (`real_museum_trace.js`, scratch-only) loading the real `.vtheme` through the real import path and driving Theme Load ŌåÆ Scene Creation ŌåÆ Object Registry/Runtime ŌåÆ Thumbnail ŌåÆ Object Strip ŌåÆ Context Panel end to end, confirming all 7 of the requester's own acceptance criteria (museum shows in thumbnail and main canvas, Object Strip lists every real Builder object with no phantom entries, Context Panel's ­¤īŹ/Ō£Å’ĖÅ disclosure works correctly on selection, no "Nothing on this page yet," no renderer fallback to an empty scene). Full regression across every existing suite (`regression.js`, `final_qa.js`, `frame_variation_test3.js`, `ws_check.js`, `publish_stages.js`, `lang_check.js`, `baseline3.js`, `scene_object_test.js`, `sticker_owner_check.js`, `diag_layerpack3.js`, `runtime_pass_test.js`, `museum_fidelity_test.js`) passes unchanged, zero console errors. No Builder redesign, no Theme contract redesign, no new object model ŌĆö both fixes are root-cause corrections to existing, documented contracts that a synthetic test fixture had accidentally been masking all along. See `docs/CREATOR_THEME_FIDELITY.md`'s new Addendum section for the full account.)

- Screen 2 World Library Card ŌĆö Thumbnail vs. Hero Image (a real, user-reported bug: the World Library/Vihu Worlds row card on Screen 2 was rendering a World's Hero Image (`manifest.previewImage`) instead of its Thumbnail (`manifest.thumbnail`) ŌĆö two separate assets Builder's own Overview screen authors distinctly (Thumbnail for small card/list contexts, Hero Image as the larger representative source), silently conflated in `js/creationFlow.js`'s `_themePreview()` into one generic `image` field that always preferred `previewImage`. Confirmed directly, not assumed: the real Museum Gallery `.vtheme`'s `manifest.thumbnail` (386 chars) and `manifest.previewImage` (1758 chars) are genuinely different images, and before this fix the World Library card's rendered `<img src>` matched the Hero Image, never the Thumbnail. Fixed by having `_themePreview()` resolve both fields separately (`thumbnail`/`heroImage`, each through `ThemeRegistry.resolveAssetRef()` exactly as before) instead of collapsing them into one; `_worldRowCard()` (the World Library/Vihu Worlds row card this bug was reported against) now reads `pv.thumbnail`; `_repThumbnail()`'s own World-level fallback (used only when a Representation has no `thumbnail` of its own, for the larger Screen 2 Representation carousel slide) now prefers `pv.heroImage` before falling back to `pv.thumbnail` then the icon glyph ŌĆö a more appropriate asset for that bigger visual context, not a behaviour change for any theme that already sets a per-Representation thumbnail. `paintPreview()`'s own top badge is unaffected ŌĆö it only ever showed `pv.icon` (the `themeIcon` emoji), never an image, and still doesn't. One related, disclosed-not-fixed finding: `js/themeEngine.js`'s `_renderThemeCard()` (the separate, older in-editor Theme Library picker modal, out of scope for this Screen-2-specific report) has the identical `previewImage`-only pattern and may have the same small-card-shows-hero-image issue ŌĆö left untouched since it wasn't the reported surface and touching it wasn't requested. Verified via Playwright against the real `MuseumGallery.vtheme`: the World Library card's rendered image now byte-matches `manifest.thumbnail` exactly (not `previewImage`) via full-string comparison (a same-PNG-header short-prefix check was insufficient and initially gave a false pass, corrected before relying on it). Full existing regression suite (`regression.js`, `final_qa.js`, `frame_variation_test3.js`, `ws_check.js`, `publish_stages.js`, `lang_check.js`, `baseline3.js`, `scene_object_test.js`, `sticker_owner_check.js`, `diag_layerpack3.js`, `runtime_pass_test.js`, `museum_fidelity_test.js`, `real_museum_trace.js`, `real_museum_selection_check.js`) passes unchanged, zero console errors. No Builder/Theme-contract/architecture change ŌĆö a two-field resolution fix inside one existing Creation Flow helper.)

- Object Strip Label + Zero-Holder Layout fixes (two real, user-reported Builder->Creator gaps, both root-caused, not guessed at, from a real authored World ("My Artwork Gallery") screenshot: an Object Strip showing 3 visually-identical "Scene SinŌĆ”" cards, and a request that "if the builder theme does not have holder so does in creator." **Investigation confirmed the actual pixel z-order was already correct** ŌĆö a genuine Scene-hosted Background (`setSceneBackground`, a full-bleed `{0,0}/{1,1}` fill) converges onto the pre-existing `target:'slide'` scope, which `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `render()` already paints first, before the Frame/Panel/every Place ŌĆö traced and confirmed via code reading, not assumed. **The real Object Strip bug**: `tools/world-builder-v2/js/services/builder.js`'s `convergeSceneLayer()` never carried a Scene Layer's own author-given `name` (e.g. "Background," set by `js/projectModel.js`'s `addSceneLayer`/`setSceneBackground`) into the compiled Layer Pack entry's `label` field ŌĆö so `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_pushLayerObject` fell back to `_humanizeLayerId(layer.id)`, humanizing the compiled id `scene-<sceneId>-<layerId>`; since every Layer on one Scene shares that same Scene-id prefix, they all read as near-identical truncated "Scene SinŌĆ”" cards no matter how many genuinely distinct Layers a Scene has. Fixed with one additive field: `convergeSceneLayer`'s `base` object now carries `label: layer.name || undefined`, so each converged Layer shows its own real name. **The real "no Holder" gap**: a Scene converged with zero Places has no way to tell Creator apart from "one Place, no Frame chosen yet" ŌĆö both produce `representation.defaultFrame: null` ŌĆö because the compiled `theme.layouts[]` entry never recorded a Scene's actual Place count, despite Sprint 9.6 having reserved exactly this field ("`holders`: Reserved, always 1 in V1") for exactly this purpose; Museum Gallery's own real hand-authored Layouts don't even set it. `convergeScene()` now populates `holders: holders.length` on the converged Layout ŌĆö the real count, `0` for a genuinely Place-less Scene. Creator's consuming side: `renderer/slideRenderer.js` gained `_activeLayoutHolders(s)` (resolves the active Layout preset, reads its `holders` field, `null` when absent) and `_resolveBorder`'s Artwork Theme branch now skips resolving Frame/mat/wall chrome entirely when `_activeLayoutHolders(s)===0` ŌĆö exported as `SlideRenderer.activeLayoutHolderCount()`; `js/objectStrip.js`'s Artwork Place card gains the matching `!noHolderAuthored` check before showing itself. Both changes are strictly additive and null-safe: absent the `holders` field (every Layout that predates this, including Museum Gallery's own hand-authored ones), the count resolves to `null`, never `0`, so every existing theme's behaviour is completely unchanged ŌĆö confirmed directly via the full existing regression suite, `museum_fidelity_test.js`, and `real_museum_trace.js` all passing unchanged with Museum Gallery's own "Artwork Place" card still showing exactly as before. Verified via two independent passes: (1) a synthetic Playwright theme with two Layouts (`holders:0` and `holders:1`) confirmed the Artwork Place card is correctly absent for the zero-Holder Layout and correctly present for the other, both consuming a Layer Pack entry whose `label` renders as a clean "Background" instead of a humanized id; (2) `builder.js`'s real `convergeScene`/`convergeSceneLayer` methods driven directly (no mock/reimplementation) against a hand-built zero-Place Scene and a one-Place Scene, confirming the real producer emits `holders:0`/`holders:1` correctly and the real `label` field carries through unmodified. `tools/world-builder-v2/verify/goldenBuild.js`'s full 30-assertion suite passes unchanged. `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md` ┬¦6/┬¦7 updated ŌĆö the `holders` field's row now documents its real producer/consumer instead of only "Reserved, always 1"; a new `label` row documents the Layer Pack field. No Engine V2/Scene Model/architecture change; both fixes are additive fields threaded through an existing, already-open compile/render pipeline.)

- World Builder ŌĆö Overflow-Menu Duplicate Didn't Actually Leave View Mode (a real, user-reported bug: "Builder: duplicate option is not working for official theme... we should be able to duplicate it to use as a template for a new theme"). **Root cause, found already half-disclosed in the code**: an Official World opens in read-only View Mode (`currentProjectReadOnly`), determined by checking whether the open Project's `manifest.id` is in `_lastKnownOfficialIds` ŌĆö and Duplicate is deliberately the one action View Mode leaves enabled, since it's documented as "exactly how you're meant to leave View Mode." The Welcome-screen card's own Duplicate button already regenerated the copy's manifest id for exactly this reason (a plain `ProjectStore.duplicate()` keeps the source's own id, which would make the copy match `_lastKnownOfficialIds` too and silently open in View Mode again) ŌĆö but the in-Workspace overflow menu's "Ō¦ē Duplicate World" (`#wb-menu-duplicate`, the one reachable from *inside* an open Official World, i.e. the actual reported flow) was added afterwards and called `ProjectStore.duplicate()` directly, missing that same fix. The practical symptom: opening an Official Theme, clicking Duplicate from the overflow menu, and getting back to the Welcome screen ŌĆö where the "duplicate" opened right back into View Mode, indistinguishable from the original, reading as "Duplicate doesn't work." **Fix**: extracted the Welcome-card's existing id-regeneration logic into one shared `_duplicateProject(project)` helper in `tools/world-builder-v2/js/worldBuilderApp.js`, used by both call sites now ŌĆö the card's own button (refactored, behaviour unchanged) and the overflow menu's `menuDuplicate` handler (the actual fix). Verified via Playwright: both the Welcome-card Duplicate button and the in-Workspace overflow-menu Duplicate now produce a new Project whose `manifest.id` is a fresh, distinct id (`<source-id>-copy-<random>`), not the source's own id ŌĆö confirmed directly by listing every Project's id via `ProjectModel.manifest()` before and after each duplicate action, for both call sites independently. `goldenBuild.js`'s full 30-assertion suite passes unchanged (no Build/Publish/Validate pipeline touched ŌĆö this is Welcome/Workspace UI wiring only). No Repository/Theme-contract/architecture change.

- World Builder ŌĆö Duplicate Silently Failing on Large Worlds (a follow-up, second bug found under the first fix: after the overflow-menu Duplicate fix above landed, a user report ("nothing happens, no error, no new card, the page just flickers") described a symptom the id-regeneration fix couldn't explain ŌĆö reproduced directly, not assumed, with a real 4MB test Project rather than a mock. **Root cause**: `js/projectStore.js`'s `duplicate()` deep-copies a Project's entire `files` map (every uploaded Thumbnail/Hero Image/asset) and calls `_writeAll()`, but ŌĆö unlike `save()`, which AV-009 already hardened to return `{ok,error}` after an earlier Hero-Image-vanishing bug ŌĆö `duplicate()` discarded `_writeAll`'s result and always returned the in-memory `copy` object regardless of whether the write actually reached `localStorage`. Duplicating a World roughly doubles that World's own storage footprint (original + copy both now exist simultaneously), which is exactly the realistic case that pushes an image-heavy World over this browser's per-origin quota ŌĆö confirmed by reproducing the exact "flicker, no new card, zero console output" symptom against a real, deliberately oversized Project (Chromium's real quota, not a simulated one). **Fix**: `duplicate()` now mirrors `save()`'s own `{project, ok, error}` shape; the shared `_duplicateProject()` helper (used by both the Welcome-card and in-Workspace overflow-menu Duplicate actions, per the fix above) propagates that result instead of assuming success, and a new `_reportDuplicateFailure()` shows a real, honest `window.alert()` ŌĆö "Couldn't duplicate ... this browser's storage is full. Try deleting an old World you no longer need, then try again." ŌĆö the same "never silently lie about success" principle AV-009 already established for uploads, now closing the one remaining code path (Duplicate) that had never gotten it. Verified via Playwright against a real, reproducible browser-level quota failure (not a mock `localStorage.setItem` override): before the fix, silent failure with zero signal; after, the exact alert text fires and no phantom project is created. Confirmed the normal, non-quota-exceeded case (small/typical Worlds) is unaffected ŌĆö both Duplicate paths still produce a correctly id-regenerated copy exactly as the prior fix established. `goldenBuild.js`'s full 30-assertion suite passes unchanged ŌĆö this fix touches only `js/projectStore.js` and `js/worldBuilderApp.js`'s Duplicate wiring, no Build/Publish/Validate pipeline change.)

- World Builder ŌĆö Browser Storage Meter (Welcome screen) (a direct follow-up requested after the Duplicate quota-failure fix: the user's own Worlds already sat close to the limit, Delete wasn't a real option for them, and there was no way to see this coming ŌĆö "why don't u put a real time memory show on the page. total-consumed-available." **A real, disclosed constraint shaped the design**: no browser API reports an exact `localStorage` quota (it has always been governed separately from the async Storage API's own much larger, IndexedDB/CacheStorage-oriented `navigator.storage.estimate()` quota figure, which would be actively misleading if shown as "Available" here) ŌĆö so rather than fabricate a precise Total/Available pair no browser actually promises, the meter shows what's genuinely measurable (`js/projectStore.js`'s new `getStorageStats()`, a real `new Blob([raw]).size` measurement ŌĆö UTF-16-accurate, not `.length` ŌĆö of every localStorage key this module and its two small siblings actually write: `vihu-world-builder-projects`, the editing-context resume-position, the Workspace layout preference) next to one disclosed, conservative reference floor (5 MB, the lowest ceiling any mainstream browser is known to enforce), rather than a fabricated "Total." **New `.wb-storage-meter` section** on the Welcome screen (`index.html`, between "My World Projects" and "Explore Worlds"): a used-MB readout, a percentage-of-floor bar (green under 75%, gold 75ŌĆō99%, red at/over 100%), and an explanatory note that flips to a real, actionable warning once at or past the floor ŌĆö explicitly naming that Publish/Promote moves a *built Theme* to Supabase's Personal/Official Repository, but the editable Project itself stays local and the only real relief is removing a World Project no longer needed, correcting the user's own stated belief that "everything is on Supabase" (only compiled, published output ever leaves the browser ŌĆö the editable Scene/Place/Experience/Frame data this meter measures never does). Wired into the existing `renderMyWorlds()` (called before its own empty-state early return, so the meter shows a real `0.00 MB` baseline even with zero Worlds, not a blank gap) ŌĆö since every Create/Rename/Duplicate/Delete already calls `renderMyWorlds()`, the meter updates live with no separate refresh mechanism of its own. Verified via Playwright: baseline 0%, a real 2MB asset save showing 40%/correct bar width, a subsequent real Duplicate showing 4MB/80%, and (via a controlled `getStorageStats()` stand-in, since reliably forcing this sandbox's own real quota to a precise round number isn't practical) the Ōēź100% state showing the red fill and the real warning copy. `goldenBuild.js`'s full 30-assertion suite passes unchanged ŌĆö purely additive Welcome-screen UI and one new read-only `ProjectStore` query, no Build/Publish/Validate pipeline change.)

- World Builder ŌĆö "My World Projects" Lists Personal/Official/Growing, Not Just Local (a direct follow-up to the Browser Storage Meter work, closing the gap surfaced when the user asked why an incognito window showed neither Personal nor Official Themes ŌĆö "my world projects should list all my personal, official and growing projects" ŌĆö "without any local storage." **Root cause, not a bug**: "My World Projects" only ever listed local `ProjectStore` records; `_annotateProjectBadges` already fetched `ThemeRepositoryClient.list('personal')`/`list('official')`, but only to *badge* a local card that happened to share its World Id ŌĆö a Personal/Official Theme with no local draft on this browser (never published from here, deleted locally, or a genuinely fresh/incognito profile) had no card at all. **Product decision, confirmed via AskUserQuestion rather than assumed**: an Official-only card stays permanently read-only (matching View Mode's existing "the only way out is Duplicate, never edit in place" rule); a Personal-only card should be editable when possible ŌĆö "this was discussed before too," referring to the existing Builder Project Cloud Backup (`js/services/projectSync.js`, pushes the full editable Project JSON to a `builder_projects` Supabase table, owner-scoped by the same anonymous session Personal Repository access already uses). **Implementation**: `projectSync.js` gained `list()` (selects every `builder_projects` row this session's own `auth.uid()` owns ŌĆö never throws, mirrors `push()`'s existing graceful-degradation shape). `worldBuilderApp.js`'s `_annotateProjectBadges` ŌĆö already fetching `personalRows`/`officialRows` ŌĆö now also computes `officialOnly`/`personalOnly` (rows whose `theme_id` matches no local Project's `manifest.id`) and renders a `_repoOnlyCard` for each: Official cards show a small standalone info modal (name/description/version, reusing `.wb-modal*` CSS but a fresh DOM tree ŌĆö NOT the shared `#wb-modal`/`_closeModal` machinery, which assumes an open Workspace `currentProject` and would be wrong to touch from the Welcome screen) and never open a Workspace. Personal-only cards cross-reference `ProjectSync.list()`'s backups by `data.files['manifest.json'].id === theme_id`: a match restores the **real, original editable Project JSON** (never a reconstruction from the compiled Theme, which is a confirmed one-way compile with no Scene/Place/Experience data to reverse ŌĆö see `docs/ENGINE_V2_PROMOTION_STRATEGY.md`'s own "no reverse path exists" finding) via `ProjectStore.save()` + `openWorkspace()`, exactly as if the local draft had never been deleted; no match shows a plain disclosed message ("no editable backup was found... it may have been published before Cloud Backup existed, or from a different browser session") rather than fabricating an empty draft. `renderMyWorlds()`'s early-return-when-empty was removed ŌĆö the empty-state message now toggles off only once repo-only cards actually render, so a genuinely empty *local* list still shows Personal/Official content when the Repository has it (the literal "without any local storage" case). A disclosed, structural limitation carries over from the anonymous-auth model documented in the Cloud Backup sprint: since both Personal Repository access and `builder_projects` ownership are scoped by this browser's own anonymous session (no real account system exists yet), a genuinely different browser/incognito profile gets its own new `auth.uid()` and correctly ŌĆö per RLS ŌĆö cannot see another session's Personal rows at all; this feature restores what the *current* session's own identity already owns, it does not solve cross-device sync. Verified via Playwright, including a real (not hand-rolled) Blank World generated through the actual Create-New-World flow, captured, re-tagged, and fed back as the "with backup" fixture so the restore exercises the genuine `openWorkspace()` path: zero local projects still renders exactly 3 repo-only cards (Official/Personal-with-backup/Personal-no-backup) with the empty-state message correctly hidden; the Official card's click opens a read-only info modal and never leaves the Welcome screen; the no-backup Personal card discloses the message and never leaves the Welcome screen; the with-backup Personal card restores the real Project and opens a fully editable Workspace; returning Home shows the restored World as an ordinary badged local card and exactly 2 repo-only cards remain (correct de-duplication). `goldenBuild.js`'s full 30-assertion suite and every prior Duplicate/Quota/Thumbnail/Holders/Storage-Meter regression script pass unchanged ŌĆö this is additive Welcome-screen UI plus one new read-only `ProjectSync` query, no Build/Publish/Validate/Repository-schema change.)

- Real Identity Foundation ŌĆö Base "Vihu Planet" Builder Account (SQL only, not yet wired in) (the first step toward real, persistent user accounts for World Builder, replacing the anonymous-per-browser identity model that every earlier Repository sprint (Phase 1 onward) has disclosed as a real limitation ŌĆö "a genuinely different browser/incognito profile gets its own new `auth.uid()` and correctly cannot see another session's Personal rows." Scoped via AskUserQuestion rather than assumed: the account is meant to eventually become the one identity Builder sessions sign in as, but explicitly **not** a permanent single-user ceiling ŌĆö "there can be more builders," i.e. this is the first of potentially several real accounts, each created the identical way. New `supabase/create_base_builder_user.sql` is a disclosed, unexecuted script (this sandbox cannot reach Supabase, same standing limitation every prior Supabase-touching sprint has hit) that creates one real email+password Supabase Auth user (`vihu-planet-builder@vihustudio.app` by default, `user_metadata:{name:"Vihu Planet",account_type:"base-builder"}`) by inserting directly into `auth.users`/`auth.identities` ŌĆö a well-known community pattern for seeding a sign-in-capable user without the officially documented Admin API (which needs a service-role key and a reachable-to-Supabase script environment this sandbox doesn't have); the script's own header discloses that fallback (a small Node script using `supabase.auth.admin.createUser()`) if the direct-insert approach ever errors against a real project's exact schema version. The literal password is a placeholder (`CHANGE_ME_STRONG_PASSWORD`) the account owner must substitute locally before running and never commit back ŌĆö no real credential is stored in this repository. **Deliberately does not require any schema change**: every RLS policy in `supabase/schema.sql` already keys off `auth.uid()` generically (`owner_id = auth.uid()::text`), with zero special-casing for anonymous vs. real authenticated sessions ŌĆö confirmed by reading the existing policies before writing this script, not assumed ŌĆö so a real signed-in session works identically to today's anonymous one for Personal Repository and Builder Project Cloud Backup access with no migration. **Explicitly disclosed as NOT done**: no sign-in UI exists anywhere in World Builder yet ŌĆö `js/themeRepositoryClient.js`'s `_ensureAuth()` still unconditionally calls `signInAnonymously()` for every session; this sprint only creates the account *in Supabase*, it does not yet change how Builder authenticates. Wiring a real sign-in flow (replacing anonymous auth, deciding what happens to content already owned by old anonymous sessions) is separate, not-yet-built follow-up work. Not verified against a live project for the same reason every earlier `supabase/schema.sql` change wasn't ŌĆö no network path to Supabase from this environment.)

- Real Identity Foundation ŌĆö Sign In (the direct follow-up to the base "Vihu Planet" builder account script: "sql executed now lets build the signin." Adds a real, optional sign-in flow to World Builder's Welcome screen, so a session can upgrade from the disposable per-browser anonymous identity every earlier Repository sprint has disclosed as a limitation to a real, persistent one. **`js/themeRepositoryClient.js`** gained three functions alongside the existing `_ensureAuth()` (left completely unchanged ŌĆö every session still gets a working anonymous identity with zero action required, matching the product decision that this account is "the first of potentially several real accounts," never a forced migration): `signIn(email,password)` (calls `client.auth.signInWithPassword()`, replaces the cached `_authPromise` so every subsequent `list()`/`load()`/`publish()`/`getStats()`/`reset()` call sees the new session immediately, never throws ŌĆö failures come back as `{ok:false,error}`), `signOut()` (ends the session and clears the cache, deliberately not re-establishing a fresh anonymous one itself ŌĆö the next `_ensureAuth()` call does that lazily, exactly like a first-ever page load, keeping this function's job to just "end the current session"), and `getIdentity()` (a read-only snapshot ŌĆö `{configured,signedIn,email}` ŌĆö for the UI, using a new `_isAnonymousUser(user)` helper that prefers the real Supabase `user.is_anonymous` flag and falls back to "has no email" only if that flag is ever absent). **A real, disclosed consequence, not a bug**: signing in *replaces* the active session ŌĆö Personal Themes and Builder Project Cloud Backups owned by whatever anonymous `auth.uid()` was active a moment before become invisible afterward, since RLS scopes everything by that id; this is a genuine sign-IN, not Supabase's separate "convert my anonymous session in place" mechanism, which this deliberately does not attempt. **New `#wb-identity-bar`** in `index.html`'s Welcome header, rendered by `worldBuilderApp.js`'s new `_renderIdentityBar()` (wired into both `showWelcome()` and the app's own boot sequence ŌĆö a real bug caught during first Playwright verification: boot never actually called `showWelcome()`, it called `renderMyWorlds()` directly, so the identity bar rendered blank until `_renderIdentityBar()` was added to that same boot call) ŌĆö four honest states matching the exact diagnostic-disclosure pattern `_annotateProjectBadges` already established (Repository unavailable / not configured / check failed / real content), with the real content being either "­¤æż Browsing anonymously" + a Sign In button or "Ō£ō Signed in as `<email>`" + a Sign Out button. **`_showSignInModal()`** reuses the standalone `_showInfoModal()` modal shell (built for the Repository-only info cards) with a real email+password form (`.wb-field-group`/`-label`/`-input`, the same classes every other Inspector field already uses, so the form needed zero new input styling) ŌĆö a failed sign-in shows an inline `.wb-signin-error` message and keeps the modal open for another attempt; a successful one closes the modal and re-renders both the identity bar and `renderMyWorlds()` (so Personal/Official Repository content immediately reflects the new identity, reusing the Repository-listing work from the previous sprint with no separate wiring). Verified via Playwright against a stateful mock `ThemeRepositoryClient` (anonymous ŌåÆ open modal ŌåÆ wrong password shows the inline error and keeps the modal open ŌåÆ correct password closes the modal and updates the bar to "Signed in as ..." ŌåÆ Sign Out reverts to "Browsing anonymously") with zero console errors; full regression across every prior Duplicate/Quota/Thumbnail/Holders/Storage-Meter/Repository-listing script and `goldenBuild.js`'s 30-assertion suite passes unchanged. No RLS/schema change was needed ŌĆö confirmed in the prior sprint that every policy already keys off `auth.uid()` generically. Studio itself (root `js/themeRepositoryClient.js`, shared by both `tools/world-builder-v2` and the main app) gained the same three functions, but no sign-in UI was added there ŌĆö this sprint's scope was World Builder's Welcome screen only, per the user's own literal request.)

- Repository-Only Card Thumbnails ŌĆö Real Image, Not Just the Icon Glyph (a real, user-reported bug found comparing two browser windows: "in non incognito the thumbnail is visible but in incognito its just a frame." Traced to the Repository-only card work above ŌĆö `ThemeRepositoryClient.list()` deliberately returns only `{theme_id,name,version,manifest}` ("keeps this a listing, not a load," per its own comment), never a resolved `assets` map, so `_repoOnlyCard` had nothing to build a real `<img>` from and always fell back to the manifest's plain `themeIcon` glyph; for an Artwork World that glyph is ­¤¢╝’ĖÅ, which visually reads as an empty picture frame rather than a broken feature ŌĆö exactly what the report described. **Fix**: new `_resolveRepoThumbnailURL(repositoryId, themeId, manifest)` calls the real `ThemeRepositoryClient.load(repositoryId, themeId)` ŌĆö the same call Studio's own `refreshFromRepository()` already makes for every repository theme ŌĆö whose returned `assets` map already carries a real signed Storage URL for `manifest.thumbnail`'s relative-path reference (Asset Repository Transition sprint); `_repoOnlyCard` now kicks this off asynchronously right after mounting and swaps the glyph for a real `<img>` once it resolves, so the card never blocks or looks broken while the request is in flight, and silently keeps the glyph if resolution fails (unreachable Repository, no thumbnail authored, etc.) rather than surfacing an error. Verified via Playwright with a mock `load()` returning a real embedded thumbnail: the card's `.wb-project-thumb` swaps to a real `<img>` with the correct source; full regression across the Duplicate/Repository-listing/Sign-In/Holders/Storage-Meter suites and `goldenBuild.js`'s 30-assertion suite passes unchanged.)

- Repository-Only Cards ŌĆö Real Read-Only View + Deep Clone (a direct follow-up to the Repository-Only Card work: "why can't it be a deep clone?" and "by view only means u cant edit them but u can still open them in read only mode" ŌĆö a Repository-only card (no local draft in this browser) no longer only shows a plain info modal; it opens a real Workspace, or clones into a real editable World, depending on ownership. **The hard limit, disclosed rather than glossed over**: a compiled Theme's Layouts/Frame Variations/Representations/Layer Pack are a confirmed ONE-WAY compile from Scenes/Places/Experiences (`docs/ENGINE_V2_PROMOTION_STRATEGY.md`'s own "no reverse path exists" finding ŌĆö `convergeSceneLayer()` keeps only the rendering-relevant subset of a Scene Layer and discards the Experience/Place/Holder authoring data that produced it) ŌĆö so "deep clone" means everything that CAN faithfully round-trip, not a byte-for-byte resurrection of the original authoring Scenes, which no data in the published package could ever reconstruct. **New shared `_materializeProjectFromPackage(pkg, opts)`** turns a real `ThemeRepositoryClient.load()` result into a valid, in-memory World Project file map: `manifest.json`/`metadata.json`/`theme.json` rebuilt from the compiled manifest, plus the compiled `layouts`/`frameVariations`/`representations`/`layerPack` arrays un-flattened straight back into real, individually editable `layouts/<id>.json`/`frames/<id>.json`/`representations/all.json`/`layer-packs/from-repository.json` files ŌĆö genuinely lossless for these, since the compiled arrays already carry every field those files would ŌĆö plus every real asset byte/signed-URL carried over verbatim (already keyed by the exact relative paths `manifest.thumbnail`/etc. reference, so no path translation is needed). `opts.newId` decides the fork: `false` keeps the real World Id (View ŌĆö must match for View Mode's own id-check); `true` regenerates a fresh id and appends "(Copy)" to the name (Clone), mirroring `_duplicateProject`'s own existing convention. **Official ŌåÆ View**: `_openRepositoryThemeReadOnly()` loads the package, materializes with the real id, adds it to `_lastKnownOfficialIds` (the same opportunistic cache `_annotateProjectBadges` already populates for a locally-matched Official card) so `openWorkspace()` correctly computes `currentProjectReadOnly=true`, and opens it ŌĆö **never persisted to `ProjectStore`**, relying on the pre-existing `_persist()` backstop (`if (currentProjectReadOnly) return;`) that already guarantees a read-only Project can never leak into `localStorage` even if some edit path were missed. **Personal-with-no-backup ŌåÆ direct Clone**: `_cloneRepositoryThemeAsNewWorld()` loads the package, materializes with a new id, actually saves it, and opens it fully editable immediately ŌĆö replacing the earlier "sorry, no editable backup was found" dead end with a real, working starting point built from the compiled Theme itself. **Leaving View Mode needed zero new UI**: the Workspace's own pre-existing overflow-menu "Ō¦ē Duplicate World" (`_duplicateProject(currentProject)`) already deep-copies whatever `currentProject` currently is with no assumption that it was ever itself persisted ŌĆö so it transparently clones the ephemeral, never-saved View materialization into a real, saved, editable World with the exact same mechanism a real local Official-badged card already used; the View Mode banner's copy was corrected from "Go to My Worlds and Duplicate this card" (which assumes a Welcome-screen card that a Repository-only View never has) to "Use the Ōŗ« menu above and choose Duplicate World," correct for both origins. **A real, disclosed architectural gap, not silently bridged**: world-builder-v2's own Workspace is Scene-first with no remaining Global Nav entry for the legacy Layouts/Frames/Representations/Layer Packs screens (retired on purpose in Builder V2 Slice 1) ŌĆö a materialized World with no Scenes (every Theme authored before the Scene Model existed, including Museum Gallery) opens showing the honest AV-008 "No Scene yet" empty state, not a browsable view of its real Layouts/Frames/Representations/Layer Pack content; that data is still real, still reachable through Frames' existing "Manage Theme Assets" bridge once a Scene/Place exists to reach it from, and still round-trips correctly through Validate/Build/Publish ŌĆö it just isn't independently browsable the way it was in the theme's own original authoring Project, a limitation of the Workspace's current navigation, not of the materialized data itself.
