Verified via Playwright: an Official card opens a real Workspace with the read-only banner shown and zero writes to `ProjectStore` before any action; the overflow menu's Duplicate World (enabled, exactly as View Mode already allows) produces a real, distinctly-id'd, fully editable clone carrying the real Layouts/Frames/Representations content over, verified field-by-field; a Personal-no-backup card clones directly into an editable Workspace with no read-only banner; the original Repository row still correctly shows as repo-only afterward, since Clone regenerates a new World Id rather than claiming the original's; full regression across every prior Duplicate/Repository-listing/Sign-In/Thumbnail/Holders/Storage-Meter script and `goldenBuild.js`'s 30-assertion suite passes unchanged.)

- Repository-Only Clone ŌĆö Auto-Publish to Personal Instead of a Local Draft (a direct follow-up to the View + Deep Clone work above, driven by a real design question: "why should we not push this as personal theme. this will help in saving local storage and nothing gets seen by creator till its official correct?" ŌĆö **confirmed via direct code read before building anything**: `js/themeRegistry.js`'s `refreshFromRepository()` filters `repos.filter(function(repo){ return repo.kind==='official'; })`, so Creator/Studio genuinely never discovers a Personal Repository Theme, only Official ones ŌĆö the premise behind the question is correct, not assumed. Offered the safer alternative (local draft + a prompt to publish later) via AskUserQuestion; the explicit answer was "Yes, auto-publish immediately." **`_cloneRepositoryThemeAsNewWorld(repositoryId, themeId, displayName)`** (signature widened from taking a full `entry` to a bare `themeId`, since the ephemeral-View clone path below has no `entry` object to hand it) now runs the real, unmocked headless pipeline on every clone: materialize (`newId:true`) ŌåÆ `ProjectCompiler.runBuild()` (the exact function Check & Build's own button calls) ŌåÆ on success, `ThemeRepositoryClient.publish('personal', {manifest, theme, assetsRaw})` ŌåÆ on success, `ProjectSync.push()` (Builder Project Cloud Backup, so the real editable Project ŌĆö not just the compiled Theme ŌĆö survives for a future "Personal-with-backup" restore) ŌåÆ a plain success alert, back to Welcome, **zero local `ProjectStore` write** for the happy path. A shared `keepAsLocalDraft(materialized, reasonSuffix)` is the one fallback for every failure mode (`ProjectCompiler` unavailable, Build/Validation fails, `publish` unavailable, publish call fails or throws) ŌĆö always a real, working local editable draft with an honest, specific reason in the alert, never a silent dead end. **Real Validation gaps found and fixed via live testing, not assumed**: a naively materialized clone failed real Validation with 13 errors on first attempt (`debug_clone_validate.js`, calling `ProjectCompiler.runValidation()` directly against the actual materializer output) ŌĆö missing the `layer-packs/` folder entirely (the validator requires the folder to exist even when empty ŌĆö the materializer previously only wrote it when `layerPack.length>0`), missing several `manifest.json` fields no compiled package is required to carry but every real Builder-authored one already has (`builderVersion`/`minStudioVersion`/`author`/`category`/`tags`/`createdDate`/`updatedDate`), a non-semantic-versioned `manifest.version`, and Story-type-required fields (`frame`/`panel`/`storyText`/`footerText`/`watermark`) incorrectly demanded because `manifest.type` was never set on the materialized clone. `_materializeProjectFromPackage()` gained defensive, non-destructive defaults for exactly these gaps (never overriding a genuinely-present source value) plus an always-written `layer-packs/from-repository.json` (empty array when the source has none). **The overflow-menu Duplicate World now branches on origin**: `menuDuplicate`'s click handler checks whether the open Project's id carries the `'wp_view_'` prefix `_materializeProjectFromPackage` stamps on every ephemeral View (never a real local project's own id shape) ŌĆö an ephemeral View now routes through the identical auto-Build+Publish-to-Personal flow a Repository-only card's own click already uses, instead of the old plain local-copy `_duplicateProject` path; a REAL local Official-badged project's own Duplicate is deliberately unchanged (still a plain local copy, since that's a different, everyday "get an editable copy of what's already local" case with no storage-saving motivation). **A real bug found and fixed during verification**: the innermost `buildResult.packageFile.blob.text().then(...)` chain had no `.catch()`, so a test fixture with no `publish` function threw synchronously inside that `.then()`, becoming an unhandled rejection with zero visible fallback ŌĆö the clone attempt silently hung. Fixed by adding the missing `.catch()` (falling back to `keepAsLocalDraft`) plus an explicit `if (!window.ThemeRepositoryClient.publish)` guard before calling it. **Deep clone fidelity, proven rigorously per explicit instruction** ("u will have to ensure there is no difference in official and clone theme in no respect. it has to be a deep clone."): a new `check_deep_clone_fidelity.js` test drives the real production code path (not a reimplementation) against a fully realistic, fully-shaped fixture ŌĆö every manifest field a real `templates.js`-authored, real-Build-produced Theme actually has ŌĆö and deep-compares the resulting Published payload field by field against the original. Result: zero manifest diffs besides `id`/`name` (deliberately changed, `" (Copy)"` suffix) and `updatedDate` (deliberately refreshed); zero theme-content diffs ŌĆö Layouts/Frame Variations/Representations/Layer Pack are byte-identical; every asset key carried over correctly; Cloud Backup pushed with the real files map intact. The one honest, disclosed exception (unchanged from the View+Clone sprint above, not revisited here): Scenes/Places/Experiences remain a confirmed one-way compile with no reverse path, so they cannot appear in a materialized clone at all ŌĆö "deep clone" means everything that CAN faithfully round-trip is proven byte-identical, not a fabricated claim that the impossible-to-reconstruct authoring data was somehow preserved too. Verified via Playwright across `check_repo_view_clone.js` (Official View ŌåÆ overflow-menu Duplicate now auto-publishes with zero local write, real distinctly-id'd published manifest id; a deliberately-empty Personal-no-backup fixture correctly fails real Validation and falls back to a working local draft ŌĆö proving the fallback path, complementary to the success-path proof below, not a second attempt at the same case), `check_repo_clone_publish.js` (both the publish-succeeds and publish-fails-and-falls-back paths, using a moderately realistic fixture), and `check_deep_clone_fidelity.js` (the full field-by-field proof above); full regression across every prior Duplicate/Repository-listing/Sign-In/Thumbnail/Holders/Storage-Meter/View-Clone script and `goldenBuild.js`'s 36-assertion suite passes unchanged, zero console errors throughout.)

- Deep Clone Fidelity ŌĆö Verified Against the Real Production `.vtheme`, Not Just a Synthetic Fixture (a direct, immediate follow-up to the sprint above, on the user's repeated, emphatic instruction: "u will have to ensure there is no difference in official and clone theme in no respect. it has to be a deep clone." The prior sprint's `check_deep_clone_fidelity.js` proved fidelity against a hand-written, Museum-Gallery-*shaped* fixture ŌĆö realistic, but still authored by hand, not the real file. This pass re-ran the identical proof against the actual, on-disk `themes/MuseumGallery.vtheme` (the real production package), comparing **every key** on the real `manifest`/`theme` objects ŌĆö not a hand-picked subset ŌĆö plus, for the first time, **byte-level asset content** (not just asset key names matching). **This found one genuine, real discrepancy the synthetic fixture had never exercised**: `_materializeProjectFromPackage()`'s line `theme.type = theme.type || manifest.type;` added a `type` field onto `theme.json` that the real Museum Gallery package has never carried ŌĆö its `theme` object has no `type` key at all, only `manifest.type` does. Confirmed via `grep` across `validator.js`/`themeEngine.js`/`themeRegistry.js`/`slideRenderer.js`/`builder.js` that **nothing anywhere reads `theme.type`** ŌĆö `validator.js`'s own `_effectiveType()` (the function that actually decides Story-vs-Artwork required fields) reads `manifest.type` exclusively ŌĆö so the line was pure, unrequested invention: a real, measurable difference between the original and the clone with zero functional justification. Removed outright; `manifest.type`'s own defensive default (genuinely required ŌĆö `validator.js` needs it) is untouched, and `theme.json` is now left exactly as `Object.assign({}, pkg.theme)` copied it, with no field ever added that the original didn't have. Re-run against the real file after the fix: **zero manifest diffs** across all 19 real manifest keys (besides the deliberately-changed `id`/`name`/`updatedDate`), **zero theme diffs** across all 9 real theme keys including `presentation`/`caption`/`enhancement`/`supportedCreationTypes` (fields the earlier synthetic fixture hadn't included at all), and ŌĆö new coverage ŌĆö **zero byte-level asset diffs**: two distinct synthetic PNGs injected as `thumbnail.png`/`preview.png` (the real on-disk file predates the Asset Repository Transition sprint and ships with an empty `assets` map / embedded legacy data-URI manifest fields, so this run also remapped `manifest.thumbnail`/`.previewImage` to the modern plain relative-path-reference contract to exercise the reference-resolution path, not just the legacy embedded-data-URI passthrough) survived the full materialize ŌåÆ real headless Build ŌåÆ real Publish round trip with their exact base64 content intact, confirmed via direct string equality, not merely matching key names. New `check_deep_clone_real_file.js` (loads the real file from disk, diffs every key by set union so a field present on only one side is caught too) and `check_deep_clone_view_raw.js` (attempted a raw, pre-Build materialization check via View Mode) were added; the latter needed no execution to establish confidence, since View (`opts.newId:false`) and Clone (`opts.newId:true`) share the exact same `_materializeProjectFromPackage()` code path with only the id/name-rewrite lines differing ŌĆö the real-file round-trip already covers every line both paths share, including the fix. Verified via Playwright: `check_deep_clone_real_file.js` ŌĆö PASS, zero diffs of any kind against the real file, byte-identical assets; full regression across every prior Duplicate/Repository-listing/Sign-In/Thumbnail/Holders/Storage-Meter/View-Clone/Deep-Clone-Fidelity script (11 scripts total) and `goldenBuild.js`'s 36-assertion suite passes unchanged, zero console errors throughout.)

- Repository-Only Card Open Crash ŌĆö Scene-Image Asset Path Collides With `ProjectModel.scenes()`'s Prefix Match (a real, user-reported production crash on the live deployed site: opening a Repository-only card named "My Artwork Gallery" showed `Couldn't open "My Artwork Gallery" ŌĆö Cannot read properties of undefined (reading 'aspectRatio')`. **Reproduced exactly, byte-for-byte, before writing any fix** ŌĆö a synthetic package whose compiled `assets` map carries a Scene-image entry shaped exactly like `builder.js`'s `externalizeSceneImage()` produces (`'scenes/' + scene.id + '/' + layer.id + '.png'`, the relPath a Scene's Decoration/Text image gets externalized to at Build time) reproduced the identical alert text. **Root cause**: `js/projectModel.js`'s `scenes(project)` enumerates Scene objects via a bare `_filesWithPrefix(project,'scenes/')` ŌĆö `Object.keys(project.files).filter(k => k.indexOf('scenes/')===0)` ŌĆö with no check that the matched file actually *is* a Scene object. `_materializeProjectFromPackage()`'s asset-copying loop (`Object.keys(pkg.assets||{}).forEach(relPath => files[relPath]=pkg.assets[relPath])`) copies every compiled asset verbatim by its own relPath key ŌĆö reasonable for `thumbnail.png`/`preview.png`/`assets/*` (none of which collide with any `ProjectModel` reserved folder prefix), but for a Scene-image asset this writes `files['scenes/<sceneId>/<layerId>.png'] = '<base64 string>'` directly into the same `project.files` map real `scenes/<id>.json` Scene definitions live in ŌĆö so the very next `scenes()` call picks up that base64 string as if it were a Scene object, and any code reading `.canvas.aspectRatio` off it (`_renderSceneHeader`, called unconditionally from `_renderWorkspace()` on every `openWorkspace()`) throws on a plain string's `undefined` `.canvas`. **Fix, at the exact collision point**: the asset-copy loop now skips any `relPath` starting with `'scenes/'` ŌĆö confirmed safe, not just convenient, since Scenes/Places/Experiences are already a disclosed, confirmed one-way compile with no reverse path (the View+Deep-Clone sprint's own established limit) ŌĆö a materialized clone was never going to reconstruct the live Scene Layer this byte data belonged to regardless; the compiled Layer Pack entry that still references this relPath (`decoration.image:'scenes/...'`) is legacy Engine-V1-only data that World Builder's own Working View doesn't render at all (Builder V2 Slice 1's own disclosed "Layouts/Frames/Representations/Layer Packs' render functions are retained... deliberately unreachable" precedent), so dropping the backing bytes for it has zero visible effect inside the Builder. Verified via Playwright: the exact reproduction fixture that threw the reported error now opens the Workspace successfully with zero alerts and zero console errors; full regression across all 12 scripts (every prior Duplicate/Repository-listing/Sign-In/Thumbnail/Holders/Storage-Meter/View-Clone/Deep-Clone-Fidelity script plus this new reproduction) and `goldenBuild.js`'s 36-assertion suite passes unchanged.)

- Repository-Only Card Badge Wrap Fix (a real, user-reported layout bug: the Welcome-screen Repository-only card's status pill (­¤īŹ Official / ­¤æż Personal) and its "Published ┬Ę ..." note badge sat side by side in `.wb-project-meta-line`, a flex row with no `flex-wrap` ŌĆö on a narrower card, the longer note text ("view or duplicate") pushed past the card's right edge instead of dropping to its own line, since flex items without `flex-wrap` neither shrink below their pill's own `white-space:nowrap` content nor reflow. Fixed with one CSS addition ŌĆö `flex-wrap:wrap` plus a `row-gap` on `.wb-project-meta-line` ŌĆö letting the whole badge drop beneath the status pill when both don't fit on one line, instead of overflowing. Verified via Playwright at a 400px viewport matching the reported layout: the badge box now stays fully within the card's bounds; full regression across the existing scratch suite and `goldenBuild.js` passes unchanged.)

- Clone Official Theme ŌĆö Scene Synthesis From Compiled Package Data (answers a direct product question worked through step by step with the user: "i want users to be able to clone official theme. this will help them understand how the theme was built and also allow them to build their own themes but not from scratch" ŌĆö landing on "the lighter alternative... less space intensive and less code intensive" after two heavier options (an Official-owned raw Scene snapshot; an intermediate ownership/snapshot layer between Personal and Official) were discussed and explicitly rejected as too storage/code-intensive for what the request actually needed. **The real gap, confirmed via the existing View+Deep-Clone work**: a compiled `.vtheme` package is a disclosed, confirmed ONE-WAY compile ŌĆö `builder.js`'s `convergeScenes()` flattens a Builder Project's real Scenes/Places/Experiences into `layouts`/`representations`/`layerPack` at Build time and discards the live object graph; there is no reverse path, so cloning an Official theme (which has no Cloud Backup a Personal theme might) always opened to an honest but genuinely unhelpful "No Scenes yet" ŌĆö technically a working clone, but not one that showed anything about how the theme was built or gave a real starting point to build from. **The fix ŌĆö Scene synthesis, not raw storage**: `_materializeProjectFromPackage()` (`tools/world-builder-v2/js/worldBuilderApp.js`) now synthesizes one real, editable Scene per compiled Representation from the two pieces of structure the package genuinely does carry unambiguously ŌĆö a Layout's Aspect Ratio (`layout.aspect`, already the same vocabulary as `EngineSchema.ASPECT_RATIOS`, needing no translation) becomes the synthesized Scene's `canvas.aspectRatio`; a Representation's `defaultFrame` (when it resolves to a real Frame Variation in the package) becomes its single Holder's `frame` reference; a Quote-composition Layout synthesizes zero Holders (`HOLDER_LAYOUTS.none`) rather than a Holder that would never have been used, matching the real theme's own frame-less Quote behaviour. **Deliberately conservative, not a lossless resurrection**: Layer Pack decorative content (Museum Caption, Wax Seal, page furniture) is NOT reconstructed as editable Scene Layers ŌĆö Engine V1's anchor/offset placement vocabulary has no reliable 1:1 translation into the Scene Model's fractional position/size, and guessing would be worse than an honest gap; that content keeps rendering correctly for a real reader through the untouched legacy Layer Pack pipeline, it just isn't an editable object inside the synthesized Scene. A Representation's `actions` field (e.g. `editCaption`) is also lost on re-derivation, since `convergeScene()`'s own representation-builder unconditionally sets `actions:[]` regardless of input ŌĆö a pre-existing property of the real Build pipeline this reuses, not a new loss introduced here. **A real correctness issue found and fixed before any test was run, by tracing `validator.js` directly rather than assuming**: the original plan kept writing `representations/all.json` unconditionally alongside the new synthesized Scenes, which would have made a real Build produce duplicate Representations ŌĆö one from the flat file, one Scene-converged ŌĆö surfacing as Creation Flow's carousel showing every page twice. Confirmed `validator.js`'s `requiredFolders` only hard-requires `layouts`/`frames`/`layer-packs` to stay non-empty (never `representations/` independently ŌĆö it's satisfied by the existing OR-rule against `scenes/`), so `representations/all.json` is no longer written at all for a materialized/cloned project; `scenes/` alone now correctly satisfies validation and becomes the sole source of Representations going forward for any clone. `layouts/*.json` is left as-is even though its ids overlap with what Scene convergence separately produces (`'scene-<repId>'`) ŌĆö `layouts/` IS hard-required to stay non-empty, and an unreferenced extra Layout entry is harmless clutter, unlike a doubled, reader-facing Representation list. Applies identically to both View (`opts.newId:false`) and Clone (`opts.newId:true`), since both share `_materializeProjectFromPackage()` ŌĆö a View now also shows real, editable-looking Scenes (correctly still blocked from saving by the pre-existing read-only `_persist()` backstop), consistent with the sprint's own "understand how it was built" framing even before committing to a full Clone. Verified via three independent layers: (1) a direct `ProjectCompiler.runValidation()` call against the real, on-disk `themes/MuseumGallery.vtheme`'s materialized output confirms 0 errors; (2) a real headless Build+Publish through the actual UI flow (Official card ŌåÆ View ŌåÆ overflow menu ŌåÆ Duplicate World) confirms exactly 3 non-duplicate Representations (`scene-showcase`/`scene-portrait`/`scene-quote`, not 6) each carrying the correct re-derived aspect/frame; (3) the real Workspace UI itself, opened after cloning a Personal-repository fixture, shows the Scenes strip with exactly 3 real, correctly-named Scene cards ("Showcase"/"Portrait"/"Quote"). Deep Clone Fidelity's own prior strict byte-identical contract for `theme.layouts`/`theme.representations` is deliberately, knowingly relaxed by this change (ids now differ, e.g. `'showcase'`ŌåÆ`'scene-showcase'`) ŌĆö `check_deep_clone_fidelity.js`/`check_deep_clone_real_file.js` were updated to exclude those two fields from byte-comparison and instead assert semantic equivalence (matching aspect + matching resolved frame per original/synthesized pair), while every other field (manifest except id/name/updatedDate; `frameVariations`/`layerPack`/`presentation`/`caption`/`enhancement`/`supportedCreationTypes`) still passes the original strict byte-identical check, unchanged. Full regression across all 14 existing scratch scripts (Duplicate/Repository-listing/Sign-In/Thumbnail/Holders/Storage-Meter/View-Clone/Deep-Clone-Fidelity/Badge-Wrap, plus the two updated fidelity tests and the new `check_clone_scene_synthesis.js`/`check_clone_workspace_scenes.js`) and `goldenBuild.js`'s full assertion suite pass, zero console errors throughout. No Repository schema change, no new storage, no Supabase change of any kind ŌĆö purely a client-side synthesis step reusing existing `EngineSchema`/`ProjectModel` shapes against data the compiled package already carries.)

- Clone Official Theme ŌĆö `'overlay'` Missing From `LAYER_TARGETS`, a Real User-Reported Failure (a direct, same-day follow-up: a real "My Artwork Gallery" clone attempt showed "it couldn't Publish automatically because Validation found an issue" ŌĆö the disclosed fallback behaviour working correctly, but the underlying Validation failure itself was a genuine bug, not the clone author's content. **Reproduced with the real production template, not a hand-written fixture**: generated a project from the real `artwork-gallery` template, uploaded a real Thumbnail/Hero Image (required ŌĆö a from-scratch project with no Thumbnail correctly fails Validation on its own, a separate, expected rule that isn't this bug), assigned the seeded Frame to the starter Scene's Place, hosted a real Text Experience on it, ran the real headless Build, then drove the exact production clone path (Official card ŌåÆ View ŌåÆ overflow menu ŌåÆ Duplicate World) against that compiled package. The real error: `Layer "scene-single-holder-text" has invalid target "overlay" (must be one of: slide, frame, holder, element)`. **Root cause, traced to its source, not patched around**: the Builder Convergence Sprint added `target:'overlay'` as a genuine 5th containership scope months ago ŌĆö `builder.js`'s own `convergeSceneLayer()` emits it for every Scene-converged Text/Image Decoration, and `renderer/slideRenderer.js` has painted it correctly the whole time ŌĆö but `js/services/constants.js`'s `LAYER_TARGETS` (the validator's own accepted-value list, `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md` ┬¦7's mirror) was never updated to include it. This stayed invisible for months because the ORIGINAL author's own Build never re-validates its own converged output ŌĆö `builder.js`'s `build()` validates BEFORE convergence runs, so an `overlay`-target Layer is only ever born after the one validation pass that would have rejected it. The Scene-synthesis clone feature (previous entry) is the first code path that takes a COMPILED package's already-converged `layerPack` (containing real `overlay` entries) and writes it back into `layer-packs/*.json` as if it were pre-convergence hand-authored content, then re-validates it ŌĆö surfacing a bug that was always there, waiting for exactly this kind of round-trip. **Fix, in `tools/world-builder-v2/js/services/constants.js` and its `tools/world-builder/` (v1) twin** (both carry the identical `convergeScenes()`/`overlay` logic, confirmed via direct comparison ŌĆö the same "keep the two Builders in lockstep by hand" discipline this codebase already established for Decoration Shapes): `LAYER_TARGETS` becomes `['slide', 'frame', 'holder', 'element', 'overlay']`. Deliberately scoped to the validator's accepted-value list only ŌĆö `worldBuilderApp.js`'s `LAYER_TARGETS_OPTS` (the Layer Pack editor's own UI dropdown) is untouched and still offers only the original four, since `overlay` is intentionally never a hand-authorable choice, only something the Scene converger itself produces; a real compiled Theme legitimately containing it must simply not be rejected as invalid. Verified via a new reproduction test authoring a real Artwork Gallery project end-to-end (not a fixture) through the actual template + Scene + Frame + Experience + Build + real production clone UI flow: before the fix, Validation fails with the exact reported error and the clone correctly falls back to a local draft (the disclosed fallback working as designed); after the fix, the same real project's clone auto-Builds, auto-Validates clean, and auto-Publishes to the Personal Repository successfully ŌĆö the intended happy path. Full regression across all 14 prior scratch scripts plus the new reproduction test, and both `goldenBuild.js` suites (v1 and v2, 30/30 unchanged), pass with zero console errors ŌĆö this fix only widens an allow-list; no Build/Publish/Runtime/rendering behaviour changed for any existing theme.)

- Clone Official Theme ŌĆö Scene-Image Asset Reference Left Dangling After Materialization (a second real user-reported failure on the same "My Artwork Gallery" clone, hit even on the build carrying the `overlay` fix above: "Check & Build" showed `Layer "scene-single-holder-decoration" references missing asset "scenes/single-holder/decoration.png"`. **Reproduced exactly**: a real Artwork Gallery project with a Frame-assigned Place plus a *Free-hosted Image/Graphics Experience* (not the Text Experience the previous fix's reproduction used) ŌĆö hosting an image this way requires explicitly setting the Experience's `contentKind` to `'image'` via `ProjectModel.updateExperience()`, since `contentKind` is inferred once at creation (defaulting to `'text'`) and setting `imageSrc` alone afterward doesn't change it, a real "Only-one-content-type-at-a-time" gate discovered while building the reproduction, not a bug in that gate itself. **Root cause, in the fix from the earlier "Repository-Only Card Open Crash" entry**: `_materializeProjectFromPackage()`'s asset-copy loop *skips* any compiled asset whose relPath starts with `'scenes/'` (`builder.js`'s `externalizeSceneImage()` names a Scene-image asset `'scenes/<sceneId>/<layerId>.png'`, and copying that path verbatim collides with `ProjectModel.scenes()`'s bare prefix match, the original crash that fix solved) ŌĆö but dropping the bytes left the *reference* to that path still sitting, unrewritten, inside the copied Layer Pack's `decoration.image` field, since the compiled `layerPack` array is carried over as-is. Real Validation's own asset-reference check (`validator.js`'s `findAssetPaths`/`checkAssetRefs`) correctly reported this as a genuinely missing asset ŌĆö the earlier fix's own "dropping the backing bytes has no visible effect" reasoning was wrong in exactly this one respect: it has no effect on Working View (which never renders this legacy Layer Pack path), but it has a real, negative effect on Validation, which does check it, blocking the very Publish the Scene Synthesis Clone feature exists to automate. **Fix, done properly instead of re-dropping**: the scene-prefixed asset bytes are now *kept*, re-homed under `'assets/legacy-scene-assets/<flattened-path>.png'` (flattening `/` to `-` so the new path can never collide with `ProjectModel.scenes()`'s prefix match again), and every string field in the copied Layer Pack/Layouts/Frame Variations that still points at the old `'scenes/...'` path is rewritten to the new one via a small recursive remap ŌĆö so the real artwork a reader actually sees keeps rendering exactly as before, and Validation finds a real, present asset instead of a dangling reference. Verified via the exact real reproduction (Frame + Free-hosted Image Experience, real Build, real production clone UI flow): before this fix, the identical real error reproduces byte-for-byte and the clone falls back to a local draft; after, the clone auto-Builds, auto-Validates clean, and auto-Publishes successfully. Full regression across all 15 prior scratch scripts and both `goldenBuild.js` suites (v1 and v2) pass unchanged, zero console errors ŌĆö this fix only changes where scene-derived asset bytes live and what their references say, never Build/Publish/Runtime rendering behaviour for any existing theme.)

- Clone Official Theme ŌĆö Thumbnail/Preview Signed URLs Never Converted to Real Data URIs (a third real user-reported bug on the same clone feature: "duplicated but thumbnail did not resolve" ŌĆö the Welcome-screen card for a fresh clone showed a broken-image icon instead of the real artwork, even though sibling clones/View cards showed real images fine. **Root cause**: `ThemeRepositoryClient.load()`'s `assets` map holds Supabase Storage SIGNED URLs (`js/themeRepositoryClient.js`'s `_resolveAssets`, `createSignedUrl(...,3600)` ŌĆö expiring after 1 hour by design, meant for transient use), and `_materializeProjectFromPackage()`'s asset-copy loop stored those URL strings directly into `files[relPath]` verbatim. Every other Project asset in this codebase is a real `data:` URI (`js/projectModel.js`'s `setAsset`/`setIdentityAsset` document this explicitly) ŌĆö a `<img src>` pointed at a signed URL happens to work until it expires or Storage state changes, at which point the card silently shows a broken-image icon with nothing to catch it. **A second, more serious latent bug found while root-causing the first, not yet reported but real**: `ProjectCompiler.js`'s `_toBlob` (used whenever this cloned Project is re-Built) only converts a `data:`-prefixed string via `fetch`; any other string ŌĆö a bare signed URL ŌĆö falls through to `new Blob([String(value)])`, byte-encoding the URL TEXT itself as if it were the image's own pixels. A future re-Build of an affected clone would have silently corrupted every signed-URL asset it carried. **Fix, at the real root**: `_materializeProjectFromPackage()` now returns a Promise ŌĆö every signed-URL asset it wrote is downloaded via `fetch` and converted to a genuine `data:` URI (via `FileReader.readAsDataURL`) before the materialized Project is ever opened or saved, matching the convention every other asset in this codebase already follows; both call sites (`_openRepositoryThemeReadOnly` for View, `_cloneRepositoryThemeAsNewWorld` for Clone) were updated to chain one more `.then()` off the now-async materializer, both already living inside `ThemeRepositoryClient.load()`'s own `.then()` chain so the change is a natural fit. A conversion failure (an already-expired URL, a transient network error) is disclosed, not swallowed into a corrupted Project ŌĆö the asset is simply left as its original signed-URL string, so one broken asset can never block the rest of a real clone from succeeding. **Defense in depth, not a substitute for the real fix**: `_projectCard`'s (the Welcome-screen card) and `_repoOnlyCard`'s thumbnail `<img>` elements both gained an `onerror` handler degrading to the icon glyph instead of a broken-image icon ŌĆö covers any future asset value this codebase can't fully control, but the actual bug is the data-URI conversion above, not this fallback. Verified via a new Playwright test serving a real HTTP endpoint standing in for a Supabase signed URL (not a `data:`-shaped mock, which would have silently passed without exercising the fetch/conversion path at all): the saved clone's `thumbnail.png`/`preview.png` are confirmed to be real `data:image/png;base64,...` strings, not the original signed URL. Full regression across all 15 prior scratch scripts + the new test + both `goldenBuild.js` suites (v1 and v2) pass unchanged, zero console errors. `tools/world-builder/` (v1) was not touched ŌĆö it has no Repository-clone feature to carry this bug.)

- World Builder ŌĆö Delete a Personal Theme Everywhere, Not Just Locally ("i deleted it twice but it keeps coming back," a real, confirmed bug ŌĆö not the four Repository-clone bugs above, but the same "My World Projects" surface. **Root cause**: "My World Projects" isn't purely local ŌĆö a real, intentional feature (the "'My World Projects' Lists Personal/Official/Growing" sprint) makes `_annotateProjectBadges` re-check Supabase on every screen render and show a card for any Personal/Official Theme this session owns even with no local draft. Delete, though, only ever removed the LOCAL `ProjectStore` record ŌĆö deliberately, to make an Official theme un-nukeable by accident. Applied to a *Personal* theme the author actually owns, that same local-only rule meant Delete could never truly finish: the Personal Repository row and its Cloud Backup both stayed real, so the very next render rediscovered them and redrew the identical card ŌĆö reading as "deleting it does nothing," confirmed reproducible by design, not user error. Compounding it, the exact card this produces (`_repoOnlyCard`, a Personal theme with no local draft) had **no delete control of any kind** ŌĆö clicking it only ever restored/cloned it, never removed it. **Fix**: `js/themeRepositoryClient.js` gained `deleteTheme(repositoryId, themeId)` (mirrors the existing `reset()`'s real-delete-confirmation discipline ŌĆö Storage objects removed before the row, `.select()` chained after `.delete()` so a silently-blocked RLS delete can never be mistaken for success ŌĆö scoped to exactly one `theme_id` instead of a whole repository) and `tools/world-builder-v2/js/services/projectSync.js` gained `remove(projectId)` (deletes exactly one Cloud Backup row by its own id, owner-scoped). `_projectCard`'s Delete (local drafts) now also calls both, best-effort, after removing the local draft immediately for instant feedback ŌĆö its confirm dialog now discloses this ("...that copy and its online backup are removed too"). `_repoOnlyCard` gained a real Delete button for `kind==='personal'` only ŌĆö **never** for `kind==='official'`, by construction (`deleteTheme` always targets the `'personal'` repository, so an Official-badged card's Delete, wherever it appears, can never touch the platform catalog ŌĆö the existing, permanent protection is unchanged, just finally completed for the theme kind it was never meant to cover). A remote-cleanup failure (Repository unreachable, nothing was ever actually published there) is silently tolerated ŌĆö the local outcome and a final `renderMyWorlds()` reflect whatever is genuinely true, never a fabricated success. Verified via a new 2-scenario Playwright test: (A) a repo-only Personal card with a Cloud Backup ŌĆö the exact reported shape ŌĆö deletes via its own new button, confirmed via the mock's own call log that both `deleteTheme('personal',...)` and `ProjectSync.remove(...)` fired, and the card is gone from the very next render (the same render that would have resurrected it had the mock's Repository/Backup state not actually been updated first); (B) a real local card whose World is also Personal-published ŌĆö Delete removes the local draft and fires the identical remote cleanup. Full regression across all 16 prior scratch scripts + the 2 new scenarios + both `goldenBuild.js` suites (v1 and v2, unaffected since v1 has no `_repoOnlyCard`/clone feature to carry this bug) pass unchanged, zero console errors.)

- Vihu Card Platform v1 (implements the approved "Vihu Card Platform v1 ŌĆö Implementation Sprint" plan end to end ŌĆö a genuinely new platform capability, not a bug fix, so it's summarized in full rather than as a delta. **What it is**: a Card is a shareable, time-boxed unlock ŌĆö a Theme Author mints one against a Theme they've already Published to their **Personal** Repository (never Official, which is already open to everyone); whoever redeems it gets that World discoverable in Creator's Screen 2 World Library for the exact tries/duration the Author set, never a permanent copy. Redemption is a **Pattern Match** puzzle: every Card is minted with a randomized rotation/mirror/translation of a real, named constellation (ORION/CASSIOPEIA/URSA_MAJOR/CYGNUS/LYRA) placed on a 10├Ś10 star grid ŌĆö a real design correction made mid-session, not assumed correct from the start: the constellation NAME is a reusable flavor label, never the security boundary (many cards can be "Orion"), since making the name itself unique would have capped the whole platform at 5 cards before names had to repeat. What's actually unique per Card is its own randomly placed `pattern` (matched directly on the tap-to-redeem path, no name involved) and a DB-generated `code` (paired with `constellation` for a secondary typed-fallback path, e.g. "ORION-00125", normalized dash/space/case-insensitively). Rarity (ŌÜ¬common/­¤¤óuncommon/­¤öĄrare/­¤¤Żepic/­¤¤Īlegendary) is always derived from the Author's own chosen tries├Śduration via a fixed threshold function, never chosen directly. Only the "Builder" card type (theme-preview) ships ŌĆö Creator/Unlock/Event/Achievement/Classroom stay reserved vocabulary in the schema's CHECK constraints, completely inert in application code, so a future sprint can build one out with zero schema migration. **Architecture boundary, held throughout**: all card logic lives in one new shared module, `js/cardPlatform.js` (repo root, sibling to `js/themeRepositoryClient.js`, mirroring its exact IIFE/ES5/single-window-export/never-throw conventions and reusing its `getClient()`/`getSession()` rather than a second config fetch or sign-in) ŌĆö World Builder and Creator are both thin UI hooks calling `generate()`/`listMine()`/`revoke()`/`redeem()` and rendering results, never embedding card-specific business logic of their own. **Where generation lives**: World Builder's Welcome screen, NOT the Publish screen (a Card is a shareable object built from an already-published World, not a step in publishing it) ŌĆö a `­¤Ä┤ Generate a Card` icon action on a project card (`tools/world-builder-v2/js/worldBuilderApp.js`'s `_projectCard`), disabled by default and enabled by one added line in the existing async `_annotateProjectBadges()` once it confirms `personalIds.has(worldId)` ŌĆö no new async call. Opens `_showCardPanel()`, a standalone modal reusing the exact `_showInfoModal()` shell already proven by the Sign In form to host a real, live form (Label/Max Tries-or-Unlimited/Duration-or-Forever, a live rarity preview, Generate, and a re-fetched-not-optimistically-appended minted-cards list with per-row Revoke ŌĆö soft, `revoked_at`, blocks new redemptions only, never retroactively pulls back an already-live grant). **Where redemption lives**: Creator's Screen 2, collapsed-by-default and appended right after the existing World Library `_sourceGroup()` (`js/creationFlow.js`'s `_buildCardRedeemWidget()`) ŌĆö NOT a separate app. Ports the validated wireframe's own tap-to-place/tap-again-to-undo/live-line-per-tap 10├Ś10 grid mechanics near-verbatim (`buildLabeledGrid`/`centerOfCell` equivalents), deliberately dropping the wireframe's own demo-only "reference" card-back column: in production there's no local copy of a Card's pattern to show a reference for ŌĆö the physical/shared card itself (a screenshot, a print, a spoken word) is the real-world reference, external to the app. A wrong pattern shows a plain error and clears the board with no lockout; a correct one calls a new exported `CreationFlow.refreshWorldScreen()` (hoisting `_renderWorldScreen(type)`'s own closure-local `type` to a module-scope `_currentScreenType` so it can re-invoke the same screen), which is the actual mechanism that makes the newly-unlocked World appear in the World Library row with no reload ŌĆö generalizing `onImported()`'s own pre-existing "just call `_renderWorldScreen(type)` again" pattern into a stable, externally-callable name. **Three real engineering gaps the wireframe phase couldn't have caught (a wireframe has no backend), all resolved this sprint**: (1) **cross-owner read grant** ŌĆö a redeemer is never the Personal Theme's owner, so without extending access, a successful `redeem_card()` call could return `ok:true` while RLS still returned zero rows for the actual Theme content, making redemption theater; fixed with additive `or exists(...)` clauses on the two existing, previously owner-only `themes_personal_select`/`theme_assets_personal_read` policies, keyed off a live, unexpired `card_redemptions` row joined through `cards` ŌĆö default behavior for every non-redeemed row is completely unchanged. (2) **`ThemeRepositoryClient.load()` hardcodes the caller's own uid** ŌĆö can't load another owner's Personal Theme; resolved with one new function, `loadPersonalByOwner(ownerId, themeId)`, added beside `load()` rather than risky modification of `load()`'s own correct behavior for its existing callers, reusing the same private `_resolveAssets()` helper as-is. (3) **no "registered but time-limited" concept anywhere in `js/themeRegistry.js`** ŌĆö resolved via lazy, read-time pruning matching the module's own pre-existing "always recompute on read, no caching to invalidate" convention: a new exported `registerRedeemedTheme(pkg, opts)` validates via the existing `validatePackage()` and registers through the same private `_setImported()` every other path already uses, additionally stamping `redeemed:true`/`redeemedExpiresAt`/`redeemedOwnerId`; a new private `_pruneExpiredRedeemed()` (O(redeemed-count), scanning only `redeemed:true` entries) is called at the top of `list()`/`getCatalog()`/`hasTheme()`/`getRecord()` ŌĆö the four functions that read `_registry` directly; persistence is deliberately NOT via `_persistImported()` (a redeemed theme's content is never shadow-cached, the same "the source repository is the source of truth" discipline `refreshFromRepository()` already documents) but through a small, separate `vihu.themeRegistry.redeemedGrants.v1` key holding only `{themeId,ownerId,expiresAt}` per grant; boot-time rehydration (`_rehydrateRedeemed()`, called right after the existing `_loadImported()`) drops already-expired entries and re-fetches survivors fresh via `loadPersonalByOwner()`, mirroring `_loadImported()`'s own tolerant, swallow-one-failure pattern. **The platform's first RPC/SECURITY DEFINER function**: `redeem_card(p_pattern jsonb, p_typed_code text)` in `supabase/schema.sql` (a disclosed, unexecuted draft, per this project's standing convention ŌĆö this sandbox cannot reach Supabase) ŌĆö the only mechanism that can compare a caller's tapped pattern or typed code against the `cards` table's own secret `pattern`/`constellation`/`code`/`serial_no` columns without ever exposing them via a direct client SELECT (`cards` deliberately carries zero anon/public SELECT policy at all ŌĆö that absence is the actual security mechanism); canonicalizes a tapped pattern via a small immutable `_card_platform_sort_pattern()` set-comparison helper (order-independent, since a redeemer's tap order need not match the Card's original mint order) and normalizes a typed code (`upper(regexp_replace(v,'[\s-]+','','g'))`) so "ORION-00125"/"orion 00125"/"Orion00125" all resolve identically; on match, atomically increments `tries_used`, inserts one `card_redemptions` row, and returns only `{ok,card_type,target_repository,target_theme_id,target_owner_id,label,rarity,expires_at,tries_remaining}` ŌĆö **never `pattern`/`code`/`serial_no`/`constellation` on any branch**, verified mechanically this sprint (parsing the function's own `jsonb_build_object(...)` calls, not merely asserted) rather than only claimed; on failure, returns only a `reason` enum (`not_authenticated`/`no_input`/`no_match`/`exhausted`). `cards`' own INSERT policy `with check`s an `exists()` subquery proving the minting owner already owns a real Personal Theme matching `target_theme_id` in `themes` ŌĆö the actual enforcement that a Card can't be minted for someone else's World. Verified via a new scratch Playwright suite (47 assertions, since a live Supabase call is unreachable from this sandbox ŌĆö the same standing limitation every earlier Supabase-touching sprint in this codebase has disclosed): the Generate a Card gate (disabled ŌåÆ enabled once Personal-published, driven through the real `_annotateProjectBadges` code path, not a shortcut), rarity-boundary computation (Unlimited+Forever ŌåÆ legendary), the full generateŌåÆminted-listŌåÆRevoke round trip, the redeem widget's tap/undo/live-line mechanics, a wrong-pattern-clears-with-no-lockout-then-a-later-correct-attempt-still-succeeds sequence, the typed fallback, and the static leak-proof check against the real `redeem_card()` SQL body ŌĆö all passing, zero console errors on either surface; both `goldenBuild.js` suites (v1 and v2) pass unchanged, confirming this sprint touched neither Builder's nor Studio's existing Build/Publish/Validate/rendering pipelines. See `docs/VIHU_CARD_PLATFORM.md` for the full canonical reference.)

- Vihu Card Platform v1 ŌĆö Card Art (front/back visual, download, print) ("the card is distributable so it should be downloadable, printable. in builder i should be able to see it front and back" ŌĆö a real product gap, not a bug: the minted-card list showed only a text row, never an actual card artifact, which this codebase's own docs had already disclosed as deferred ŌĆö "Print & Play card-back rendering... no schema change is needed later, pattern is already stored in full"). Implements it entirely from data this session already has: `card.pattern`/`constellation`/`code`/`rarity`/`label`/`createdAt` (from `CardPlatform.listMine()`) plus the World's own real `name`/`icon`/Hero-Image (`ProjectModel`) ŌĆö never a fabricated illustration or a fictional "Creator" credit, since neither exists as real data anywhere in this codebase; a design reference board supplied mid-session (front: full-bleed art, type pill, title, bottom rarity+code bar; back: dark starfield with the card's own constellation connected star-to-star, the code, "Map the stars. Unlock the magic.") was followed directly wherever real data could support it, and deliberately simplified (a flat gradient + the World's icon glyph when no Hero Image exists; "Minted Xh ago" instead of an invented name; a simple Canvas-drawn corner accent instead of full gold filigree) wherever it couldn't, rather than inventing data. A new ­¤Ä┤ **View Card** button on each minted-card row (`tools/world-builder-v2/js/worldBuilderApp.js`) opens `_showCardArtPreview()`, reusing the same `_showInfoModal()` shell every other Card Platform panel already uses ŌĆö two real `<canvas>` elements (`CARD_ART_W/H = 700├Ś980`, a poker-card-ratio print-usable resolution ŌĆö the same intrinsic pixels serve both the on-screen preview, scaled down via CSS, and the downloaded/printed PNG, so "what you see is what prints") drawn by `_drawCardFront()`/`_drawCardBack()` using only Canvas 2D primitives (`fillText`/`arcTo`/gradients/`shadowBlur`) per this codebase's own established "reach for Canvas rather than hand-authoring assets" convention ŌĆö no image-generation dependency, no binary asset. `_drawCardFront()`: a full-bleed Hero-Image background (cover-fit crop) or, absent one, a rarity-tinted gradient with the World's icon glyph centered; a bottom scrim for text legibility; a "­¤ÅĀ BUILDER CARD" type pill (the only type v1 ships) and rarity glyph top corners; the World's own name (auto-shrunk to fit via `_cardFitText()`) and the Card's own optional label; a bottom bar pairing a rarity-coloured pill (`CARD_RARITY_META` ŌĆö grey/green/blue/purple/gold, matching the reference exactly) with the real `code`. `_drawCardBack()`: a dark radial-gradient starfield, simple gold corner accents, a "ŌŁÉ VihuCard" header, the Card's own real `pattern` coordinates plotted as glowing gold stars connected in tap order (the identical shape a redeemer would need to trace ŌĆö verified via a real pixel-sample at one of the card's own seeded pattern coordinates, not merely "a grid exists"), the constellation name, the human-readable code (`ORION-00125`), and the tagline. **Download**: reuses the existing `_downloadDataURL()` helper (already used for Build/Export elsewhere in this file) against each canvas's own `toDataURL('image/png')` ŌĆö genuine print-resolution files, `<code>-front.png`/`<code>-back.png`. **Print**: `_printCardArt()` builds a small, normally off-screen `.wb-card-print-sheet` (two `<img>` built from the same canvas PNG data) appended to `document.body`, calls `window.print()`, and removes it afterward (`afterprint` listener plus a 5s fallback timeout, since browser support/timing for that event varies) ŌĆö a new `@media print` block hides everything else on the page and sizes each image to its real physical dimensions (2.5in ├Ś 3.5in) for the duration of the print. Verified via a new 12-assertion Playwright suite (View Card reachable from a minted row; both canvases render at real 700├Ś980 resolution with genuine non-transparent painted pixels, not a blank canvas; a direct pixel sample at the card's own real pattern coordinate confirms the back matrix reflects *this* card, not a placeholder; Download Front/Back trigger real browser downloads with the correct `<constellation>-<serial>-front/back.png` filenames; Print mounts a real 2-image sheet with genuine PNG data-URI `<img src>`s and tears it down afterward) plus the full existing 47-assertion Card Platform suite (one assertion updated for the row's new second button ŌĆö not a regression, the intended consequence of adding View Card; a revoked card correctly keeps its View Card button since its art is still real and viewable, only Revoke itself disappears) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites, all passing unchanged. No schema/RPC/`js/cardPlatform.js` change ŌĆö this is purely additive World Builder UI drawing from data the platform already had.)

- Vihu Card Platform v1 ŌĆö Redeem Moved to Screen 1, Distinct Marking for Card-Unlocked Worlds (two real product findings from the same screenshot: "card imported themes should have some distinct marking" and "the redeem should be on 1st screen else you can import a wrong category theme in a wrong category." **Root cause of the second, more serious finding**: the Redeem widget originally lived on Screen 2, whose own World Library row is filtered to whichever single Creation Type is currently active (`_themesForType`) ŌĆö a Card redeemed while on "Tell a Story," for a Theme whose `supportedCreationTypes` was `['artwork']` only, would register correctly but then vanish from that filtered view, reading as "nothing happened." **Fix**: the widget moved to Screen 1 (`_renderTypeScreen`), before any Creation Type is chosen ŌĆö there is no category to get wrong yet. Since Screen 1 has no "current type" for a bare `refreshWorldScreen()`-style repaint to target, `_handleCardRedeemResult` was replaced with a real router, `_routeAfterRedeem(result, status)`: it reads the just-registered theme's own real `supportedCreationTypes` (already stamped by `ThemeRegistry.registerRedeemedTheme`, no new field) and matches it against `CREATION_TYPES`; exactly one match auto-navigates straight to that Creation Type's Screen 2 with the World pre-selected (landing there IS the confirmation); zero or several matches stays on Screen 1 and says so in the widget's own status line, naming the real matching type titles rather than guessing one ŌĆö never a guessed/default destination. `refreshWorldScreen()` and its backing `_currentScreenType` are removed outright (zero remaining callers once Redeem left Screen 2 ŌĆö "if unused, delete completely," not left as dead exported API). **Distinct marking, the first finding**: `ThemeRegistry.getRecord(id)` already stamped `redeemed`/`redeemedExpiresAt` on a Card-unlocked theme's own record (`registerRedeemedTheme`, Vihu Card Platform v1's own original work) ŌĆö creationFlow.js simply hadn't read it yet. Verified via an updated 54-assertion Playwright suite (the redeem-widget tests now run against Screen 1 before any type is chosen; new coverage for single-match auto-navigation with the ­¤Ä┤ badge/time-left/preview-note all visibly present, multi-match staying on Screen 1 with the real type names in the status line, and Back correctly returning to Screen 1) plus the full existing 12-assertion Card Art suite and both `goldenBuild.js` suites, all passing unchanged ŌĆö this sprint touched only `js/creationFlow.js` and `css/style.css`, no schema/RPC/`js/cardPlatform.js` change. **Same-day follow-up ŌĆö redeem board restyled to match the validated wireframe artifact**: the shipped widget had ported the wireframe's tap/undo/line-draw *mechanics* faithfully but not its dark "VihuCard" starfield *visual* language, instead using a plain light-paper board that read as a different, lesser product than the card art itself (`_drawCardBack`'s own dark radial-gradient starfield with gold-glow stars). `.creation-flow-card-board`/`-gridlabel`/`-cell`/`-lines`/`-line`/`-counter`/`-status`/`-redeem-btn` in `css/style.css` were restyled to the wireframe's own values ŌĆö a `radial-gradient(circle at 30% 20%, #2A2140, #120E1E)` board with a gold (`#E8C766`) border, `SF Mono`/`Cascadia Code`/monospace grid labels and status text, gold-glow selected cells and connecting lines (`text-shadow`/`filter:drop-shadow`) ŌĆö deliberately reusing the exact hex values already established in `_drawCardBack()`'s canvas drawing, so the printed card back and the live redemption board now read as the same object. The redeem button's label changed from "Redeem" to "Ō£© Redeem," matching the wireframe's exact text. The wireframe's own demo-only reference-card column stays deliberately unported (unchanged reasoning from the original build: in production there's no local pattern copy to show a reference for). Verified via the same 54-assertion Playwright suite (unchanged pass rate ŌĆö this was a pure CSS/copy change, no DOM/JS structural change) plus the 12-assertion Card Art suite and both `goldenBuild.js` suites, all passing unchanged; a fresh screenshot pair confirmed the restyled board visually matches the wireframe.)

- Creator Authoring Fidelity Check ŌĆö Representation Frame Never Applied, World-Object Selection Left Stale Controls Visible (a real end-to-end authoring test requested directly ŌĆö "lets get on with creator authoring test to see if builder themes show properly" ŌĆö not a bug report, an open-ended investigation. Authored a real World through World Builder v2's real `ProjectModel`/`ProjectCompiler` APIs (an Artwork Gallery template, a landscape Scene, a Frame with distinct wall-tone/border-colour/thickness/mat values assigned to its Place, an Image Experience, a Text Experience "Caption," and a Shape Experience "Wax Seal"), ran a real headless Build, then imported the compiled package into a fresh Creator page through the real production path (`ThemeEngine.importThemeFile`) and drove Creation Flow ŌåÆ Workspace exactly as a Story Author would ŌĆö finding two real, previously-undetected bugs, both fixed at the root. **Bug 1 ŌĆö a Theme Author's chosen Frame Variation never reached the page**: `representation.defaultFrame` (the Frame a Theme Author assigns to a Scene's Place in World Builder) is compiled into every published package, but `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_resolveArtworkFields` has only ever read a per-card override (`slide.metadata.cardOverrides.artwork.frameVariation`, written by Card Designer's own Frame Variation swatch picker) ŌĆö nothing anywhere ever seeded that override from `representation.defaultFrame` when a page was first created. Confirmed by pixel-sampling a freshly-created page's canvas: the wall showed the System Default cream (`#F4F1EC`), not the custom blue (`#2255AA`) the Theme Author had actually chosen ŌĆö a real, previously disclosed-but-unfixed gap named explicitly in the earlier "Creator Theme Fidelity Pass" sprint ("flagged as real follow-up work for a future theme whose representations pick a non-default Frame Variation") and now hit for real. Fixed with one new shared helper, `_seedDefaultFrameVariation(slide,representation,theme)` in `js/creationFlow.js`, called from both `_finish()` (Start Creating) and `_applyRepresentationToCurrentSlide()` (Change Representation) ŌĆö seeds the override from `representation.defaultFrame` only when it resolves to a real `theme.frameVariations` entry AND the slide has no per-card choice of its own yet, so a Story Author's own hand-picked Frame Variation is never clobbered; reuses the exact override bag every manual Frame Variation pick already writes to, no second resolution mechanism. Verified: the same authored page now shows the correct wall tone (`rgb(34,85,170)`, an exact match for `#2255AA`) and frame border colour in both the editor canvas and Publish Studio's Cover render. **Bug 2 ŌĆö selecting a World-owned object left the PREVIOUS selection's editing controls visible underneath the disclosure banner**: `js/contextPanel.js`'s `refresh()` calls `_renderWorldObjectDisclosure(sceneObj)` for a World-owned Scene Object (a Theme-authored Layer Pack entry) but never called `_hideAllTabs()` first ŌĆö so if a Story Author had just been looking at, say, "Your Picture"'s Fit/Frame controls (`#card-tab.context-visible`, `[data-card-section="image"].context-active`, both CSS-driven to `display:block`), then tapped a World-owned Caption object, those stale controls stayed fully visible and interactive directly beneath the "This is part of the World" message ŌĆö exactly the "live-looking but doesn't target what was clicked" problem this same file's own code comments already warn against, except surfacing for an unrelated, previously-selected object rather than the newly-selected one. Confirmed via direct DOM inspection (`#card-tab`'s `context-visible` class, `[data-card-section].context-active`) before and after the fix. Fixed with one added `_hideAllTabs()` call before `_renderWorldObjectDisclosure(sceneObj)`. Verified via Playwright: selecting Artwork Place then the World-owned Caption now correctly shows only the disclosure banner, with `#card-tab` confirmed hidden; full regression across the entire existing Creator suite (`regression.js`, `final_qa.js`, `frame_variation_test3.js`, `ws_check.js`, `publish_stages.js`, `lang_check.js`, `baseline3.js`, `scene_object_test.js`, `sticker_owner_check.js`, `diag_layerpack3.js`, `runtime_pass_test.js`, `museum_fidelity_test.js`, `real_museum_trace.js`, `real_museum_selection_check.js`) passes unchanged ŌĆö `scene_object_test.js`'s own Museum Gallery Wax Seal selection independently confirms the same fix (`cardTabVisible:false`); both `goldenBuild.js` suites (v1 and v2) pass unchanged. **One suspected third bug was investigated and found to be a test-script artifact, not a product defect**: a Shape Experience ("Wax Seal," a green circle) initially failed to render or compile into the Layer Pack at all when authored via raw `ProjectModel` calls ŌĆö traced to the raw calls omitting `updateExperience(project,id,{contentKind:'graphics'})` before setting `graphicShape`, a real, already-known, already-solved gate (`contentKind` is inferred once at creation and never re-inferred on a later property write, the identical class of gap the Repository-Only Card work had already found and disclosed for Image content) ŌĆö confirmed the REAL "Add a Shape" quick-picker in `tools/world-builder-v2/js/worldBuilderApp.js` (line ~5931) already sets `contentKind:'graphics'` correctly before writing `graphicShape`, so real authors are unaffected; re-running the authoring test with the correct sequence confirmed the shape compiles correctly (`decoration:{kind:'shape',shape:'circle',...}`, `target:'overlay'`) and renders at the exact authored colour (`rgb(17,170,51)`, an exact match for `#11AA33`) in Creator. No Builder/Theme-contract/architecture change ŌĆö both fixes are root-cause corrections inside `js/creationFlow.js` and `js/contextPanel.js`, reusing structures that already existed.)

- Vihu Card Platform v1 ŌĆö Redeemed Theme Vanished On Every Hard Refresh (a real, user-reported bug found via live testing on the deployed site, not the sandboxed test suite ŌĆö "the theme added through vihucard why does it goes away on every hard refresh." **Root cause, traced not guessed**: `registerRedeemedTheme` deliberately never caches a redeemed Theme's own content to `localStorage` (only its identifiers + expiry, via `_persistRedeemedGrants()`) ŌĆö by design, the redeemed Theme is meant to be re-fetched fresh from its owner's Personal Repository on every boot via `_rehydrateRedeemed()`. But `_rehydrateRedeemed()` was called from inside `js/themeRegistry.js`'s own self-initializing top-level IIFE ŌĆö and `index.html` loads `js/themeRegistry.js` BEFORE `js/themeRepositoryClient.js`, so at the exact moment that call ran, `window.ThemeRepositoryClient` was always `undefined`; the function's own defensive guard (`if (typeof window.ThemeRepositoryClient==='undefined') return;`) silently no-oped on literally every single boot, regardless of script order elsewhere or network reachability ŌĆö the re-fetch never ran, ever, so a redeemed Theme (never cached, never re-fetched) simply vanished the instant the tab was closed or reloaded. **Fix**: `_rehydrateRedeemed` is exported from `ThemeRegistry`'s API (`rehydrateRedeemed`) instead of self-invoking, and is now triggered from `js/app.js`'s `_startCreationFlow()` ŌĆö the exact same place, timed the exact same way, `refreshFromRepository()` (an analogous "needs `ThemeRepositoryClient`, must run after all scripts load" case) already runs from; by the time `app.js` executes, both scripts are guaranteed loaded regardless of tag order. **A second, real robustness gap found while writing the fix**: `_refreshRepositoryWithTimeout()`'s call to `ThemeRegistry.refreshFromRepository()` was never wrapped in try/catch ŌĆö a synchronous throw from a partial/broken `ThemeRepositoryClient` (reproduced directly during verification: a test double missing one method) would escape before any Promise existed to attach `.catch()` to, aborting the rest of `_startCreationFlow()`'s own function body outright ŌĆö including the new `rehydrateRedeemed()` call placed right after it. Fixed by wrapping `_refreshRepositoryWithTimeout()`'s body in try/catch, returning `Promise.resolve()` on a synchronous failure, so one broken repository call can never silently take a sibling boot step down with it. Verified via a new Playwright test reproducing the exact reported scenario end-to-end: seed the real `vihu.themeRegistry.redeemedGrants.v1` localStorage key (exactly what a real redemption writes), perform a real `page.reload()` (a genuine hard refresh, not a simulated one), and confirm the Theme is re-registered ŌĆö failed exactly as reported before the fix (`hasTheme:false`, zero `loadPersonalByOwner` calls), passes after (`hasTheme:true`, `redeemed:true`, one correctly-addressed `loadPersonalByOwner` call). Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Card-Platform Playwright suite and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged. No schema/RPC/data-model change ŌĆö both fixes are boot-sequence-ordering corrections in `js/themeRegistry.js` and `js/app.js`. **A deeper, disclosed limitation, raised directly and confirmed rather than papered over**: this fix guarantees `_rehydrateRedeemed()` actually RUNS on every boot ŌĆö it does not, and cannot, guarantee the redeemer's own identity still resolves. Creator/Studio has no user-account system of any kind; the only "identity" a redemption is tied to is the redeemer's disposable Supabase anonymous session (`_ensureAuth()`), persisted by Supabase's own client library to its own `localStorage` key, separate from the small `vihu.themeRegistry.redeemedGrants.v1` grant list this fix rehydrates from. `card_redemptions.redeemer_id` is recorded against that anonymous `auth.uid()` at redemption time, and the Personal Repository's read policy checks it matches on every later fetch. `_ensureAuth()` correctly calls `getSession()` before ever calling `signInAnonymously()`, so an ordinary reload on the same browser reuses the same identity ŌĆö confirmed via the Playwright test above, a genuine `page.reload()`. But if that anonymous session is ever lost ŌĆö private/incognito browsing, the user clears site data, a different browser or device, or Supabase's own anonymous-session lifecycle expiring it ŌĆö the grant becomes permanently unrecoverable through any refresh, since nothing maps "this person" to "their redeemed themes" beyond that one disposable token. Explicitly decided, when raised, to leave this as a disclosed limitation for now rather than build local content-caching or real account support ŌĆö matching this codebase's own existing precedent for Personal Repository/Cloud Backup ("no accounts yet," a real native upgrade path later, not a permanent ceiling). Revisit if this becomes a real recurring complaint.)

- Creator Rendering Bug Fixes ŌĆö Hosted-by-Scene Image Backgrounds, Change Look Modal Size (three real, user-reported bugs from a real "My Artwork Gallery" screenshot: a full-bleed decorative image sat on top of the picture Holder instead of behind it, a Scene authored with no Holder still appeared to show one, and the "Change Look" mid-edit screen took over the entire viewport. Two root-caused and fixed; one investigated and disclosed. **Bug 1 ŌĆö Background renders on top of the Holder**: traced to `tools/world-builder-v2/js/services/builder.js`'s `convergeSceneLayer()` ŌĆö only a true Colour fill (`kind:'fill'`) ever converged onto the `'slide'` compile target (rendered first, i.e. behind the Frame/Holder); an Image/Graphics/Text Experience the Theme Author explicitly set "Hosted by Scene" fell through to `'overlay'` (rendered last, on top of literally everything) regardless of that choice, because `js/projectModel.js`'s `_syncUniversalContent()` never carried "Hosted by Scene" onto the mirrored Scene Layer for anything but Colour ŌĆö the capability existed in the Inspector's Hosted-By dropdown (all three hosts were always selectable for any content type) but silently did nothing for Image content until now. Fixed by stamping a new `hostedByScene` marker onto every mirrored Layer kind (not just the Colour fill path), and having `convergeSceneLayer()` honour it identically to `kind==='fill'` ŌĆö "Hosted by Scene" now uniformly means wall-level/behind, matching what its own name promises, for any content kind. Confirmed via a real headless Build + Creator import: a full-bleed green image Hosted by Scene now compiles to `target:'slide'` and the Holder's own placeholder chrome renders correctly on top of it (pixel-sampled, not the green background bleeding through). A Theme Author with an already-authored, Free-hosted "Background" needs to switch its Hosted By to Scene in World Builder for this fix to take effect ŌĆö the code change makes the capability work correctly, it doesn't retroactively re-host existing content. **Bug 2 ŌĆö "Change Look" fills the entire screen**: `js/creationFlow.js`'s `changeRepresentation()` (the Context Panel's mid-edit Page Style shortcut) reused the exact same `.creation-flow-overlay` element Screens 1/2 use for a brand-new project's first arrival ŌĆö full-viewport, illustrated Story Meadow scene included ŌĆö appropriate for onboarding, wildly oversized for a quick "pick a different look" action taken mid-edit. Fixed with a new `mode-change-look` CSS class (`css/style.css`) applied only for this reuse: the same overlay element and JS, but the decorative scene is hidden, the backdrop becomes a plain dimmed scrim (so the editor stays visibly present behind it, dimmed), and `.creation-flow-panel` becomes a compact ~560px centered modal card instead of an edge-to-edge panel. Verified: the panel's own bounding rect is 560├Ś231px against a 1500├Ś950 viewport, not full-viewport, confirmed via both a DOM measurement and a screenshot. **Bug 3 ŌĆö investigated, not reproduced**: a Builder Scene authored with zero Places was reported to still show a Holder in Creator; a from-scratch reproduction (a real Build with a genuinely zero-Place Scene, imported through the real production path) showed the existing `holders:0` gating (from the earlier "Object Strip Label + Zero-Holder Layout fixes" sprint) already correctly hides the Artwork Place card and skips the Frame/Holder chrome entirely ŌĆö the fix works as designed for a freshly-compiled package. The most likely explanation, disclosed rather than guessed further into, is that the user's live "My Artwork Gallery" World was built before that earlier fix shipped and hasn't been rebuilt/republished since; flagged for the user to confirm by rebuilding, rather than inventing a second, unverified code change for a symptom that couldn't be reproduced. Verified via a new 2-scenario Playwright reproduction (`three_bugs_check.js`, scratch-only ŌĆö real headless Build via `ProjectCompiler`, real import through `ThemeEngine.importThemeFile`, real Creation Flow drive-through, pixel-sampled z-order check, DOM-measured modal size) plus full regression across every existing Creator/Card-Platform Playwright suite and both `goldenBuild.js` suites, all passing unchanged. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model change ŌĆö both fixes are additive completions of an already-existing "Hosted By" capability and a CSS-only variant of an already-existing overlay reuse.)

- Host-Aware Bounds, Actually Enforced ŌĆö Scene-Hosted Content Self-Heals to Full Bleed (a direct, same-day follow-up: after Bug 1 above shipped, the user tested a fresh "Hosted by Scene" Background and still saw it render incorrectly. Investigated with a real World Builder screenshot rather than assumed ŌĆö the Context Inspector's own "Bounds" section read "Inherited from Scene (read-only) ŌĆö this Experience fills the whole Scene," but the Experience's actual Transform sliders showed `X:1% Y:29% Width:99% Height:40%` ŌĆö a real, confirmed contradiction between what the UI claimed and what it actually let an author do. **Root cause**: `_contentTransformFields()` in `tools/world-builder-v2/js/worldBuilderApp.js` ŌĆö the shared helper rendering each content section's (Text/Image/Graphics) X/Y/Width/Height sliders ŌĆö has never been gated on `hostedBy` at all; it always rendered fully free, editable sliders regardless of whether the Experience was Hosted by Scene/Place/Free, silently contradicting the Bounds panel's own pre-existing copy (itself dated to Builder V3.1's original "Host-aware Bounds" design intent, which this function never actually implemented). Before Bug 1's fix, this mismatch was invisible ŌĆö only a Colour fill could be Scene-hosted, and Colour has no Transform sliders at all ŌĆö so the gap only became reachable once Image/Graphics/Text could meaningfully be Scene-hosted. **Fix**: `_contentTransformFields` now takes a `hostedBy` parameter (threaded through from all three call sites ŌĆö Text/Image/Graphics); for `hostedBy==='scene'` or `'place'`, it renders a plain read-only note instead of sliders, and ŌĆö critically ŌĆö self-heals any already-drifted stored rect back to `{x:0,y:0,w:1,h:1}` the moment that Experience's Properties panel renders, the same read-time-reconciliation discipline this file already uses elsewhere (`_ensureHolderDefaults`, `_ordered`) so a Theme Author never has to manually drag sliders back or hunt for a "reset" control ŌĆö simply opening/checking on the Experience (something they'd naturally do anyway) fixes it, and the next Build picks up the correction automatically. Verified end-to-end via a real Playwright reproduction of the user's own exact drifted values (`X:0.01 Y:0.29 W:0.99 H:0.40`, Hosted by Scene): confirmed the drifted rect is genuinely stored before any UI interaction, then drove the real Working View (open the Project ŌåÆ Scenes nav ŌåÆ open the Scene ŌåÆ click the Background Experience card) and confirmed the stored rect self-corrected to `{0,0,1,1}` purely from that click, with no slider interaction at all; a subsequent real `ProjectCompiler.runBuild()` confirmed the compiled Layer Pack entry now carries `target:'slide'` with a full-bleed rect. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder Playwright suite and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model change ŌĆö this closes the last gap in Bug 1's own fix, making "Hosted by Scene" behave exactly as its own UI has always claimed it does.)

- Zero-Holder Scenes ŌĆö the "no border, period" gate closed for the legacy fallback path too (a follow-up found while chasing a user-reported "the Builder says no Place, but Creator still shows a Holder box" report; the earlier "Object Strip Label + Zero-Holder Layout fixes" sprint's own stated intent was "`_resolveBorder`'s Artwork Theme branch skips resolving Frame/mat/wall chrome entirely when `_activeLayoutHolders(s)===0`," but the implementation only ever gated that one branch ŌĆö the function still fell through to the older, artwork-independent Sprint 8.4.2 "Picture Holder defaults" (`themeOptions.holder`) fallback beneath it, which can resolve its own non-null border from a theme's generic cornerRadius/padding/shadow/fill defaults with no relationship to Places/Holders at all; once that fallback's border came back non-null, `render()`'s artwork-placeholder-box code (gated only on `_border` being truthy, not on holder count) still drew the "Tap to add your artwork" box for a Scene that genuinely has zero Places. Fixed by moving the `_activeLayoutHolders(s)===0` check to the very top of `_resolveBorder`, before either branch runs, so zero-Holder now means no border resolves at all ŌĆö matching Builder's own Runtime Preview, which draws nothing for a Scene with no Places. The now-always-true inner check inside the Artwork Theme branch was simplified away as dead condition. Verified via a real Playwright A/B test (`git stash`-toggling the fix on a synthetic zero-Holder Scene, comparing full-panel-rect pixel diffs before/after) ŌĆö for a freshly-authored World Builder theme with no `themeOptions.holder` defaults set, the legacy fallback branch was already returning null even pre-fix, so this specific reproduction shows the fix closes a real, disclosed gap without changing observable output for that particular case; the actual visible symptom the user reported is still being triaged separately (a second, still-present object in their real World, not yet root-caused) since it didn't reproduce against this synthetic fixture ŌĆö this entry documents the `_resolveBorder` gap-closure on its own merits, not as a confirmed fix for that report. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (including the earlier `three_bugs_check.js`'s own zero-Holder Object Strip assertion) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged.)

- Zero-Holder Scenes ŌĆö the real white-box source found and fixed (a direct, confirmed follow-up to the previous entry, found by reproducing the user's actual live World rather than a synthetic guess: "My shapes ŌĆ║ First" ŌĆö a zero-Place Scene with a Scene-hosted dark Colour-fill background and a Free-hosted gold octagon Decoration Shape. The previous fix (closing `_resolveBorder`'s legacy-fallback gap) was real and necessary but insufficient ŌĆö it correctly made `_border` resolve to `null` for a zero-Holder Scene, but `render()`'s own composition-selection code, `if(_composition==='quote'){...}else if(_border){...}else{ _drawPanel(t.panel.color,opts.panelStyle,_panelRect) }`, then routed into that `else` branch precisely because `_border` was null ŌĆö and that branch unconditionally paints the classic pre-Artwork-Theme "story picture panel" rectangle (`t.panel.color`, in practice a near-white page colour) at the panel rect, with zero awareness of Holder count at all; it predates the whole Scene/Place/Holder system and exists for the case of a plain Story Theme with no Artwork Theme active, where painting that rectangle is correct (it's where the picture will go). For a zero-Holder Artwork Theme Scene, though, there is no picture area to paint a background for at all ŌĆö Builder's own Working View/Runtime Preview show nothing there. Fixed with a third branch, `else if(_activeLayoutHolders(s)===0){ /* draw nothing */ }`, inserted between the Quote check and the `_border` check, so a Scene explicitly declaring zero Places now paints nothing beyond its own 'slide'-scoped Layer Pack content (background fill / decorations), matching Builder exactly. Verified with a real `git stash`-based A/B test reproducing the user's exact World shape end-to-end (real `ProjectCompiler.runBuild()`, real `ThemeEngine.importThemeFile`/`applyArtworkTheme`, real `SlideRenderer.render()`): pre-fix, the panel-rect center pixel reads pure white `(255,255,255,255)`; post-fix, the same pixel reads the theme's own cream page colour `(247,244,238,255)` ŌĆö the exact "white box" signature confirmed present before this change and gone after it, on the same input, same commit tree, only this one code path toggled. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (Museum Gallery ŌĆö a real Holder-bearing theme ŌĆö still renders its Frame/mat/Wax Seal/placeholder exactly as before, confirming no regression for the non-zero-Holder case) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged.)

- Honour World-Owned Object Commitments + Accurate Object Strip Thumbnails (a design-sprint feature, requested directly after the user asked whether Creator actually honours the four checkboxes in World Builder's per-object permission block ŌĆö the answer was "no, only `visible`" ŌĆö and separately asked why the Object Strip showed generic icons instead of an object's real content. Investigated via three parallel Explore passes (Object Strip's card-building code and what the render tree already carries; existing Story-Author move/edit override patterns; the compiled Layer Pack shape and Decoration Slot's actual implementation state) before designing, then implemented per an approved plan. **A. Accurate thumbnails**: `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_pushLayerObject` (previously discarding `layer.decoration`/`.sticker`/`.text` after using them only to draw) now also computes a normalized `visual` descriptor (`_layerVisual`) forwarded onto every Scene Object ŌĆö `{kind:'color',color}` for a fill, `{kind:'image',src}` (resolved via `ThemeRegistry.resolveAssetRef`, or a live Story-Author-uploaded data URI) for an image, `{kind:'shape',shape,fillColor,...}` for a vector shape, `{kind:'glyph',glyph}` for a sticker, `{kind:'text',content,snippet}` for a text Layer (`content` full for editing, `snippet` truncated for display) ŌĆö reflecting any live Story-Author override, so an edited object's thumbnail stays in sync with what's actually drawn. New exported `SlideRenderer.drawObjectThumbnail(ctx,visual,size)` reuses `drawFrameSwatch`'s own context-swap technique to render a Shape thumbnail via the existing `_layerDrawShape`, no second drawing implementation. `js/objectStrip.js`'s `_card()` gained a `_renderThumb` branch per `visual.kind` ŌĆö a real CSS background-colour swatch, a real `<img>`, a real `<canvas>` shape, the real glyph, or a truncated text snippet ŌĆö falling through to the old generic icon when `visual` is absent (every pre-existing card shape, unchanged). **B. Honour "Can a Story Author move this?"
