(moveable)**: two structural gaps closed together ŌĆö `_pushLayerObject` previously hardcoded `locked:true` regardless of the real `moveable` value (the one flag `js/app.js`'s existing drag machinery actually checks), now `locked:!layer.moveable`, so a `moveable:true` World object engages the *exact same* mousedown/mousemove/mouseup chain Cover/Hook/End elements already use ŌĆö no new drag code; and since `js/app.js`'s existing non-sticker drag path already reads/writes `slide.metadata.elementOverrides[id].position` generically for *any* element id (confirmed by reading the code, not assumed ŌĆö this made the plan's original "new sibling override bag" design unnecessary and simpler to just reuse the existing bag directly, since a Builder-generated Layer id never collides with SceneEngine's own fixed blueprint-element ids and `getRenderData()` only ever reads keys present in the current page's own blueprint), `_layerDrawDecoration`/`_layerDrawText`/`_layerDrawSticker` each gained one resolution step reading that same bag via a new shared `_layerOverride(s,layerId)` helper before falling back to the authored anchor/rect ŌĆö a pure translation applied to whatever the Layer would have drawn naturally (computed from the natural bbox center for text, so the shift stays correct regardless of alignment), byte-identical to before this sprint when no override exists. **C. Honour "Can a Story Author change this?" (editable) ŌĆö in-place content edit only, no delete/remove, confirmed directly with the user**: `js/sceneEngine.js` gained one generic `setContentOverride(slide,id,field,value)` (mirroring `setPosition`/`setRotation`'s own `_ensureEntry`/`_maybePrune` shape) for the `fillColor`/`content`/`image` fields a World-owned object's content can carry; `js/contextPanel.js`'s `_renderWorldObjectDisclosure` now renders one real, kind-specific control when `editable:true` and the object's `visual.kind` supports one ŌĆö a colour input for `color`/`shape`, a Replace Image upload row for `image`, a Words textarea for `text` ŌĆö writing through that same override bag and redrawing live (never calling the panel's own `refresh()`, which would rebuild the very input mid-edit); a bare `glyph` object keeps the original "that kind of edit isn't available in Creator yet" wording, a disclosed simplification since recolouring/replacing a glyph has no natural analog and wasn't one of the two examples the user named. **D. Decoration Slot, shipped in the same sprint per explicit direction, rather than deferred**: `tools/world-builder-v2/js/services/builder.js`'s `convergeSceneLayer` previously never copied World Builder's own `layer.decorationSlot` (the 4th permission-block checkbox) into the compiled package at all ŌĆö dead data on both sides ŌĆö now carried through as `decorationSlot` on the compiled entry. Creator reuses the *existing* Sticker Studio flow end to end (pick-from-library ŌåÆ place-on-canvas ŌåÆ `slide.metadata.stickers[]`) rather than inventing a second "Story Author adds content" mechanism: a selected `decorationSlot:true` object's disclosure gains a "Ō£© Add your own decoration here" button; `js/stickerStudio.js` gained a one-shot `setNextPlacementSeed(centerX,centerY)` (consumed and cleared by the very next insert only, so every other Add-a-Sticker flow keeps its ordinary centered default) seeding that one placement near the slot's own position instead of dead-center ŌĆö the resulting sticker is a completely ordinary, fully Story-owned object with the same Select/Move/Resize/Rotate/Layer/Lock/Delete capabilities every other sticker already has. Verified end-to-end via a new Playwright fixture (a synthetic World with a Scene-hosted Colour fill [moveable+editable], a Free-hosted Shape [moveable+editable+decorationSlot], a Free-hosted Image [editable, not moveable], and a Free-hosted Text layer [editable] ŌĆö each compiled through the real `ProjectCompiler`, imported through the real `ThemeEngine`/`ThemeRegistry`, rendered through the real `SlideRenderer`): all four kinds show accurate, distinguishable Object Strip thumbnails; the moveable/non-moveable objects' `locked` flags resolve correctly; a real colour-input edit persists into `elementOverrides` and the Object Strip thumbnail reflects it live with zero panel rebuild; the Decoration Slot button appears only for the flagged object and is absent otherwise. One real bug found and fixed during fixture-building, unrelated to this sprint's own code: the test's Scene-hosted Colour Experience initially failed to compile at all, traced to a spelling mismatch (`contentKind:'color'` vs. the codebase's actual `'colour'` enum value in `_syncUniversalContent`) ŌĆö not a defect, just confirms this convention is real and consistent. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (Museum Gallery's own Wax Seal ŌĆö a glyph-kind, non-real-control object ŌĆö still shows the original disclosure wording unchanged, confirming the new control only appears where a real one exists) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged.)

- Change Look Modal ŌĆö Oversized Representation Thumbnails Blew Out the Panel (a direct, user-reported layout bug: "change look is very bad looking layout" ŌĆö a screenshot showed a giant, cropped photo overflowing the "Change Look" mid-edit modal with visible scrollbars, distinct from the earlier "Change Look fills the entire screen" bug already fixed via the `mode-change-look` CSS class. **Root cause**: `js/creationFlow.js`'s `_repCard()` (the Page Style card builder used only by `_renderChangeRepresentationScreen`, the Context Panel's "Change Representation"/"Change Look" shortcut) renders `<img class="creation-flow-card-icon-image">` whenever a Representation's thumbnail resolves to a real image ŌĆö which, per `_repThumbnail()`'s own fallback chain, means the World's own Hero Image whenever the Representation itself has no thumbnail of its own (the common case) ŌĆö but `css/style.css` had zero rules for that class at all; the `<img>` rendered at its full intrinsic photo resolution (e.g. a real 900├Ś1200 upload) with nothing constraining its size, blowing out its card, the grid, and the `mode-change-look` panel's own 560px/85vh box (confirmed via a real `git stash` A/B test: pre-fix, `panel.scrollWidth` 1211px against a 560px `clientWidth` ŌĆö genuine horizontal overflow ŌĆö with each `<img>` rendering at its full 900├Ś1200 natural size; post-fix, both images constrain to 196├Ś110 with zero overflow). **Fix**: added `.creation-flow-card-icon-image{width:100%;height:110px;object-fit:cover;border-radius:14px;box-shadow:inset 0 0 0 1px var(--cf-line);flex-shrink:0;}` right after `.creation-flow-card-icon`'s own rule ŌĆö the same `width:100%`/fixed-height/`object-fit:cover` shape every other Creation Flow image thumbnail already uses (`.creation-flow-world-thumb img`, `.creation-flow-carousel-art img`), sized as a real photo preview rather than the small 56├Ś56 emoji-badge circle `.creation-flow-card-icon` uses for a glyph. `_repCard` itself, `_renderChangeRepresentationScreen`, and the `mode-change-look` modal sizing from the earlier fix are all unchanged ŌĆö this was purely a missing CSS rule for one image class. Verified via a new Playwright reproduction (`change_look_image_overflow.js`, scratch-only) driving the real `CreationFlow.changeRepresentation()` against a synthetic World whose Representation has no thumbnail of its own (forcing the Hero Image fallback, a realistic 900├Ś1200 photo): post-fix, both Page Style cards' images measure 196├Ś110 with the panel holding its 560px width and zero horizontal overflow; full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (`regression.js`, `final_qa.js`, `frame_variation_test3.js`, `ws_check.js`, `publish_stages.js`, `lang_check.js`, `baseline3.js`, `scene_object_test.js`, `sticker_owner_check.js`, `diag_layerpack3.js`, `runtime_pass_test.js`, `museum_fidelity_test.js`, `real_museum_trace.js`, `real_museum_selection_check.js`, `three_bugs_check.js`, `commitments_test.js`) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged ŌĆö this fix touches only `css/style.css`, no JS/architecture change.)

- A New Sticker Sits Centered But Can't Be Dragged, Layer Order Buttons "Don't Work" (a real, user-reported bug from a real "My shapes" screenshot: an Apple sticker sat centered over a large World-owned Decoration Shape and could not be dragged on canvas. **Root cause, traced directly, not assumed**: the Honour World-Owned Object Commitments sprint's own `_pushLayerObject`/`_layerObjectBboxes` accumulator (introduced earlier, in the Creator Reconciliation Sprint) concatenates every World-owned Layer Pack object onto the very END of `_lastSceneElements` as one lump, regardless of which of the 5 containership scopes (`slide`/`frame`/`holder`/`element`/`overlay`) actually drew it ŌĆö but only `overlay`-scoped objects are genuinely drawn LAST, on top of everything (the Builder Convergence Sprint's own explicit design); `slide`/`frame`/`holder`/`element`-scoped World objects are all drawn EARLIER in the same render pass, visually BEHIND every Scene element and Story-Author sticker. `js/app.js`'s `_hitTestSceneElement` reads `_lastSceneElements` topmost-first (last element in the array wins), so a `slide`-scoped World shape ŌĆö visually sitting behind the sticker ŌĆö was nonetheless always hit-tested as if it sat on top, silently intercepting every click/drag meant for an overlapping sticker (or any Scene element) drawn beneath it; since that World shape is typically `locked` (non-`moveable`), the drag machinery correctly refused to move it, reading as "the sticker can't be dragged." **Fix**: `_pushLayerObject` now records which `target` scope produced each entry (`renderer/slideRenderer.js`); at the single concatenation point, the accumulator splits into `overlay`-scoped objects (still appended after everything, unchanged) and every other scope (now spliced in BEFORE Scene elements/Stickers instead of after) ŌĆö restoring hit-testing to match real visual z-order: an `overlay`-scoped World object correctly still wins over an overlapping sticker (verified, unchanged), while a `slide`/`frame`/`holder`/`element`-scoped one no longer steals clicks from Story content drawn on top of it. **The second symptom, investigated and found to be a real, disclosed structural limit rather than a bug**: `SceneEngine.bringStickerForward`/`sendStickerBackward`/`bringStickerToFront`/`sendStickerToBack` (`js/sceneEngine.js`) only ever reorder a sticker relative to *other stickers* in the same array ŌĆö with exactly one sticker on the page (the reported case), every one of the four Order buttons is a correct, guarded no-op (`i===arr.length-1`/`i<=0`), since there's nothing else to swap with; Story-Author stickers and World-owned Layer Pack content are drawn in two structurally separate phases (stickers always after Scene elements, before `overlay`) and Order buttons have never reordered across that boundary ŌĆö not touched, since doing so would be a real architecture change, not a bug fix, and wasn't what broke here. Verified via two new Playwright reproductions (scratch-only): `sticker_dragorder_bug.js` (a `git`-comparable A/B ŌĆö reproduced the exact wrong-hit-test-id bug pre-fix, confirmed the sticker's own center now resolves correctly post-fix) and `sticker_dragorder_bug2.js` (confirms an `overlay`-scoped World object still correctly wins hit-testing when genuinely on top, then drives a real end-to-end `page.mouse` down/move/up drag on the canvas and confirms the sticker's real `x`/`y` actually change, not the locked World shape beneath it). Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged ŌĆö the fix is confined to `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_pushLayerObject`/concatenation step, no Theme Contract/Scene Model/Builder change.)

- Unified Layer Ordering ŌĆö the Object Strip Becomes a Real Reorder Control (a direct follow-up to the sticker drag/hit-test fix above: "as we are fixing creator one by one, i think we should fix this [layer order buttons]" ŌĆö the user's own follow-up question, "can object strip be used as layering order? if we reorder objects there the layering reorder itself?", became the design. Investigated via a dedicated Explore pass (Plan Mode) before designing, confirming the real root cause was structural, not cosmetic: three completely separate, disjoint ordering mechanisms existed with no shared key ŌĆö Scene blueprint elements (Frame/Decoration/Text-holder on Cover/Hook/End pages) order via a numeric `zIndex` (`SceneEngine.adjustZIndex`); Stickers order via plain array position (`SceneEngine.bringStickerForward`/etc., `js/sceneEngine.js`); World-owned Layer Pack objects order purely by containership scope. `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `render()` assembled the final hit-test/paint array as a **fixed concatenation**, never a true merge-sort ŌĆö Scene elements always drawn first, then every Sticker unconditionally after, regardless of either's own ordering value ŌĆö so a Sticker could never be reordered relative to a Frame/Decoration element on ANY page role (Cover/Hook/End included, not just Story), which is the real reason a lone sticker's "Front" button looked like it did nothing. **Fix, scoped deliberately after investigating the render pipeline's real constraints**: Scene blueprint elements and Stickers now draw as ONE interleaved, resolvable pass instead of two fixed loops. New `_naturalStoryOrder(s)`/`_resolveStoryOrder(s)` (`renderer/slideRenderer.js`) compute the reorderable group's order ŌĆö natural (no override) is exactly the old fixed sequence, so every existing page/theme renders byte-identically until a Story Author actually reorders something; a new, additive `slide.metadata.layerOrder` array (`SceneEngine.getLayerOrder`/`setLayerOrder`, mirroring the existing override-bag "delete when empty" convention) lets that reordering persist. New exported `SlideRenderer.getReorderableIds(s)` is the one place both entry points read/write the current effective order from. Card Designer's three previously-separate Order button blocks (Sticker's 4-button row calling `SceneEngine[fn]`; Frame's 2-button row calling `_frameAdjustZ`ŌåÆ`adjustZIndex`; Decoration's 2-button row calling `adjustZIndex` inline) all collapse onto one shared `_reorderSelected(edge, commitFn)` helper (`js/cardDesigner.js`) ŌĆö so "Bring Forward" on a lone sticker now genuinely moves it in front of a Frame/Decoration element too, and the buttons can never disagree with what the Object Strip shows, since both write the same `layerOrder`. `js/objectStrip.js` gained real HTML5 drag-and-drop on every card whose object is in the current reorderable set (`_wireReorderDrag`/`_performReorder`) ŌĆö dragging a card left-to-right changes the object's actual paint/hit-test order (matching the strip's own existing left=back/right=front display convention), not just its own position in the list; a drop-indicator line and grab cursor (`css/style.css`'s `.object-card-draggable`/`.object-card-drop-before`/`-after`) make the affordance visible. **Scope, deliberately bounded and disclosed rather than forced** (this round): World-owned Layer Pack objects (moveable or not) are NOT part of this reorderable group ŌĆö investigated directly and found that their rect for `frame`/`holder`/`element` scopes is only resolved at specific points inside Frame/Panel drawing, and their `slide`/`overlay` scopes draw at fixed points (before Frame/Panel, and after everything else) that existing themes (including the Sprint's own "Hosted by Scene" background mechanism) already depend on ŌĆö unifying those safely would require deferred/two-pass drawing changes to the Frame/Panel rendering pipeline itself, a materially bigger and riskier change than this fix, so it's recorded as real follow-up work rather than attempted here (closed the same day ŌĆö see the entry directly below); a locked/non-moveable object of any kind keeps showing in the Object Strip (still a real object on the page) but never gets a drag handle and can never have anything dropped past its fixed boundary position, matching that it was never independently reorderable before either. Verified via a new Playwright suite (`unified_layer_order_test.js`, scratch-only) against a real Cover-role page (real Scene blueprint decorations + Stickers, not a synthetic stand-in): natural order matches the exact old fixed sequence; clicking the Sticker section's real "Front" button moves a lone sticker to the very top of the now-unified order; clicking a Scene decoration's real "Forward" button three times moves it past two Stickers in that same order (the literal cross-mechanism reorder that was previously impossible); a real `dragstart`/`dragover`/`drop` sequence dispatched on actual Object Strip card DOM elements changes the persisted `layerOrder` to match the drop position; a synthetic locked World-owned object is confirmed absent from `getReorderableIds()`. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (20 scripts) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors ŌĆö no Theme Contract/Scene Model/Builder change; the fix is confined to `renderer/slideRenderer.js`, `js/sceneEngine.js`, `js/cardDesigner.js`, `js/objectStrip.js`, and `css/style.css`.)

- Unified Layer Ordering ŌĆö Moveable World-Owned Shapes Join a Reorderable Group Too (a real, same-day follow-up: "ok so to test do i need to reauthor or just refresh the creator" led directly to a live repro screenshot of a real "My shapes" World ŌĆö Background/Builder BaŌĆ”/First BG/Apple ŌĆö where "reordering in object strip not happening." **Root cause, confirmed not assumed**: on that exact page, Builder BaŌĆ” and First BG are both moveable, non-overlay ('slide'-scoped) World-owned Decoration Shapes ŌĆö the previous entry's own disclosed scope cut excluded ALL World-owned objects from the reorderable group, so with only the Apple sticker actually draggable and nothing else wired for drag/drop at all, dropping it anywhere was structurally a no-op; there was nothing else to combine it with. **Fix, deliberately narrower than the full cross-bucket generalization** (an `AskUserQuestion` call failed with the same transient `AbortError` seen earlier this session; proceeded with the lower-risk "Recommended" default rather than block on it, disclosed here rather than silently decided): a `moveable:true` Layer Pack object now joins a reorderable group of its own ŌĆö but strictly WITHIN its own draw bucket, never crossing into another. Three buckets always draw in this fixed relative order: "earlier" (non-overlay World objects), "story" (the Scene-element/Sticker interleaved pass from the entry above), and "overlay" (overlay-scoped World objects). Two objects sharing a bucket (Builder BaŌĆ” and First BG, both 'earlier') can now be freely reordered relative to each other ŌĆö exactly as safe as the Scene/Sticker merge, since only which one draws first within the one shared `_renderLayers` call changes; crossing a bucket boundary (a Shape moving in front of the Apple sticker) is still NOT attempted ŌĆö that remains the deferred, bigger two-pass-drawing change. New `_applyOrderOverride(natural,order)` (`renderer/slideRenderer.js`) is the one resolution step both the Story bucket and the two World buckets now share, applied against the SAME page-wide `layerOrder` array ŌĆö ids are unique across buckets, so a foreign id sitting in the override is simply invisible to a bucket that doesn't contain it, keeping the three buckets from ever interfering with each other despite sharing one list. `getReorderableIds(s)` now returns the union of all three buckets' current (already-resolved, not just natural) ids ŌĆö a real bug caught and fixed mid-implementation via the test below: the first pass left `getReorderableIds`'s World-bucket helper reading only the natural push order, never applying the override, so a just-completed reorder would silently not show up on the next query even though `render()`'s own paint order was already correct; fixed by extracting one shared `_worldBucketOrder(s,wantOverlay)` that both `render()`'s bucket-splitting step and `getReorderableIds()` call, so both always agree. New `SlideRenderer.getReorderBucket(s,id)` reports which of the three buckets an id currently belongs to (`'story'`/`'earlier'`/`'overlay'`/`null`); `js/objectStrip.js`'s drag handler (`_sameReorderBucket`) uses it to refuse a cross-bucket drop outright ŌĆö no drop-indicator line, no reorder ŌĆö rather than silently accepting a drag that looked like it worked but moved nothing on the canvas. Verified via a new Playwright reproduction (`world_shape_reorder_test.js`, scratch-only) rebuilding the exact reported page shape (two moveable non-overlay Decoration Shapes + one Sticker): both Shapes are confirmed reorderable and share the `'earlier'` bucket; exactly 3 real draggable cards appear (2 Shapes + 1 Sticker, the synthetic Background/Artwork-Place cards correctly excluded); a real `dragstart`/`dragover`/`drop` sequence dragging one Shape onto the other actually swaps their resolved draw order; a same-sequence drag of the Sticker onto a Shape (different buckets) is correctly refused ŌĆö `dragover` never calls `preventDefault()`, no drop-indicator class appears, and the Shape order is unchanged afterward. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (19 scripts, including the immediately-prior `unified_layer_order_test.js`) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors ŌĆö no Theme Contract/Scene Model/Builder change; the fix is confined to `renderer/slideRenderer.js` and `js/objectStrip.js`. A locked World object's own relative position among its bucket-mates can shift slightly alongside a freshly-reordered moveable sibling ŌĆö it's simply never listed in the shared override, so it's always appended after every explicitly-reordered id (the same "last listed sits on top" convention the Story bucket's Sticker-append-on-top behaviour already established) ŌĆö a disclosed, minor nuance, not a functional regression, since a locked object was never independently reorderable to begin with.)

- Unified Layer Ordering ŌĆö Full Merge When There's No Frame/Holder Pipeline (a real, same-day follow-up: the previous entry's "own draw bucket" fix left a live "My shapes" World still broken ŌĆö a screenshot showed the Sticker's Card Designer Order buttons still doing nothing, Object Strip drag still not reordering, and "I was able to move the builder background but not the shape (First BG)." **Root cause, confirmed via a direct diagnostic, not assumed**: `convergeSceneLayer`'s bucket-assignment heuristic (`isFullBleed`, `rect.w>=0.98 && rect.h>=0.98`) is designed for an unrelated concern (Hosted-by-Scene wall-level vs. foreground content) ŌĆö a realistically-authored Shape with even a small margin (e.g. `rect:{x:0.08,y:0.08,w:0.84,h:0.84}`, matching the visible brown border around First BG in the user's own screenshot) lands in `'overlay'`, while a true full-bleed background lands in `'slide'` ŌĆö two DIFFERENT buckets under the previous fix's scoping, so Builder BaŌĆ” and First BG could never be dragged onto each other, and the lone Sticker (in the separate `'story'` bucket) could never move relative to either. All three complaints traced to this one cause: on a page with no picture Frame at all, nearly every real object a Theme Author places ends up artificially split across these three buckets by an unrelated heuristic. **Fix**: investigated whether full interleaving is actually safe here and found it is, for exactly this page shape ŌĆö a Scene explicitly converged with zero Places (`_activeLayoutHolders(s)===0`) or a Quote composition never runs the Frame/Panel drawing branch at all, so the `'frame'`/`'holder'`/`'element'` Layer Pack targets are never touched in that code path (their own `_renderLayers` calls live inside the branch that's skipped) ŌĆö meaning 'slide' and 'overlay' Layer Pack objects and every Scene element/Sticker are the ONLY things such a page ever draws, with nothing else whose draw-order depends on Frame/Panel geometry. New `_noFramePipeline` flag (`(_composition==='quote')||(_activeLayoutHolders(s)===0)`, computed once early in `render()`) switches the whole pipeline into a genuinely merged mode for exactly this case: the previously-unconditional bulk `_renderLayers(_layerPack,'slide',...)` call (drawn before the composition branch) and `_renderLayers(_layerPack,'overlay',...)` call (drawn after Scene+Sticker) are both skipped, and instead every 'slide'/'overlay' Layer Pack entry is combined with the Scene-element/Sticker natural order into ONE list, resolved via the same `_applyOrderOverride(natural,layerOrder)` mechanism the Story bucket already used, and drawn in that single resolved order via a new `LayerEngine.renderOne(layer,rect,helpers)` (extracted from `render()`'s existing per-layer body, reused by both the bulk and the new per-layer call sites ŌĆö never a second drawing implementation) exposed as `_renderOneLayer(layer,rect,s,target)` in `renderer/slideRenderer.js`. Each drawn Layer Pack entry is popped straight out of the shared `_layerObjectBboxes` accumulator into `_lastSceneElements` at its correct interleaved position (rather than the old end-of-pass bulk fold, which is now correctly a no-op for these pages since nothing populates `_layerObjectBboxes` for `'frame'`/`'holder'`/`'element'` in this path). A page WITH a real Frame/Holder (Museum Gallery and every other existing theme) is completely untouched ŌĆö `_noFramePipeline` is false there, so the exact previously-shipped 3-bucket behaviour runs unchanged, byte-identical. New `_lastRenderWasMerged` flag + `_mergedReorderableIds()` (`renderer/slideRenderer.js`) tell `getReorderableIds(s)`/`getReorderBucket(s,id)` that a merged-pass page has exactly ONE reorderable group (bucket name `'merged'`) read directly off `_lastSceneElements`'s own already-resolved order, rather than the old per-target `_layerObjectBboxes` scan (which would now find nothing, since every merged-pass entry is popped out immediately) ŌĆö a real bug caught and fixed mid-implementation by the very first version of the new verification test, which showed the bucket check failing until this was added. Verified via a new Playwright reproduction (`merged_order_test.js`, scratch-only) rebuilding the exact reported page (a full-bleed 'slide' background, a margin-inset shape that genuinely converges to 'overlay', and a Sticker, all on a zero-Holder Layout): all three objects now share one `'merged'` bucket and all three ids are reorderable; the Sticker's real Card Designer "Back" button now moves it behind BOTH shapes (previously impossible, since it was alone in the old 'story' bucket); a real Object Strip drag of First BG onto Builder Background actually swaps their resolved order; a direct pixel sample at the canvas center confirms the real PAINT order changed (not just id bookkeeping) ŌĆö the sampled colour matches Builder Background's `#3B2A1E` after the reorder, not First BG's `#E0A526`. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (21 scripts, including both prior Unified-Layer-Ordering tests) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors ŌĆö the fix is confined to `js/layerEngine.js` (new `renderOne`, `render()` refactored to call it) and `renderer/slideRenderer.js` (`_noFramePipeline`, the merged draw pass, `_lastRenderWasMerged`/`_mergedReorderableIds`); no Theme Contract/Scene Model/Builder change. Crossing into a page that DOES have a real picture Frame/Holder remains the one still-deferred piece ŌĆö reordering a 'slide'/'overlay' World object relative to Frame/Panel-interleaved content there would need the Frame/Panel drawing branch itself restructured, a materially bigger change intentionally left out of this pass.)

- Object Strip Becomes the ONE Reorder Control ŌĆö Card Designer Buttons Removed + Lock Badge Added (direct product feedback after trying the shipped Object Strip drag-to-reorder: "i like the reordering function in object strip. 2 recommendations. 1st remove any reordering function from the right panel. 2nd for an object which cannot be reordered, put a lock or some kind of information show." **Recommendation 1**: Card Designer's Sticker/Frame/Decoration sections each still carried the pre-Object-Strip "Order" button row (Back/Backward/Forward/Front for Sticker, Backward/Forward for Frame/Decoration) ŌĆö a second, now-redundant way to do the same thing the Object Strip's drag already does better, and a real UX inconsistency once both existed side by side. Removed all three button rows outright from `js/cardDesigner.js`, along with the shared `_reorderSelected(edge, commitFn)` helper they called (now genuinely dead code, not left orphaned) and `_frameAdjustZ` (Frame's own thin wrapper around it); `SlideRenderer.getReorderableIds()`/`SceneEngine.setLayerOrder()` ŌĆö the actual mechanism ŌĆö are completely unchanged, since the Object Strip's drag handler already reads/writes them directly. Also removed the now-unused `.sticker-layer-row`/`.sticker-layer-btn`/`.sticker-layer-glyph`, `.frame-layer-row`/`.frame-layer-btn`/`.frame-layer-glyph`, and `.decoration-layer-row`/`.decoration-layer-btn`/`.decoration-layer-glyph` CSS from `css/style.css` (careful to only strip the `-layer-` selectors out of combined rules like `.sticker-flip-row, .sticker-layer-row{...}`, leaving the still-used Flip LeftŌåöRight/UpŌåöDown button styling completely untouched). **Recommendation 2**: a real object (has its own render-tree id) that ISN'T in the current reorderable set ŌĆö a locked/non-`moveable` World-owned Layer Pack object ŌĆö now gets a small ­¤öÆ badge on its Object Strip thumbnail (`js/objectStrip.js`'s `_card()`, new `.object-card-lock-badge` CSS in `css/style.css`), positioned on the opposite corner from the existing Ō£Å’ĖÅ edit-capability badge so both can show independently (an object can be editable but not reorderable, or vice versa) ŌĆö plus a `title="Can't be reordered"` tooltip. Deliberately gated on `opts.id` truthy so the two synthetic Background/Artwork-Place cards (page-level concepts with no real id, never reorderable to begin with) never show it ŌĆö a lock badge there would answer a question nobody asked. Verified via a new Playwright test (`lock_badge_check.js`, scratch-only): a locked World-owned Shape shows the lock badge, a reorderable Sticker shows none, and the synthetic Background card shows none either. Two existing tests (`unified_layer_order_test.js`, `merged_order_test.js`) had their now-intentionally-broken button-click assertions replaced ŌĆö one confirms the Order buttons are genuinely gone rather than clicking dead DOM, the other re-proves the exact same cross-mechanism reorder (Sticker moving behind both World Shapes) via a real Object Strip drag instead of a button click, since that's now the only way to do it. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (22 scripts) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors ŌĆö no Theme Contract/Scene Model/Builder/rendering change; the fix is confined to `js/cardDesigner.js`, `js/objectStrip.js`, and `css/style.css`.)

- Click Empty Space Anywhere in Creator Deselects (direct product feedback: "any click in empty space anywhere in creator should get us out from any selected state. that is if apple is selected right now and i click in empty space in center pane, it should get deselected. this will ensure natural usage tendencies are respected." **Investigation confirmed a genuinely separate gap, not a duplicate of existing logic**: `js/app.js`'s `previewCanvas` `mousedown` handler already deselects when a click lands on empty CANVAS pixels ŌĆö hit-tests, finds nothing, and clears `_selectedTextElement`/`_selectedSceneElement` ŌĆö this has existed since before this sprint and needed no change. But `.preview-area` (the center pane) has real, separate clickable DOM space around the canvas itself: the flex gutter `.preview-wrapper` uses to center a fluid-sized canvas (`justify-content:center; align-items:flex-start`), and the Object Strip's own background beneath it ŌĆö neither ever had a listener, so a click there silently did nothing, exactly the reported symptom. **Fix**: one new `mousedown` listener on `.preview-area` (`js/app.js`), guarded by `e.target.closest('#previewCanvas, .object-card')` so it never fires for a click the canvas's own hit-testing already handles, or for an Object Strip card click (which already selects/deselects via its own `onClick` routing into `PageRuntime.selectSceneObject`/`selectTextObject`/`clearSelection`) ŌĆö only a genuine empty-background click reaches it, clearing both selection channels the same way the canvas's own fallback does. Verified via a new Playwright test (`deselect_empty_space_test.js`, scratch-only): a selected sticker is confirmed deselected by a real `page.mouse.click()` landing inside `.preview-area`'s bounding rect but outside `#previewCanvas`'s; a subsequent Object Strip card click ("Background") is confirmed to still work correctly and is unaffected by the new listener. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (22 scripts) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors ŌĆö no Theme Contract/Scene Model/Builder/rendering change; the fix is confined to `js/app.js`. See `docs/CREATOR_PAGE_RUNTIME.md` ┬¦5's new "Deselect on empty-space click" subsection for the full account.)

- "Change Look" Left Stale Object Strip Content From the Previous Scene (a real, user-reported bug found authoring a real Landscape "Dual Holder" Scene in World Builder v2's test theme: after switching this page's Page Style to it via the Context Panel's "Change Look" shortcut, Creator showed the page as if it still had the PREVIOUS Scene's content ŌĆö a Decoration Shape ("First BG") that belonged to an entirely different, zero-Holder Scene bled onto the newly-selected page, and "Artwork Place" (which should appear once the new Scene's Holder count is non-zero) was missing. **Root cause, confirmed via a real headless-Build + real-import reproduction, not guessed**: `js/creationFlow.js`'s `_applyRepresentationToCurrentSlide()` (the function "Change Look" calls) correctly updates `slide.metadata.layout` to the new Representation's Layout id, and correctly called `window.redrawPreview()` ŌĆö so the CANVAS pixels were, confirmed via pixel-sampling both before and after this fix, already rendering the right geometry (the correct landscape-shaped picture area, the correct wall tone) even in the buggy version. But it predates the Creator Page Runtime Sprint's `PageRuntime.notify()` dispatch (`redrawPreview`+`CardDesigner.refresh`+`ContextPanel.refresh`+`ObjectStrip.refresh`) and had never been updated to use it ŌĆö it only ever called `redrawPreview`/`renderList`/`ContextPanel.refresh` directly, missing `ObjectStrip.refresh()` entirely, so Object Strip kept showing whatever Layer Pack objects the PREVIOUS Representation's Scene had converged, stale, until some unrelated action happened to trigger a refresh. **Fix**: `_applyRepresentationToCurrentSlide()` now calls `PageRuntime.notify()` (falling back to the original three calls plus the previously-missing `ObjectStrip.refresh()` if `PageRuntime` isn't loaded for some reason) ŌĆö the same one dispatch every other selection/page-change path in Creator already routes through. **Two things investigated and confirmed NOT to be bugs, disclosed rather than silently "fixed"**: (1) the whole page canvas staying portrait-shaped (1080├Ś1350) regardless of a Scene's authored Aspect Ratio is Engine V1's known, disclosed, structural canvas-model limitation (`docs/ENGINE_V2_PROMOTION_STRATEGY.md`'s own finding ŌĆö "Engine V2 uses a genuinely different canvas model... Engine V1's always-fixed 1080├Ś1350 logical canvas") ŌĆö the picture FRAME area inside that fixed page correctly resolves to the Scene's own aspect (`renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_resolveLayout`/`LAYOUT_RECT`, confirmed via pixel-sampling to already produce the exact landscape rect `{x:70,y:340,w:940,h:610}`), it's only the outer page shape that stays fixed; (2) the wall-tone colour filling the ENTIRE page behind a smaller picture placeholder is Sprint 9.7's own deliberate "wall-level" design (`_resolveWallTone`, resolved independently of the image-gated Picture Border pipeline, a gallery-room-paint concept distinct from the picture area itself) ŌĆö not a rendering bug, confirmed identical before and after this fix. **A separate, disclosed, structural platform ceiling, not touched this session**: `tools/world-builder-v2/js/services/builder.js`'s `convergeScene()` only ever converges the Scene's FIRST Place's Frame reference onto the compiled Representation's `defaultFrame` (its own code comment: "Engine V1 has exactly one Holder per page... a pre-existing, disclosed ceiling this sprint does not lift") ŌĆö a Dual/Triple/Grid Holder Scene authored in Builder can only ever offer ONE artwork upload area in Creator, no matter how many Places exist; the `holders` count on the compiled Layout is used only to gate whether that one Artwork Place card/placeholder shows at all (zero vs. non-zero), never to render multiple independent picture regions. Lifting this would mean extending Engine V1's whole Representation/Holder model from one to many ŌĆö a real architecture change requiring its own explicit approval, not something to attempt as a side effect of this bug fix. Verified via a new Playwright reproduction (`dual_holder_repro2.js`, scratch-only) building a real two-Scene World (a zero-Holder "First" Scene with a Decoration Shape, a Landscape "Dual Holder" "second" Scene with a Frame assigned to both Places) through the real `ProjectCompiler`, importing the real compiled package, and driving the real "Change Look" UI flow: before the fix, Object Strip showed `["Background","Background","First BG"]` (stale) after switching to "second"; after, it correctly shows `["Background","Artwork Place"]`. A companion pixel-sampling check (`git stash`-based A/B) confirmed the canvas geometry/wall-tone rendering was correct in both the buggy and fixed versions, isolating this fix to the Object Strip staleness alone. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (22 scripts) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors ŌĆö no Theme Contract/Scene Model/Builder/rendering change; the fix is confined to one function in `js/creationFlow.js`.)

- Multiple Artwork Places Per Page (lifts the exact platform ceiling the entry directly above disclosed and deliberately did not touch: "than lets support as many holders as many authored by builder," approved via Plan Mode since this genuinely changes the core picture data model, rendering, hit-testing, Object Strip, and Context Panel/Card Designer. Until now, `renderer/slideRenderer.js` only ever resolved ONE picture area per page (`_panelRectFor(s)`) no matter how many Places (Builder's own "Holder" concept, renamed in Builder V3) a Theme Author built in World Builder v2 ŌĆö a "Dual Holder" Scene compiled and rendered exactly like a single-Holder one, missing its second artwork area entirely. **Compile-time** (`tools/world-builder-v2/js/services/builder.js`'s `convergeScene()`): a new, purely additive `placeRects` array rides alongside the existing (unchanged) `holders` count and `representation.defaultFrame` ŌĆö one entry per compiled Holder, carrying its own `id`/`name`/`position`/`size`/`shape`/`padding`/`fit`/`frame` (Frame Variation reference) exactly as Builder authored it; absent on every pre-existing compiled Layout (including Museum Gallery, which isn't Scene-authored at all) and on any `tools/world-builder/` (v1) output, which is deliberately left untouched. **Runtime** (`renderer/slideRenderer.js`): `_activeLayoutPlaces(s)` reads it (or returns `null`); `_placePixelRectFor(panelRect,place)` maps a Place's fractional rect onto the resolved panel rect; `_resolveBorder`/`_cardArtworkOverride`/`_resolveArtworkFields`/`_drawImage` all gained an *optional* trailing `placeId` parameter ŌĆö omitted, every one of them is byte-identical to before this feature (Place 1's legacy `s.image`/`cardOverrides.image/.border/.artwork` fields, untouched); a real id resolves that Place's own storage instead. **The two-id-space design, deliberately kept separate**: a compiled Place carries its own Builder-authored id (e.g. `holder-2`); Creator mints its own, distinct SELECTION id (`'image-holder'` for Place 1, `'image-place-2'`/`'image-place-3'`/... by array position for the rest) ŌĆö the key into `slide.metadata.placeContent[id]`/`slide._placeImages[id]` ŌĆö never the Builder id, since a real Theme Author could rename/reorder Places between Builder sessions and Creator's own storage must stay stable against Creator's OWN position-based addressing, not Builder's internal ids; `_placeByExternalId`/`_placeIndexForId` translate one to the other. **A real correctness question resolved deliberately mid-implementation, not left arbitrary**: should Place 1 itself be subdivided by its own authored fraction once 2+ Places exist, or always stay at the full panel rect regardless? Keeping it always full-panel (the naive "byte-identical, no exceptions" reading) would make Place 1 draw across the ENTIRE panel while Place 2+ occupy fractional sub-rects beside it ŌĆö visibly overlapping, defeating the entire point of a Dual-Holder layout; caught via direct pixel-sampling during verification (Place 1's sampled colour read as a wall-tone blend, not its own picture, because it was drawing full-bleed underneath Place 2's smaller inset rect). Resolved as: Place 1 stays at the full, untouched panel rect ONLY when 0 or 1 Places are authored (every existing theme, and a theme rebuilt post-feature with exactly one Place ŌĆö a lone Place's own Builder-authored fraction has no reliable 1:1 correspondence to Engine V1's already-caption-aware panel rect, so it's deliberately not applied there); once 2+ Places are authored, Place 1 is subdivided by its own fraction exactly like every other Place, so a Dual Holder layout genuinely renders two side-by-side, non-overlapping picture areas as Builder intended. `getPlaceRects(s)` (the one function Object Strip/hit-testing/pixel-verification all consume) mirrors this exact same conditional so it always reports precisely what `render()` actually draws. **Per-Place storage**: `slide.metadata.placeContent[placeId]={dataURL,imageView,cardOverrides:{artwork,border}}` for every Place beyond the first (the identical shape `cardOverrides.image/.border/.artwork` already use, just relocated) ŌĆö needs no `serialize()` change (already a wholesale `metadata` copy); `slide._placeImages[placeId]=<Image>` is the sibling runtime-only cache to today's `slide.image`, rehydrated by a new async loop in `ProjectManager.deserialize()` parallel to its existing `loadImageFromDataURL(p.image)` call. `js/pageOps.js`'s `duplicatePage()` gained one line copying `_placeImages` alongside its existing `image`/`metadata` copy. **Selection/hit-testing** (`js/app.js`): a new `_hitTestPlace`/`_placeImageFor` pair loops `SlideRenderer.getPlaceRects(s)` for the mousedown picture-pan gesture and cursor-hover check ŌĆö index 0 keeps its exact existing id/behaviour, index Ōēź1 gets its own id and its own pan/zoom state, reading/writing that Place's own storage; selection `type` stays uniformly `'image-holder'` for every Place (only `id` varies) so Context Panel's existing dispatch needed zero changes to its own routing logic. `js/pageRuntime.js`'s `selectionIsValid()` generalized from an exact `'image-holder'` string match to also accept any `'image-place-N'` id. **Object Strip** (`js/objectStrip.js`): one card per Place ŌĆö Place 1 keeps its exact existing "Artwork"/"Artwork Place" wording; extra Places show the Builder-authored Place `name` (e.g. "Place 2") or fall back to "Artwork Place N". **Context Panel + Card Designer**: `_currentPlaceId()` (undefined for Place 1, the id string otherwise) threads through `_applyImageResult`/`_replaceArtwork`/`_cropRotateArtwork` and through `_ensureView`/`_setMode`/`_setScale`/`_setImageProp`/the offset sliders/every reset, so Fit/Fill/Original + BiggerŌåöSmaller/Move controls edit exactly the selected Place and never bleed into another. **Deliberately scoped, disclosed limitations, not silently expanded**: `tools/world-builder/` (v1) is untouched ŌĆö this is `tools/world-builder-v2/`-only, matching where all new Builder capability has landed this session; `js/pageDesigner.js`'s own older, largely-superseded per-role Image manager stays Place-1-only (Context Panel already covers every role's Replace/Crop/Frame needs); only Place 1 gets composition-aware caption placement (`_captionRectFor`'s `'right'`/Wide-layout behaviour) and only Place 1 renders `'frame'/'holder'/'element'`-scoped Layer Pack content (Museum Caption/Wax Seal-style entries) ŌĆö extra Places never get a caption or Layer Pack content, since Builder V2's own compiled Scene Layers never target those three scopes anyway (confirmed: always `'slide'`/`'overlay'`), so this is a narrow, pre-existing non-gap, not a regression; Frame Look/Frame Style/Artwork Presentation's `WorkspaceBuilder`-driven theme controls stay Place-1-only for now, a disclosed, bounded follow-up. WYSIWYE holds for free ŌĆö Thumbnail/Publish Studio/PDF export/Story Destinations all resolve through the identical `SlideRenderer.buildPayload`+`.render()` pair the editor canvas uses, so every Place renders correctly on every surface with zero code changes there; `buildPayload()` gained one line forwarding `slide._placeImages` onto the payload as `placeImages`. Verified end-to-end via a new Playwright test (`multi_place_test.js`, scratch-only): built a real Dual Holder Scene with two DIFFERENT Frame Variations (distinct border colours) through the real `ProjectCompiler`, imported the compiled package into real Studio, and drove the real Change-Look UI to switch onto it ŌĆö confirmed both Places render at pixel-distinct, non-overlapping rects with their own distinct picture colours AND distinct frame border colours (pixel-sampled, not merely inspected); Object Strip shows exactly 2 independently-selectable Place cards; Card Designer's Fit-mode toggle edits only the selected Place; a full `serialize()`ŌåÆ`deserialize()` round trip and a `PageOps.duplicatePage()` both carry every Place's picture over correctly; and the theme's OTHER, single-Place "first" Scene ŌĆö captured before any multi-Place switching ever happens on that session ŌĆö still resolves `holderCount===1`/`placeRectCount===1`, confirming zero behaviour change for the single-Place case. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (23 scripts) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors.)

- Scene Viewport ŌĆö the Page Itself Honours a Scene's Aspect Ratio (a direct, explicit follow-up: after shipping Multiple Artwork Places Per Page, the user confirmed the "portrait page shape" limitation that entry's own investigation had disclosed and deliberately left untouched was itself the next thing to fix ŌĆö "we need to honour the commitments of builder." Until now, `renderer/slideRenderer.js` drew every page onto a fixed, module-level 1080├Ś1350 logical canvas no matter what Aspect Ratio a Scene declared ŌĆö a Layout's resolved aspect only changed the *inner* picture-panel rect's shape, never the outer page/canvas shape itself (`getCanvasSize()` always returned `{w:1080,h:1350}`). Planned via Plan Mode as a genuine architecture change (touches rendering, hit-testing, thumbnails, CSS); scope narrowed to **editor/page canvas shape only** after an `AskUserQuestion` call failed with a transient tool error twice ŌĆö proceeded with the lower-risk default per this project's own established precedent, disclosing it rather than blocking: Publish/Export (`js/storyDestinations.js`/`js/publishStudio.js`/`js/pdfWriter.js`) keep their own fixed destination formats (Instagram Portrait/Square, PDF) completely unchanged, since those are a deliberate, separate destination-format menu ŌĆö zero edits to those three files. **A real naming-forward-compatibility note, raised directly by the user before implementation began**: rather than name the new machinery around "canvas size"/"aspect ratio" specifically, every new construct is named around a general **Scene Viewport** concept ŌĆö the resolved on-screen area a Slide's own content actually occupies ŌĆö so this stays compatible with whatever a future generalized presentation-surface investigation lands on, without this vocabulary needing to change again; the pre-existing public `getCanvasSize(s)` keeps its exact name/signature (real callers in `js/app.js`/`js/thumbnails.js` today) but is now a thin wrapper over the new `_sceneViewportFor(s)` resolver. **Design**: a new `SCENE_VIEWPORT_BY_ASPECT` table (mirroring World Builder v2's own real `ASPECT_RATIOS` pixel values from `engineSchema.js` ŌĆö `landscape:1350├Ś1080`, `wide:1600├Ś900`, `'full-bleed':1080├Ś1920`, `portrait`/`quote` unchanged at `1080├Ś1350`) resolves through the same `_resolvedAspectKey(s)` helper `_resolveLayout` already uses internally (extracted so the two tables can never disagree on a slide's aspect), explicitly gated on `SceneEngine.getRenderData(s)!==null` ŌĆö Cover/Hook/End Scene-blueprint pages always get the portrait default regardless of what the active theme's own Layouts contain, a stronger guard than merely checking `slide.metadata.layout` is unset, since `_resolveLayout` was already found (during investigation) to silently fall back to the theme's `layouts[0]` for these pages too. Module-level `_viewportW`/`_viewportH` replace the old fixed `W`/`H` constants throughout the ~28 drawing-code call sites that referenced them (background fill, Layer Pack full-slide rects, safe-area guide, story-text centering, `_drawHandle`/`_drawFooter`/`_drawPageNumber` anchors); two sites needed more than a rename ŌĆö `STORY_MAX_WIDTH` moved from a module-parse-time constant (which would have permanently cached the very first viewport ever seen) to a value computed fresh inside `_drawStoryText` on every call, and `_drawFooter`/`_drawPageNumber`'s baked-in bottom-anchor literals (`1285`, `1325`, `900`) were converted to their real `_viewportH-65`/`_viewportH-25`/`_viewportW-180` relationships so they scale correctly on a non-portrait page instead of anchoring to the old fixed page height/width. `init(cv,opts)`/`render(s)` cooperate via a new per-canvas-element sticky flag (`cv.__vihuAdaptiveViewport`, set only by `opts.adaptiveViewport`) rather than any new shared module state or call-site parameter: only `js/app.js`'s boot-time `SlideRenderer.init(previewCanvas,{adaptiveViewport:true})` and (see below) `js/thumbnails.js`'s own temp canvas ever opt in; every one of Publish's own throwaway export canvases (`js/storyDestinations.js`, `js/publishStudio.js`) never passes this option and their own canvas elements never carry a prior stamp, so `render()`'s new resize branch is never entered for them ŌĆö **zero code changes needed in those files**, confirmed by tracing every `init()`/`render()` call site in each before implementation. `LAYOUT_RECT`'s `landscape` entry was re-authored to fit sensibly inside its own now-genuinely-wide 1350├Ś1080 canvas (previously just a narrow placement rect inside an always-portrait page); a real, previously-dormant discrepancy was also fixed while touching this table ŌĆö `LAYOUT_RECT['full-bleed']` had been authored assuming a portrait-shaped canvas (`{0,0,1080,1350}`) though World Builder's own `full-bleed` aspect is actually 1080├Ś1920, a landmine no live theme had ever reached (Museum Gallery is explicitly trimmed to Landscape/Portrait/Quote only) ŌĆö corrected to match. **A real bug found and fixed while wiring `js/thumbnails.js`, not assumed away**: the plan's original intent ("thumbnails.js already presizes manually, no opt-in flag needed") turned out to be wrong once traced through `init()`'s actual mechanics ŌĆö `init()` has *always* unconditionally reset the canvas's backing-store size to the current default the instant it's called, regardless of whatever a caller manually presized the element to immediately beforehand (true in the original code too, just invisible there since `getCanvasSize()` with no argument was always the same fixed value anyway) ŌĆö so a literal reading of the plan would have had `init()` silently clobber `thumbnails.js`'s own manual presize back to portrait on every call. Fixed by having `js/thumbnails.js`'s temp canvas *also* opt into `adaptiveViewport`, letting `render()`'s own resolution step size it correctly instead, exactly mirroring the live editor canvas's own mechanism ŌĆö the downstream thumbnail-downscale math (already reading `temp.width`/`temp.height` *after* render, not before) needed no further change. Also added one small, self-contained `MutationObserver` in `js/app.js` (watching `.publish-studio-modal`'s `class` attribute) to resync the live editor canvas the instant Publish Studio's modal actually closes ŌĆö a real gap found during investigation: Publish's own internal `init(editorCanvas)` "restore" call, made mid-export-loop, resets the canvas without ever re-rendering it, so a Scene-Viewport-resized live canvas could otherwise show a stretched/cropped page until the user's next unrelated interaction. **Backward compatibility, verified not merely asserted**: every existing `getCanvasSize()` caller (no argument) gets the byte-identical `{w:1080,h:1350}`; every theme with no `layouts`, and every Cover/Hook/End page regardless of theme, resolves to the portrait default; every existing `init(cv)`/`init(cv,{dpr:...})` call site in the three untouched Publish files resets to the exact canonical size it always has, since none of them ever pass `adaptiveViewport` and none of their (always brand-new) canvas elements ever carry a prior stamp. Verified end-to-end via a new Playwright test (`scene_viewport_test.js`, scratch-only): built a real Landscape Dual Holder Scene through the real `ProjectCompiler`, imported the compiled package into real Studio, and confirmed the live `previewCanvas` genuinely resizes to 1350├Ś1080 (not just an inner rect) with the correct inline `style.aspectRatio` set; both authored Places render at pixel-distinct, non-overlapping rects within the new wide canvas; a synthetic Cover-role page (real `SceneEngine` blueprint + `metadata.scene`) stays fixed at 1080├Ś1350 regardless of the active theme's own Layouts; and switching back to the theme's other, single-Place portrait Scene reverts the canvas to exactly 1080├Ś1350. **A real, pre-existing test-fixture bug was found and fixed in the same pass, not a product regression**: re-running the full existing regression suite surfaced `multi_place_test.js` failing ŌĆö traced to that script's own pixel-sampler hardcoding `canvas.width/1080`/`canvas.height/1350` as its DPR-scale-factor divisor, an assumption that quietly broke now that a landscape page's logical size is genuinely 1350├Ś1080; fixed by having it read `SlideRenderer.getCanvasSize(slide)` dynamically instead, the same pattern `scene_viewport_test.js` already used correctly. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (24 scripts, including the corrected `multi_place_test.js`) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors ŌĆö no Theme Contract/Scene Model/Builder change; the fix is confined to `renderer/slideRenderer.js`, `js/app.js`, and `js/thumbnails.js`.)

- Frame Look / Frame Style / Frame Variation Now Respect the Selected Place (a real, user-reported bug found hands-on testing the Multiple Artwork Places Per Page feature: "i selected first place and tried to give it round frame it was success. i selected second place tried to give it poloroid frame it applied to first place." This was the exact, disclosed scope gap that feature's own ship note named and deliberately deferred ŌĆö "Frame Look/Frame Style/Artwork Presentation's `WorkspaceBuilder`-driven theme controls stay Place-1-only for now, a disclosed, bounded follow-up" ŌĆö now closed. **Root cause confirmed by reading both sides of the pipeline**: the RENDER side (`renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_resolveBorder`/`_cardArtworkOverride`/`_resolveArtworkFields`) already fully supported a per-Place border/artwork override at `slide.metadata.placeContent[placeId].cardOverrides.border`/`.artwork`, built for this feature from day one ŌĆö but the WRITE side never used it: `js/cardDesigner.js`'s Frame Look preset buttons (`_applyFrameDesign`, e.g. Rounded/Polaroid) and every Frame Style slider/chip/toggle (`_ensureBorder`/`_readBorder`/`_pruneBorder`/`_commitBorder`/`_resetBorder`) always read/wrote the page-level `slide.metadata.cardOverrides.border` regardless of which Place was actually selected, and `js/workspaceBuilder.js`'s Artwork Presentation controls (Frame Variation swatches, Presentation/Frame/Lighting/Caption/Paper/Mat dropdowns, all built on `_ensureArtwork`/`_readArtwork`) had the identical gap against `slide.metadata.cardOverrides.artwork` ŌĆö so no matter which Place was selected on screen, every one of these controls always edited Place 1's storage, and the renderer then correctly-but-misleadingly painted whatever Place 1 now held. **Fix, mirroring the exact `_ensureView`/`_readView` per-Place convention `js/cardDesigner.js`'s own Fit/Fill/Scale/Offset controls already used successfully**: `_ensureBorder`/`_readBorder`/`_pruneBorder`/`_resetBorder`/`_applyFrameDesign` all gained an optional `placeId` parameter ŌĆö omitted (Place 1) is byte-identical to before; a real id reads/writes that Place's own bag under `slide.metadata.placeContent[placeId].cardOverrides.border` instead, reusing the pre-existing `_placeViewBag` helper. `_commitBorder`/`_refreshBorder` now resolve `_currentPlaceId()` themselves, and `_refreshBorder`'s `hasImage` gate was corrected to check the SELECTED Place's own picture (mirroring `_refreshImage`'s already-correct per-Place `hasImage` logic) rather than always Place 1's `s.image`. `js/workspaceBuilder.js`'s `_ensureArtwork`/`_readArtwork` gained the identical optional `placeId` parameter, and `_buildSelectRow`/`_buildSwatchRow`'s default get/set now read it off a new `ctx.getPlaceId` callback (mirroring the existing `ctx.getSlide`/`ctx.onChange` convention) rather than hardcoding Place 1 ŌĆö every one of `js/cardDesigner.js`'s four call sites building that `ctx` object (`_buildImageControls`'s initial "Artwork Presentation" build, `_buildBorderControls`'s initial "Frame Style" build, and both rebuilt in `_refreshFrameWorkspace` on every refresh) now passes `getPlaceId:_currentPlaceId` alongside. A control whose data doesn't live in the artwork bag (Layout, via its own explicit `store` override) is unaffected, since `store.get`/`store.set` bypass the default entirely. Verified via a new Playwright test (`frame_look_place_test.js`, scratch-only) reproducing the exact reported sequence end-to-end against a real Dual Holder Scene built through the real `ProjectCompiler` and imported into real Studio: selecting Place 1 and applying "Rounded" lands only on Place 1; selecting Place 2 and applying "Polaroid" lands only on Place 2 while Place 1's own Rounded design is confirmed unchanged (the exact bug scenario, now passing); a Frame Style slider (Round Corners) edits only the selected Place, with re-selecting Place 1 afterward confirming its own panel shows its own stored value, never Place 2's just-applied one. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (24 scripts) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors ŌĆö no Theme Contract/Scene Model/Builder change; the fix is confined to `js/cardDesigner.js` and `js/workspaceBuilder.js`.)

- Frame Variation Seeding Now Re-Seeds Correctly on Every Representation Switch (a second, real, user-reported bug found in the same "authored two Frames" testing pass: "when i authored in builder i gave white and red borders to each frame ... it did not come to the creator." Investigated by reproducing the exact scenario rather than guessing ŌĆö a Dual-Holder Scene's two Places DID both resolve correctly (confirmed via pixel-sampling: a genuinely white border is simply invisible against the near-white default wall/mat tone, not a bug), but the real defect surfaced in the OTHER common authoring shape: two separate single-Place Scenes/Representations, each with its own distinct Frame (white / red), switched between via "Change Look." **Root cause**: `js/creationFlow.js`'s `_seedDefaultFrameVariation()` writes a Representation's authored `defaultFrame` onto the page's `slide.metadata.cardOverrides.artwork.frameVariation` ŌĆö but only the FIRST time, guarded by `if(slide.metadata.cardOverrides.artwork.frameVariation) return; // never clobber a Story Author's own choice`. That guard can't tell an auto-seeded value apart from a genuine Story Author pick in Card Designer ŌĆö both are just a plain string ŌĆö so once the FIRST Representation ever seen had seeded its own Frame, every LATER Representation's own distinct Frame became permanently unreachable: the border stayed stuck on whichever Scene was seen first, exactly reading as "the border I gave the second Frame did not come to the Creator." **Fix**: a companion `_seededFrameVariation` field now travels alongside `frameVariation` in the same artwork bag, recording what THIS function itself last wrote; re-seeding is refused only when the current value has drifted from that recorded value ŌĆö meaning a Story Author genuinely picked something different via Card Designer in between ŌĆö so switching Representations any number of times correctly re-seeds each one's own Frame, while a real manual pick is still never clobbered. Verified via two new Playwright tests (`frame_color_repro2.js`/`frame_color_repro3.js`, scratch-only): the exact reported white/red two-Representation sequence, confirmed broken before the fix (`frameVariation` stuck on `"classic-white"` after switching to the Red Representation) and fixed after; a three-Representation whiteŌåÆredŌåÆblue sequence confirming re-seeding isn't a one-shot fix, with each switch's own border colour pixel-sampled and confirmed correct; and a direct manual-pick-preservation check confirming a genuine Story Author override survives a later Representation switch untouched. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (24 scripts, including the earlier Frame Look/Style per-Place fix's own test) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors ŌĆö the fix is confined to one function in `js/creationFlow.js`, no Theme Contract/Scene Model/Builder change.)

- Scene Compile Order Now Respects "Reorder Scenes" Instead of Raw Creation Order (a real, user-reported bug found from a side-by-side screenshot comparison: the World Builder v2 Scenes Library showed the authored order First ŌåÆ Single Holder ŌåÆ Single Holder ŌåÆ second (the user had drag-reordered "second," originally created early ŌĆö hence its name ŌĆö down to the end via "Reorder Scenes"), but Creator's "Choose a Page Style" showed First ŌåÆ second ŌåÆ Single Holder ŌåÆ Single Holder instead, with "second" back in its ORIGINAL creation-order position. **Root cause**: `tools/world-builder-v2/js/services/builder.js`'s `convergeScenes()` iterates `projectLoader.getFilesInFolder('scenes')` directly, and that array is built by `js/projectCompiler.js`'s `loadIntoProjectLoader()` from `Object.keys(project.files)` ŌĆö plain JS object key insertion order, i.e. the order each Scene file was first CREATED, completely bypassing `project.sceneOrder` (the array "Reorder Scenes"'s drag-and-drop, backed by `ProjectModel.moveScene`, actually writes to, and which `ProjectModel.scenes(project)` already correctly resolves everywhere else in the Builder UI). Since `builder.js`/`projectLoader` only ever see raw file Blobs ŌĆö never the live `project` object with its own `sceneOrder` ŌĆö the compiled Representation order silently reverted to creation order the moment a reordered World was Built, independent of anything in the Frame/Frame-Variation fixes shipped earlier this session. **Fix**: `loadIntoProjectLoader()` (the one adapter boundary that DOES still see the full, live `project` object) now re-sorts `folders.scenes` to match `ProjectModel.scenes(project)`'s own authored order immediately after building it from raw paths ŌĆö a single, additive `.sort()` keyed off each path's own scene id looked up against `ProjectModel.scenes(project).map(s => s.id)`, touching nothing else in the frozen `builder.js` service. Applied identically to both `tools/world-builder-v2/` and its `tools/world-builder/` (v1) twin, which carries the identical `convergeScenes()`/`loadIntoProjectLoader()` code and was found to have the exact same bug. Verified via a new Playwright reproduction (scratch-only) creating four Scenes in File-insertion order First/second/Single-Holder/Single-Holder, then calling the real `ProjectModel.moveScene()` (the same function "Reorder Scenes" drag-and-drop calls) to push "second" to the end ŌĆö confirmed the compiled `theme.representations` order matched raw creation order (bug reproduced) before the fix, and matched the reordered Scenes Library display (First/Single-Holder/Single-Holder/second) after it, for both Builders. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (including this session's own Frame Look/Style and Frame Variation reseed fixes, sticker-drag, and Object-Strip-reorder tests) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors ŌĆö no Theme Contract/Scene Model change; the fix is confined to one function in each Builder's `js/projectCompiler.js`.)

- Clicking an Empty Artwork Place Now Selects It Instead of Deselecting Everything (a real, user-reported bug flagged earlier this session and now fixed: "in creator clicks between place 1 and 2 are not being managed properly." **Root cause**: `js/app.js`'s canvas mousedown handler only ever called `_setSelectedSceneElement(_placeHit.id,'image-holder')` *inside* the same `if(_placeHit && _placeImageFor(s,_placeHit.id) && ...)` guard that also starts the image-pan gesture ŌĆö so selecting a Place was accidentally coupled to that Place already having a picture. Clicking an empty Place's placeholder box fell straight through to the "clicked empty space" branch at the bottom of the handler, which actively **deselected** whatever was selected instead of selecting the empty Place ŌĆö pre-existing legacy behaviour for Place 1 too (an unfilled Place 1 was equally unclickable before Multiple Places existed), just far more noticeable once a page has several visually-identical empty boxes side by side (exactly the scenario in the user's own screenshots). **Fix**: split "select the Place" from "start a pan gesture" ŌĆö `_setSelectedSceneElement` now fires for ANY real Place hit-test result, regardless of whether it has a picture yet (Story-role pages have no SceneEngine element for the picture, so this click is the only real target Context Panel/Object Strip can key "Artwork selected"/"Add Artwork" off); the pan gesture itself still only starts once that Place actually has an image to pan, exactly as before. Verified via a new Playwright test (`empty_place_click_test.js`, scratch-only) against a real Dual Holder Scene with NO pictures uploaded at all: clicking empty Place 1's placeholder now correctly selects `image-holder` (was previously a no-op/deselect), clicking empty Place 2's placeholder correctly selects `image-place-2`, Context Panel correctly shows "­¤¢╝’ĖÅ Add Artwork" for the selected empty Place, and clicking genuine empty canvas background still correctly deselects (unaffected). Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (26 scripts) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors ŌĆö the fix is confined to one `if` block in `js/app.js`.)

- A Place With No Frame Chosen Now Renders With Zero Chrome, Matching Builder's Own Preview (investigated a real, user-supplied screenshot pair: Builder's Working View showing a nicely-framed artwork placeholder for a Scene with two Places, vs. Creator showing the same Scene as two plain flat white boxes. **Root cause, confirmed via debug instrumentation on a real compiled package, not guessed**: both Places had no Frame Variation assigned (`holder.frame:null`), and `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_resolveArtworkFields`/`_artworkBorder` always fell back to the World's own top-level `presentation:'gallery'` preset's System Default look (white background, white-mat frame, soft shadow, gallery lighting) for ANY un-Framed Place ŌĆö correct per the Theme Language v2 architecture (Presentation Preset ŌåÆ Theme Overrides ŌåÆ System Defaults, Sprint 9.5), and confirmed to have zero visual effect on Museum Gallery's real, on-disk `.vtheme` (both its Showcase and Portrait Representations set a real `defaultFrame:'classic-white'`, so every real Place there already has explicit chrome; only Quote has `defaultFrame:null`, and Quote's composition skips the Frame/border pipeline entirely regardless) ŌĆö but confirmed via a direct product decision (asked, not assumed) to be the wrong behaviour for a Place the Theme Author deliberately left un-Framed: "builder preview is correct. creator is wrong," applied "everywhere" per explicit follow-up. **Fix**: `_resolveArtworkFields` now computes one additive flag, `_hasExplicitChrome` ŌĆö true when a Frame Variation resolves for this Place (`holder.frame`/a Story Author's own per-card pick) OR the Story Author made a manual per-card Presentation override via Card Designer's own Presentation/Frame/Lighting/Composition controls (Sprint 9.4); false when neither is true. `_artworkBorder` returns a genuine zero-chrome object (`fill:'none'`, `lineEnabled:false`, `shadowEnabled:false`, `design:null`, `_artwork:{}` so `_drawArtworkPresentation`'s paper/lighting checks and `_drawArtworkCaption`'s own gate all correctly no-op too) whenever `_hasExplicitChrome` is false, instead of resolving through `ThemePresets.resolveHolder`. `_resolveWallTone` is a deliberately separate resolution path (the gallery wall colour is a Slide-level concept independent of any one Place's own Frame choice, Sprint 9.7) and stays completely unaffected ŌĆö a Scene's own wall tone/Scene-hosted background now correctly shows THROUGH an un-Framed Place instead of being covered by a fabricated white mat. Verified via Playwright: a real Dual-Holder Scene with a navy Scene-hosted background and no Frame assigned to either Place now shows the navy correctly through both Place areas (previously solid opaque white, confirmed via before/after pixel sampling); Museum Gallery's real `classic-white` Frame Variation still renders its white border chrome pixel-exact, completely unaffected. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (29 scripts) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors ŌĆö the fix is confined to two functions in `renderer/slideRenderer.js`, no Theme Contract/Scene Model/Builder change.)

- Zero-Chrome Fix Was Being Defeated By a Dangling Frame Variation Reference (a direct, same-day follow-up: the user reported still seeing solid white Artwork Place boxes on their real "My shapes" World after the fix above shipped ŌĆö confirmed deployed via the visible build-info footer, ruling out a stale deployment. **Root-caused by walking the user through a live browser-console dump of their real project's `slide.metadata`, not by guessing further**: `slide.metadata.cardOverrides.artwork.frameVariation` was the string `"classic"`, but the active theme's `frameVariations` was `null` ŌĆö a stale, dangling seed from an earlier Builder state (a Frame the Theme Author has since renamed or removed) that survived on this already-existing Creator project. The previous fix's `_hasExplicitChrome` flag only checked whether *some* `frameVariation` id string was present (`!!frameVariationId`), never whether it actually resolved to a real entry in `theme.frameVariations` ŌĆö so a dangling reference kept tricking Creator into treating the Place as "explicitly Framed" and falling back to the Presentation Preset's white System Default, exactly reproducing the reported symptom. **Fix**: `_resolveArtworkFields` now tracks whether the Frame Variation lookup genuinely found a matching entry with real `fields` (`frameVariationResolved`) and bases `_hasExplicitChrome` on that instead of the bare id string's truthiness ŌĆö a stale/unresolvable reference now correctly falls through to zero chrome, matching a Place that never had a Frame Variation at all. Verified by reproducing the user's exact real-project state (a real Build via `ProjectCompiler`, then stripping `frameVariations` off the live theme record and seeding the identical dangling `frameVariation:'classic'` reference onto the slide): Place 1's edge pixel now reads the theme's wall tone (`234,231,226`), not solid white (`255,255,255`). Re-verified the prior fix's own navy Scene-background scenario and Museum Gallery's real `classic-white` Frame Variation are both still correct and unaffected. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors ŌĆö the fix is confined to `_resolveArtworkFields` in `renderer/slideRenderer.js`.)

- Real Root Cause Found: Theme Was Applied to the Story Slot, Not the Artwork Slot (the genuine root cause behind the persistent white-box report, found via a live browser-console diagnostic ŌĆö a temporary `SlideRenderer.debugResolveBorder` export ŌĆö rather than further speculation. **Root cause**: `AppState.project.artworkTheme` was `null` on the user's real project, even though the Layout/Holder/Place/Frame-Variation geometry rendered correctly. Both are explained by the same fact: the World's theme had been applied into the **Story Theme slot** (`AppState.project.theme`), not the **Artwork Theme slot**. `_resolveBorder`/`_resolveWallTone` required `_artworkTheme(s)` (which only ever reads the Artwork Theme slot) to be non-null, found nothing, and fell straight through to the legacy `_drawPanel(t.panel.color,...)` fallback ŌĆö painting the Story Theme's plain white/cream panel colour regardless of any earlier fix, since every one of those fixes lived inside the `_artworkTheme(s)` branch that never ran for this project. Layout/Holder/Place geometry rendered correctly anyway because `_activeLayoutHolders`/`_resolveLayout` already resolve through `_layoutTheme(s)`, which tries the Artwork Theme slot first and falls back to the Story Theme slot ŌĆö exactly the fallback the chrome-resolution functions were missing. **Fix**: `_resolveBorder` (both the per-Place and Place-1 branches) and `_resolveWallTone` now use that same `_layoutTheme(s)` fallback instead of `_artworkTheme(s)` directly ŌĆö whichever theme actually supplies Layout/Holder/Frame-Variation data now also supplies its own Frame chrome, consistent with what the rest of the Place system already does; for the normal case (a theme correctly applied via the Artwork Theme slot), `_layoutTheme(s)` prefers that real Artwork Theme first, so behaviour is byte-identical to before. Verified via Playwright by reproducing the exact real condition (`AppState.project.artworkTheme` forced `null`, `AppState.project.theme` pointing at the Layout/Holder/Frame-Variation-bearing theme): Place edge pixels now read the wall tone (`234,231,226`), not solid white (`255,255,255`). Re-verified Museum Gallery (correctly applied via the Artwork Theme slot) still renders its `classic-white` Frame Variation pixel-exact and unaffected, plus every prior fix's own reproduction (navy Scene background, dangling Frame Variation reference) still passes. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors ŌĆö the fix is confined to `_resolveBorder`/`_resolveWallTone` in `renderer/slideRenderer.js`. The temporary `SlideRenderer.debugResolveBorder` diagnostic export added to chase this down is deliberately left in place as a small, permanent, non-invasive debugging aid rather than removed, since it has no behavioural effect on any real render path.)

- Guardrails ŌĆö Artwork Places Become Moveable + Fully Reorderable (closes a real Builder-to-Creator wiring gap: World Builder's own per-Place permission block ŌĆö "Can a Story Author move this?" / "...change this? (its Frame, once populated)" / "...see this at all?" ŌĆö wrote correctly to `holder.permissions`, but `convergeScene` (`tools/world-builder-v2/js/services/builder.js`) never read it at all when compiling `placeRects`, sitting right next to `convergeSceneLayer`'s own proven `visible`/`moveable`/`editable` derivation for Scene Layers, which does exactly this correctly. **Fix**: `placeRects` now carries `visible`/`moveable`/`editable` per Place, mirroring `convergeSceneLayer`'s exact pattern (absent `permissions` ŌåÆ `true` at compile time, matching what `_ensureHolderDefaults` already stamps onto a live Holder). **Backward-compatible default asymmetry**: Creator's own render-time default for an ALREADY-compiled Layout is the OPPOSITE ŌĆö absent `moveable`/`editable` ŌåÆ `false`/locked, absent `visible` ŌåÆ `true` ŌĆö so every theme published before this fix (including Museum Gallery) keeps rendering exactly as before; `SlideRenderer.getPlacePermissions(s,placeId)`/`_resolvePlacePermissions` is the one shared resolver both the render path and Object Strip read, so the two can never disagree. Per the user's own explicit scope choices (confirmed via AskUserQuestion): **(1) a small grab-handle** appears on a selected, moveable Place (`_drawPlaceGrabHandle`/`getPlaceGrabHandleHitbox`) ŌĆö dragging it writes a new position into the exact same generic `slide.metadata.elementOverrides` bag every other draggable object already uses (`SceneEngine.setPosition`, reused verbatim via `js/app.js`'s existing `_sceneDragState` machinery), completely independent of the pre-existing content-pan gesture (which still pans/zooms the picture itself); `_placePixelRectFor`'s three call sites (`_place1Rect`, the Place-N branch, `getPlaceRects`) all resolve through a new `_applyPlaceMoveOverride` so a moved Place's rect shifts everywhere consistently. **(2) Full cross-object reorder**: every Story-role page now ALWAYS uses the fully-interleaved merged pass (`_naturalStoryOrder`/`_applyOrderOverride`, previously only when `_noFramePipeline` ŌĆö Quote/zero-Holder) so a Place, a Sticker, and a World-owned `slide`/`overlay` Layer Pack object can all be freely reordered together via Object Strip drag ŌĆö not just Places among themselves;
