Cover/Hook/End pages (which never have Places) are completely unaffected, still using the merged pass only when `_noFramePipeline`, exactly as before. `_mergedReorderableIds()` gates a Place's own reorder-membership on its `moveable` flag specifically (unlike a locked Scene element/Sticker, which stays reorderable even while position-frozen) ŌĆö matching the real bug report's own framing that "move" and "reorder" are the same guardrail for a Place. `js/objectStrip.js`'s Place-card loop gained real `id`/`draggable` wiring reusing the existing `_wireReorderDrag`/lock-badge machinery verbatim, plus a `visible:false` Place skip; a genuine duplicate-card bug (Places now living in the render tree for reorder purposes were ALSO being picked up by Object Strip's separate generic "every other object" loop) was found and fixed by excluding `isPlace`-marked entries there. **Two real, separate bugs found and fixed while verifying, not the feature itself**: (1) `js/app.js`'s `_canvasCoords` called `SlideRenderer.getCanvasSize()` with no slide argument, always resolving the portrait default regardless of a page's real Aspect Ratio ŌĆö every mouse hit-test on a non-portrait Scene was silently computed against the wrong logical size; fixed by passing the current slide through, exactly the same class of fix `js/thumbnails.js` already got in the Scene Viewport sprint. (2) A regression caught by full regression testing before shipping: the first cut of `_naturalStoryOrder`'s Place-inclusion logic required a real, populated `placeRects` array to include ANY Place at all ŌĆö since every theme compiled before Multiple Artwork Places Per Page (every theme today except a freshly multi-Place-authored one, including Museum Gallery) has no `placeRects` array, this silently dropped Place 1 ŌĆö and with it, Museum Gallery's own Frame-scoped Wax Seal/Museum Caption Layer Pack content, which only ever draws as part of Place 1's own atomic paint step ŌĆö from rendering AND from Object Strip entirely; fixed by treating an absent/empty `placeRects` as exactly one implicit Place (`place:null`), matching the identical convention `getPlaceRects`'s own fallback already establishes elsewhere in this file. `_supportsResize`/`getResizeHandlesFor` exclude Places outright (`isPlace`) rather than inheriting the generic 8-corner resize handles a Scene blueprint's own `image-holder` type would otherwise trigger, since no size-override read exists anywhere for Places today and showing them would silently do nothing. `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md`'s `placeRects` field table documents the three new fields and the compile/render default asymmetry. Verified via a new 7-assertion Playwright suite (permission resolution including the legacy-absent case; Object Strip lock-badge/draggable state per Place; a moveable Place and a Sticker sharing the same reorder bucket and a real cross-object drag changing their resolved order; grab-handle hitbox gating; a real mouse-driven drag repositioning a Place by the expected canvas-logical delta; a `visible:false` Place skipped from rendering/Object Strip/reorder entirely) plus full regression across the existing 31-script Creator/Builder Playwright suite (one script, `world_shape_reorder_test.js`, had its own bucket assertions intentionally updated ŌĆö a Sticker and a World-owned Shape on any Story-role page now correctly share one "merged" bucket instead of the narrower "earlier"/"story" split that predates this feature, not a regression) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites, all passing unchanged, zero console errors.)

- Governing Rules Compliance Pass ŌĆö Single-Place Geometry + Frame-Editable Guardrail (a direct, evidence-based follow-up to the Guardrails sprint above. After that sprint shipped, the user stated three permanent governing rules for the whole platform: **(1)** "When Scene shows up in Creator it is exactly as it was in Builder." **(2)** "Every object on Scene honors the guardrails." **(3)** "Creator can further refine the objects through options available in the right panel." A requested compliance audit (`three_rules_audit.js`) found two real, confirmed violations, both fixed here; a third check (World-owned Decoration guardrails) confirmed no regression. **Violation 1 (Rule 1)**: a single authored Place (not part of a Dual-Holder layout) had its Builder-authored fractional position/size silently discarded in favour of the full panel rect ŌĆö a deliberate design decision made mid-implementation during the Multiple Artwork Places Per Page feature, reasoned (at the time) that "a lone authored Place's own fraction has no reliable 1:1 correspondence to Engine V1's already-caption-aware panelRect." Under Rule 1 this reasoning no longer holds ŌĆö Creator must show the Scene exactly as Builder shows it, for one Place same as for several. **Fixed** in `renderer/slideRenderer.js`: `_place1Rect`'s and `getPlaceRects(s)`'s gating condition changed from "subdivide Place 1 only when 2+ Places are authored" to "subdivide Place 1 whenever ANY real `placeRects` array exists (lengthŌēź1)" ŌĆö the full-panel fallback now applies ONLY when a Layout authors zero Places at all (no `placeRects` array ŌĆö the true legacy/implicit case, e.g. Museum Gallery, completely unaffected). **Violation 2 (Rules 2/3)**: World Builder's own "Can a Story Author change this? (its Frame, once populated)" guardrail (`holder.permissions.editable`, compiled into `placeRects` by the prior sprint) had zero effect in Creator ŌĆö Card Designer's Frame Look preset buttons and every Frame Style slider/toggle/chip stayed fully interactive regardless of this flag, since nothing in `js/cardDesigner.js` had ever been wired to read it. **Fixed**: a new `_currentPlaceEditable()` helper resolves `SlideRenderer.getPlacePermissions(slide, _currentPlaceId()||'image-holder').editable` (translating Card Designer's own `undefined`-for-Place-1 convention to the real `'image-holder'` id first); `_refreshFrameWorkspace()` now disables every `.frame-design-btn` (Frame Look) and shows a plain "This Place's Frame was set by the World and can't be changed here" note when locked; `_refreshBorder()` folds `!editable` into its existing `!hasImage`-disables-controls pattern for every Frame Style padding/radius/line-width/shadow slider, fill chip, and toggle; `_applyFrameDesign()` gained a defensive early-return guard for any non-UI caller. **A real, deliberate correction to the render-time default asymmetry, not just a rewire**: `_resolvePlacePermissions`'s `editable` field changed from `p.editable===true` (absentŌåÆlocked) to `p.editable!==false` (absentŌåÆeditable) ŌĆö the OPPOSITE default from `moveable`, and a deliberate departure from the prior sprint's own "absent always means locked" framing. Reasoned explicitly: `moveable` is a BRAND NEW capability (absent must stay locked, or every pre-existing theme would suddenly gain draggable Places it never had); Frame-editing via Card Designer is a PRE-EXISTING capability that has always been unrestricted for every Place in every theme published before the Guardrails sprint ŌĆö defaulting absent `editable` to `false` would have newly LOCKED Frame-editing platform-wide, a real regression Rule 3 explicitly forbids. Only a Place whose Builder author explicitly unchecked the box (`editable:false`) is now locked. Verified via a re-run of `three_rules_audit.js` (both violations now PASS; the World-owned-Decoration regression check still PASSes unchanged) plus full regression across the existing 28-script Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite, the Guardrails sprint's own 7-assertion `place_guardrails_test.js` (including its own pre-existing "Legacy" absent-permissions fixture), and both `goldenBuild.js` suites ŌĆö all passing unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; the fix is confined to `renderer/slideRenderer.js` and `js/cardDesigner.js`, plus one small CSS addition for the new lock-note.)

- Retro Guardrails Audit ŌĆö the Whole Artwork Presentation Group Now Honours "editable" Too (a direct follow-up requested explicitly as a standing practice ŌĆö "going forward and in retro" ŌĆö after confirming the Governing Rules apply uniformly across object kinds. Auditing the previous fix against Rule 2/3 surfaced a second, real gap the earlier pass hadn't reached: World Builder's "Can a Story Author change this? (its Frame, once populated)" guardrail only ever gated Card Designer's Frame Look preset buttons and Frame Style's fill/border/radius/shadow sliders ŌĆö the separate **Artwork Presentation** subgroup (Frame Variation swatches, plus Presentation/Lighting/Caption/Paper/Mat dropdowns, all built by `js/workspaceBuilder.js`'s `CONTROL_CATALOG` via `_buildSelectRow`/`_buildSwatchRow`/`_buildToggleRow`) had **no editable gating of any kind** ŌĆö a Story Author could still change a locked Place's Frame Variation, Presentation preset, Lighting, or Caption style, bypassing the guardrail entirely. Confirmed the same gap existed one level deeper too: `paper`/`mat` (built by the identical `CONTROL_CATALOG` machinery, just rendered inside the 'frame' panel's Frame Style body rather than 'holder.image') were equally ungated, since `_refreshBorder`'s own direct-selector disabling never touched WorkspaceBuilder-built controls at all. Presented two scope options to the user ŌĆö lock only the two controls literally named "Frame" (Frame Variation + the legacy `artworkFrame` dropdown), or lock the whole Artwork Presentation group together ŌĆö and the user chose the latter: "if a Theme Author says don't let them change this Place's look, nothing about how the picture is framed, lit, captioned, or matted can be touched." **Fix**: `js/workspaceBuilder.js` gained one shared `_isCtxLocked(ctx)` helper (`ctx.getPlaceEditable`, a plain function reference resolved live at every `__sync`, mirroring the existing `ctx.getPlaceId` convention exactly ŌĆö omitted by every non-Place caller, so Layout/Text/Sticker controls are completely unaffected) wired into `_buildSelectRow`/`_buildSwatchRow`/`_buildToggleRow`'s own `__sync` functions, disabling the `<select>`/swatch buttons/checkbox alongside their existing value-sync. `js/cardDesigner.js`'s `_refreshFrameWorkspace()` now passes `getPlaceEditable:_currentPlaceEditable` in both the 'frame' panel's `borderCtx` (covering paper/mat) and the 'holder.image' panel's `ctx` (covering the whole Artwork Presentation group), and the Artwork Presentation subgroup gained its own lock note (sharing the `.frame-editable-lock-note` class with Frame Look's, toggled together by one `querySelectorAll`). New CSS (`.icon-card:disabled`, `.workspace-select:disabled`) gives the newly-disabled swatches/dropdowns a visible locked state, matching the existing `.picture-reset-btn:disabled` convention. Verified via two new Playwright variants (`artwork_presentation_lock_test.js`/`_open_test.js`, a real synthetic theme with an explicit `editor.holder.image` control list and a real Frame Variation, driven with `editable:false` and `editable:true` respectively): every Frame Look button, every Frame Style slider, every Artwork Presentation dropdown, and every Frame Variation swatch is confirmed disabled together when locked and enabled together when open, both lock notes toggle in lockstep, a forced click on a disabled swatch changes nothing, and a real click on an enabled one does. Full regression across the entire existing 31-script Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (including the prior sprint's own `place_guardrails_test.js`/`three_rules_audit.js`/`all_object_guardrails_test.js`) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors ŌĆö no Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; the fix is confined to `js/workspaceBuilder.js` and `js/cardDesigner.js`, plus one small CSS addition.)

- Screen 2 Preview Carousel Renders the Real Center Pane, Not a Static Thumbnail ("can we run the same center pane which is inside Studio here, so that author can actually see what slides a theme contain" ŌĆö the Selected World Preview's carousel (`.creation-flow-carousel-art`) showed only a static `<img>` (a Representation's own authored thumbnail, or the World's Hero Image/icon glyph as a fallback) ŌĆö never the real Frame/Layout/Layer Pack rendering a Story Author would actually get. Fixed by having each carousel slide render through the exact same `SlideRenderer` module the Workspace's own center pane uses ŌĆö a real `<canvas>` replaces the `<img>`, painted via a new `_buildPreviewSlide(theme,representation)` (a synthetic slide mirroring exactly what `_finish()` builds for a real page ŌĆö `_themeType(theme.id)==='artwork'` stamps `slide.artworkTheme`, otherwise `slide.theme`+`slide.artworkTheme=null` ŌĆö plus `_seedDefaultFrameVariation`, reused verbatim) and a new `_renderCarouselCanvas(canvas,theme,representation)` (`SlideRenderer.init(canvas,{dpr:1,adaptiveViewport:true})` + `render()`, wrapped so a failure falls back to the old thumbnail/glyph, never breaking Screen 2). **A real, load-bearing bug found and fixed while wiring this up, not assumed away**: `SlideRenderer.buildPayload(slide,opts)` ŌĆö the shared payload-builder every render surface already uses ŌĆö unconditionally resolves `theme`/`artworkTheme` off the GLOBAL `ThemeEngine` state (`ThemeEngine.resolveTheme()`/`.getActiveArtworkTheme()`), correct for the real live editor slide (which has no per-slide override) but silently ignoring `slide.theme`/`slide.artworkTheme` entirely ŌĆö so a naive `render(buildPayload(slide,...))` call always painted whatever World was already active in the background (or nothing, defaulting to portrait), never the synthetic slide's own theme; confirmed directly by comparing `SlideRenderer.getCanvasSize(slide)` (which DOES honour `slide.artworkTheme`, correct) against the actual rendered canvas size (always default) before writing any fix. Fixed, without touching `buildPayload()` itself or any global `AppState`/`ThemeEngine` state, by overriding `payload.theme`/`payload.artworkTheme` with the synthetic slide's own values (when set) immediately before the one `render(payload)` call this feature makes ŌĆö the one surgical point where a preview can diverge from the global active theme. A second real hazard, mirrored from `js/thumbnails.js`'s/`js/pageOps.js`'s own established pattern: rendering N carousel canvases repoints `SlideRenderer`'s shared module state away from the live editor canvas each time (relevant since Screen 2 can be reached from an already-open Workspace via the header's Home button) ŌĆö closed with a new `_restoreEditorCanvas()`, called once after the whole carousel paints, re-`init()`-ing `#previewCanvas` and calling `window.redrawPreview()` (a no-op before any project exists, the ordinary fresh-boot case). New CSS `.creation-flow-carousel-canvas{object-fit:contain}` (deliberately `contain`, not the `img`'s existing `cover`, so the whole rendered page is visible letterboxed rather than cropped). Verified via two new Playwright suites: a general suite (3 real canvases render with genuine non-blank painted pixels, zero `<img>` fallback, editor canvas correctly present/no-throw after restore) and an aspect-differentiation suite (a synthetic World with Landscape/Portrait/Quote Layouts produces three canvases at their own genuinely correct 1350├Ś1080/1080├Ś1350/1080├Ś1350 sizes ŌĆö the exact bug reproduction that caught the `buildPayload` issue, failing before the fix and passing after) plus a visual screenshot confirming a real Frame Variation's mat/border colour and the genuine "Add artwork" placeholder now render in the carousel. Full regression across the entire existing 33-script Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; `_repCard`/`_renderChangeRepresentationScreen` (the Context Panel's own "Change Representation" shortcut) are deliberately untouched, exactly as Sprint 11.1 originally scoped them ŌĆö this feature is confined to Screen 2's own carousel builder in `js/creationFlow.js`, plus one small CSS addition.)

- Screen 2 Carousel ŌĆö Story-Type Worlds' Own Layout/Layer-Pack Content Now Resolves Too (a direct, same-day follow-up: right after the live-render carousel shipped, the user tested it against their own real "My shapes" World ŌĆö a story-type theme with a real Scene-converged Layout and Layer Pack ŌĆö and reported "i dont think this was supposed to look like this," seeing a plain navy square with a blank white square inside where a genuine background fill + decoration shape should have shown. **Root cause, confirmed by direct code reading**: `_layoutTheme(s)` ŌĆö a SEPARATE resolution chain from `_theme(s)`/`_artworkTheme(s)`, used by `_resolveLayout`/`_activeLayoutHolders`/`_activeLayoutPlaces`/`_activeLayerPack` for all Layout/Holder/Place/Layer-Pack resolution ŌĆö only ever checked `s.artworkTheme` or the GLOBAL active theme, never `s.theme`. The carousel's synthetic preview slide sets `slide.artworkTheme=null` for a story-type World (correctly, since Screen 2's own `payload.theme`/`.artworkTheme` overrides from the just-shipped feature already handle the story/artwork split for `_theme`/`_artworkTheme`) ŌĆö so `_layoutTheme` fell straight through to the global fallback, completely bypassing the World's own `layouts`/`layerPack`/`frameVariations`, and the page rendered the plain default panel instead. Two unsafe fixes were considered and rejected: mutating global `ThemeEngine` state to preview a theme (rejected ŌĆö `applyTheme`/`applyArtworkTheme` unconditionally call `_invalidateThumbnails()`/`_refreshUI()` regardless of `opts.silent`, a real side effect on any background-open project); reusing `payload.theme` as a `_layoutTheme` fallback source (rejected ŌĆö `ThemeEngine.resolveTheme()` always returns a stripped object missing `.layouts`/`.layerPack`/`.frameVariations` entirely, and is always truthy, which would silently break Layout resolution for every real page in the app). **Fix**: `_layoutTheme(s)` (`renderer/slideRenderer.js`) now checks a new `s.layoutTheme` field first ŌĆö a distinct field from `s.theme`/`s.artworkTheme` (which `_theme`/`_artworkTheme` already interpret for other purposes and can't safely be reused for this), set only by `_renderCarouselCanvas` (`js/creationFlow.js`) via `payload.layoutTheme=theme` (the raw, un-stripped theme object) right alongside the existing `payload.theme`/`.artworkTheme` overrides. Real slides never set this field, so the fix is a no-op everywhere else in the app ŌĆö confirmed via a `git stash` A/B test reproducing the exact bug (wrong portrait-default canvas size, wrong background colour, blank white decoration area) before the fix and the correct landscape aspect + converged background fill + decoration shape colour after it. Verified via a new Playwright reproduction (`carousel_story_theme_layout_test.js`, scratch-only) using a synthetic story-type theme shaped exactly like a real World Builder v2 Scene-converged package (`supportedCreationTypes:['story']`, a landscape-aspect Layout, a `'slide'`-scoped colour-fill Layer Pack entry, an `'overlay'`-scoped decoration shape) ŌĆö pixel-sampled to confirm both the correct canvas aspect and the correct fill/shape colours render. Full regression across the entire existing 28-script Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; the fix is confined to one function each in `renderer/slideRenderer.js` and `js/creationFlow.js`.)

- Screen 2 Carousel ŌĆö Each Scene's Visible Box Now Matches Its Own Real Orientation ("its better but not fixed. the orientation for each scene is different in builder. but in creator they all are showing up as landscape" ŌĆö a direct, same-day follow-up to the `_layoutTheme` fix above. **Confirmed the internal canvas pixel buffer was already correct** ŌĆö `canvas.width`/`canvas.height` genuinely resolved a different, correct size per Representation (1080├Ś1350 for Portrait, 1350├Ś1080 for Landscape) ŌĆö but the VISIBLE box every carousel slide sits in, `.creation-flow-carousel-art`, was a fixed-shape container (`width:100%; max-width:250px; height:clamp(...)`, originally built for a cropped static `<img>` thumbnail with `object-fit:cover`) that never adapted to a Representation's own real orientation, so every Scene's correctly-sized canvas got squeezed/padded into the SAME landscape-ish box regardless ŌĆö exactly "they all show up as landscape." **A second, compounding bug found in the same trace**: `_renderCarouselCanvas`'s own `canvas.style.aspectRatio` was being computed from `SlideRenderer.getCanvasSize(slide)` ŌĆö the bare synthetic slide object ŌĆö but the `layoutTheme` override the previous fix introduced is only ever set on `payload` (built via `buildPayload(slide,...)` then overridden), never on `slide` itself; so even that inert inline style was resolving to the wrong value for every story-type Representation. **Fix**: `getCanvasSize()` is now called with `payload` (which correctly carries `.layoutTheme`); `_renderCarouselCanvas` returns the resolved `{w,h}` size instead of a bare boolean, and `_carouselSlide` (`js/creationFlow.js`) now sets `.creation-flow-carousel-art`'s own `style.aspectRatio` from that size ŌĆö the actual container that controls the visible shape, not the inert canvas-level style. `css/style.css`'s `.creation-flow-carousel-art` changed from a fixed `width:100%` to `width:auto` + a CSS `aspect-ratio:4/5` fallback (matching the editor's own default page shape before any live render has painted), so its width now genuinely derives from its height and whichever real aspect ratio is set ŌĆö letting each Representation's box take on its own real shape instead of sharing one fixed frame. Verified via a `git stash` A/B test with three Representations (Portrait/Landscape/Quote): before the fix, every visible box measured identically wide-shaped (ratio Ōēł1.55, matching the exact reported symptom) despite the internal canvas already being correctly sized per Representation; after the fix, Portrait/Quote boxes measure genuinely narrower-than-tall (ratio Ōēł0.80) and the Landscape box measures genuinely wider-than-tall (ratio Ōēł1.25) ŌĆö a real, visible difference, not just a backing-store number. Full regression across the entire existing 32-script Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; confined to `js/creationFlow.js` and one CSS rule.)

- Bigger Slide Previews ŌĆö Screen 2's Own Carousel and the "Change Look" Quick-Switch Both Grown, the Latter Now Live-Rendered Too ("can we increase the size of slide in right panel?" ŌĆö the Selected World Preview carousel's own visible box (`.creation-flow-carousel-art`) was capped at `max-width:250px`, noticeably smaller than the panel it sits in actually had room for. Widened its clamp() bounds (height `clamp(110px,17vh,200px)`ŌåÆ`clamp(110px,19vh,260px)`, max-width `250px`ŌåÆ`300px`, the carousel-slide wrapper's own min-height similarly), trimming the overlay's own top/bottom padding slightly (`clamp(14px,3vh,48px)`ŌåÆ`clamp(10px,2.4vh,48px)`) to free just enough headroom to grow without reintroducing the scroll the earlier "No-Scroll Screens" fix eliminated ŌĆö verified at every height that fix originally targeted (640/700/720/800/900px), all still zero-scroll. **A second, separate request landed in the same conversation**: a follow-up screenshot showed a DIFFERENT screen ŌĆö the Context Panel's "Change Look" quick-switch ("Choose a Page Style," `_renderChangeRepresentationScreen`/`_repCard` in `js/creationFlow.js`) ŌĆö with its own small, cropped, scrollbar-forcing thumbnails; the user then clarified the ask further: "not just the size change but other change also where we plugged the center pane in screen 2 - preview," i.e. apply Screen 2's OWN live-SlideRenderer-render treatment here too, not merely make the old static thumbnails bigger. **Size**: `.creation-flow-card-icon-image`'s fixed height went `110px`ŌåÆ`190px` and the modal itself (`.creation-flow-overlay.mode-change-look .creation-flow-panel`) widened `560px`ŌåÆ`680px` ŌĆö this modal already scrolls its own panel (`overflow-y:auto`) when content overflows, so none of the Screen-2-style no-scroll care was needed here. **Live render**: `_repCard` now resolves the full theme object (`ThemeRegistry.get(themeId)`, the same lookup `_applyRepresentationToCurrentSlide` already made) and, when it resolves, paints a real `<canvas>` via the exact same `_renderCarouselCanvas` helper Screen 2's carousel uses ŌĆö reusing `.creation-flow-card-icon-image`'s own fixed width/height CSS (so `_renderCarouselCanvas`'s inline `aspect-ratio` style, needed for Screen 2's free-floating box, has no effect here ŌĆö the live render simply crops to fill the card exactly like the old static image did, via `object-fit:cover`) ŌĆö falling back to the pre-existing static thumbnail/glyph path only when the theme can't be resolved at all, matching `_carouselSlide`'s own established fallback discipline. Verified via a new Playwright test (`change_look_live_render_test.js`, scratch-only) with a synthetic two-Representation story-type theme (distinct, properly-`scope`-tagged 'slide'-scoped background fills per Layout, mirroring the Builder Convergence Sprint's own scoping rule) confirming both Page Style cards now render real, genuinely-distinct `<canvas>` content (not `<img>`) with zero panel overflow ŌĆö a first draft of this test's fixture omitted the `scope` field on each layer entry, which reproduced a real-looking "both cards show the same colour" symptom that turned out to be the TEST fixture's own bug (an unscoped layer applies globally by design, per the Builder Convergence Sprint, so the later one simply paints over the earlier ŌĆö not a product defect), caught and corrected before relying on the test. Full regression across the entire existing 34-script Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (including the updated `change_look_image_overflow.js`, whose own size/width assertions were intentionally loosened to match the deliberately bigger dimensions, not a regression) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; confined to `css/style.css` and `js/creationFlow.js`.)

- "Choose a Page Style" ŌĆö Each Card Now Shows Its Own Real Orientation Instead of One Shared Fixed Shape ("all good but can we fix the orientation. each slide orientation as per the builder authored" ŌĆö a direct follow-up to the previous entry's live-render upgrade for the Context Panel's "Change Look" quick-switch. A screenshot showed every Page Style card sharing one identical box shape regardless of its own real Layout ŌĆö exactly the same class of bug already fixed for Screen 2's own carousel (see "Screen 2 Carousel ŌĆö Each Scene's Visible Box Now Matches Its Own Real Orientation" above), just not yet applied here: `.creation-flow-card-icon-image`'s CSS was still a fixed `height:190px` + `object-fit:cover`, so a genuinely portrait or landscape live render got cropped to fill the same shared shape every card used, hiding its real orientation. **Fix**: `.creation-flow-card-icon-image` changed from `height:190px` to `height:auto` + a default `aspect-ratio:4/5` fallback (the modal's own before-JS-paint shape, matching the editor's default page convention) ŌĆö `_repCard` (`js/creationFlow.js`) already relied on `_renderCarouselCanvas`'s existing inline `canvas.style.aspectRatio` (set from the live render's own resolved size, the exact mechanism Screen 2's carousel already established), so once the CSS stopped pinning a fixed height, that inline style could finally take over and each card's box genuinely reflects its own real orientation ŌĆö no JS change beyond an updated code comment. The static-thumbnail fallback path (used only when a theme can't be resolved at all) simply keeps the same default 4:5 shape it already had. Verified via a `git stash` A/B test with a real landscape + portrait Representation pair: before the fix, both cards measured an identical fixed ratio (1.35, one shared shape) regardless of their own Layout; after, the landscape card measures genuinely wider-than-tall (ratio 1.25) and the portrait card genuinely taller-than-wide (ratio 0.8) ŌĆö a real, visible difference matching each Scene's own authored shape. Full regression across the entire existing 35-script Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (one existing test's own height-cap assertion was intentionally loosened to allow the now-correct taller portrait box ŌĆö not a regression, the direct intended consequence of this fix) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; confined to one CSS rule in `css/style.css` plus a comment update in `js/creationFlow.js`.)

- Page Background Colour ŌĆö a Real Per-Page Override, Finally Winning Over the World's Own Wall Tone ("the creator background color. its available in right panel but changing it has not effect on the center pane slide" ŌĆö a real, confirmed bug, not a misunderstanding. **Root cause, traced not guessed**: Context Panel's "Page Background ŌåÆ Background Colour" swatch (`js/contextPanel.js`'s `_appendBackground`) wrote to the STORY Theme's global `colours.frame` sub-option via `ThemeEngine.setSubOption` ŌĆö but `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s background-fill line has always been `x.fillStyle=_wallTone||_frameColor(t,opts)`, unconditionally preferring the active World's own resolved wall tone (`_resolveWallTone(s)`, Sprint 9.7) over the Story Theme's frame colour whenever ANY World/Artwork Theme with a Frame Variation is active ŌĆö which is the common case for a real project today. The swatch's write was reaching a real, correctly-wired code path; it simply never had priority to paint anything, so it read as "changing it has no effect." A second, compounding issue: even where it *would* have won (no World active at all), the write was **global** (every page at once), not scoped to "the center pane slide" the control's own heading ("PAGE BACKGROUND") and the user's own wording both name. **Fix**: a genuine per-page override, `slide.metadata.cardOverrides.background` ŌĆö the same per-card override bag pattern every other Story-Author control in this codebase already uses (Frame Variation, Presentation, image view, etc.) ŌĆö now resolves FIRST in the background-fill line, ahead of both wall tone and the Story Theme default (`renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s new `_slideBackgroundOverride(s)`, plus a matching fix so Handle/Page-Number chrome-text legibility considers the override too, not just wall tone). `_appendBackground` now reads `_currentSlide()` (mirroring `_appendMetadataField`'s own convention) instead of the global Theme, writes to the per-slide bag, and calls `host.redraw()`/`host.markDirty()` ŌĆö the same dispatch every other live-editing control in this file already uses; `ThemeEngine.setSubOption` is no longer called by this control at all. No reset control was added (a disclosed, minor gap ŌĆö a Story Author who picks a colour has no one-click way back to the World default through this control alone, matching the scope of "fix the reported bug," not a broader redesign). Verified via a `git stash` A/B test against a real Frame-Variation-driven wall tone: before the fix, picking a new colour left the canvas pixel completely unchanged (the exact reported symptom); after, the canvas repaints to the picked colour immediately, and the value is confirmed stored per-slide (a second page does not inherit it). Full regression across the entire existing 36-script Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; confined to `js/contextPanel.js` and `renderer/slideRenderer.js`.)

## Locked Product Decisions

### 1. Workspace Simplification

- Hide Project Title, Author and editable Book Name from the editor.
- Preserve metadata in the project model.

### 2. Asset Pack System

- Decorations use installable packs.
- Local import first.
- Cloud repository later.
- Design for reusable pack architecture.

### 3. Card Designer

Reusable component supporting:

- Image scale
- Image position
- Fit modes
- Typography
- Card styling
- Theme defaults with per-card overrides

### 4. Audio Studio

- Per-card narration
- Record/import audio
- Audio linked to cards
- Foundation for narrated exports

### 5. Social-First Export

Priority:

1. Instagram Carousel
2. Instagram Reel

## Roadmap

1. Theme Designer Polish
2. Card Designer

4. Cover Designer
5. CTA Designer

9. VihuPipe

## Development Rules

- Keep prompts minimal.
- Never refactor architecture without approval.
- Prefer extending reusable components.
- Preserve backward compatibility.
- Keep commits focused and atomic.
- Update CLAUDE.md whenever a major architectural or product decision is approved.
